'To express the quadratic \\(4x^2 + 2x - 1\\) in the form \\(a(x+b)^2 + c\\), we need to complete the square.\n\nStart with the quadratic:\n\\[ 4x^2 + 2x - 1. \\]\n\nFactor out the coefficient of \\(x^2\\) from the first two terms:\n\\[ 4(x^2 + \\frac{1}{2}x) - 1. \\]\n\nNext, complete the square inside the parentheses. Take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), square it, and add and subtract it inside the parentheses:\n\\[ x^2 + \\frac{1}{2}x = \\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2. \\]\n\nSubstitute back into the expression:\n\\[ 4\\left(\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{1}{16}\\right) - 1. \\]\n\nDistribute the 4:\n\\[ 4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{4}{16} - 1. \\]\n\nSimplify:\n\\[ 4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{1}{4} - 1. \\]\n\nCombine the constants:\n\\[ 4\\left(x + \\frac{1}{4}\\right)^2 - \\frac{5}{4}. \\]\n\nNow, the quadratic is in the form \\(a(x+b)^2 + c\\) where:\n- \\(a = 4\\),\n- \\(b = \\frac{1}{4}\\),\n- \\(c = -\\frac{5}{4}\\).\n\nCalculate \\(a + b + c\\):\n\\[ a + b + c = 4 + \\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{5}{4}. \\]\n\nCombine the terms:\n\\[ 4 + \\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{5}{4} = 4 - 1 = 3. \\]\n\nThus, \\(a + b + c = \\boxed{3}\\).'
'Let the two numbers be \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), where \\( x > y \\). According to the problem, we have the following system of equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx - y = 11\n\\]\n\nTo find the values of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), we can add the two equations together:\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 25 + 11\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2x = 36\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 18\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\( x = 18 \\), we can substitute this value back into the first equation to find \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n18 + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 25 - 18\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 7\n\\]\n\nThus, the smaller of the two numbers is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
'To rewrite the quadratic \\(x^2 + bx + 1\\) in the form \\((x + m)^2 - 63\\), we need to complete the square.\n\nStarting with the quadratic:\n\\[ x^2 + bx + 1 \\]\n\nTo complete the square, we take the coefficient of \\(x\\), which is \\(b\\), divide it by 2, and square it:\n\\[ \\left(\\frac{b}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{b^2}{4} \\]\n\nAdd and subtract this square inside the expression:\n\\[ x^2 + bx + 1 = \\left(x^2 + bx + \\frac{b^2}{4}\\right) - \\frac{b^2}{4} + 1 \\]\n\nThe expression inside the parentheses is a perfect square:\n\\[ \\left(x + \\frac{b}{2}\\right)^2 - \\frac{b^2}{4} + 1 \\]\n\nWe want this to equal \\((x + m)^2 - 63\\). Therefore, we set:\n\\[ -\\frac{b^2}{4} + 1 = -63 \\]\n\nSolving for \\(b\\):\n\\[ -\\frac{b^2}{4} + 1 = -63 \\]\n\\[ -\\frac{b^2}{4} = -64 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{b^2}{4} = 64 \\]\n\\[ b^2 = 256 \\]\n\\[ b = \\sqrt{256} \\]\n\\[ b = 16 \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(b\\) is \\(\\boxed{16}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we use Vieta's formulas, which relate the coefficients of a polynomial to sums and products of its roots. For the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + ax + b = 0\\), Vieta's formulas tell us:\n\n1. The sum of the roots \\(a + b\\) is equal to \\(-a\\).\n2. The product of the roots \\(ab\\) is equal to \\(b\\).\n\nFrom the first equation, we have:\n\\[ a + b = -a \\]\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[ 2a + b = 0 \\]\nor\n\\[ b = -2a \\]\n\nFrom the second equation, we have:\n\\[ ab = b \\]\nSince \\(b \\neq 0\\) (as given in the problem), we can divide both sides by \\(b\\) to get:\n\\[ a = 1 \\]\n\nSubstituting \\(a = 1\\) into the equation \\(b = -2a\\), we find:\n\\[ b = -2(1) = -2 \\]\n\nThus, the pair \\((a, b)\\) is \\((1, -2)\\)."
'To find the y-intercept of the polynomial \\( Q(x) = P(x)^2 \\), we need to evaluate \\( Q(x) \\) at \\( x = 0 \\).\n\nFirst, evaluate \\( P(x) \\) at \\( x = 0 \\):\n\\[\nP(0) = 4(0)^3 - 2(0)^2 + 7(0) - 1 = -1\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute this into \\( Q(x) \\):\n\\[\nQ(x) = P(x)^2 \\implies Q(0) = P(0)^2 = (-1)^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the y-intercept of \\( Q(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'Let the length of the plot be \\( l \\) feet. Then the width of the plot is \\( l + 5 \\) feet. The area of the rectangle is given by:\n\n\\[\nl \\times (l + 5) \\geq 500\n\\]\n\nExpanding the expression, we have:\n\n\\[\nl^2 + 5l \\geq 500\n\\]\n\nTo find the minimum value of \\( l \\) that satisfies this inequality, we solve the equation:\n\n\\[\nl^2 + 5l - 500 = 0\n\\]\n\nUsing the quadratic formula \\( l = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 5 \\), and \\( c = -500 \\), we find:\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{5^2 - 4 \\times 1 \\times (-500)}}{2 \\times 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 + 2000}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{2025}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{-5 \\pm 45}{2}\n\\]\n\nThe two solutions are:\n\n\\[\nl = \\frac{40}{2} = 20 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad l = \\frac{-50}{2} = -25\n\\]\n\nSince a negative length does not make sense, we take \\( l = 20 \\).\n\nThus, the width of the plot is:\n\n\\[\nl + 5 = 20 + 5 = 25\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the width of the plot is \\(\\boxed{25}\\) feet.'
'To solve this problem, we need to understand the behavior of the quadratic inequality \\(x^2 + bx + c > 0\\). The inequality is satisfied for \\(x \\in (-\\infty, -2) \\cup (3, \\infty)\\), which means the quadratic expression is positive outside the interval \\([-2, 3]\\) and non-positive within the interval \\([-2, 3]\\).\n\nThis implies that the roots of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + bx + c = 0\\) are \\(x = -2\\) and \\(x = 3\\). Therefore, the quadratic can be factored as:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + bx + c = (x + 2)(x - 3)\n\\]\n\nExpanding this product, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + bx + c = x^2 - 3x + 2x - 6 = x^2 - x - 6\n\\]\n\nBy comparing coefficients, we find:\n\n- \\(b = -1\\)\n- \\(c = -6\\)\n\nThus, the value of \\(b + c\\) is:\n\n\\[\nb + c = -1 + (-6) = -7\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(b + c\\) is \\(\\boxed{-7}\\).'
'To find the coordinates \\((x, y)\\), we use the formula for the midpoint of a line segment. The midpoint \\((M_x, M_y)\\) of a line segment between two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nM_x = \\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\quad M_y = \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2}\n\\]\n\nGiven that the midpoint is \\((3, -5)\\) and one endpoint is \\((-9, 1)\\), we can set up the following equations:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x + (-9)}{2} = 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{y + 1}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nNow, solve each equation for \\(x\\) and \\(y\\).\n\n1. Solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x - 9}{2} = 3\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\nx - 9 = 6\n\\]\n\nAdd 9 to both sides:\n\n\\[\nx = 15\n\\]\n\n2. Solve for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{y + 1}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 2:\n\n\\[\ny + 1 = -10\n\\]\n\nSubtract 1 from both sides:\n\n\\[\ny = -11\n\\]\n\nThus, the coordinates \\((x, y)\\) are \\((15, -11)\\).'
'To calculate \\(42^2\\), Emily uses the identity for the square of a binomial:\n\n\\[\n42^2 = (40 + 2)^2 = 40^2 + 2 \\times 40 \\times 2 + 2^2 = 40^2 + 160 + 4 = 40^2 + 164\n\\]\n\nSimilarly, to calculate \\(38^2\\), we use the identity:\n\n\\[\n38^2 = (40 - 2)^2 = 40^2 - 2 \\times 40 \\times 2 + 2^2 = 40^2 - 160 + 4 = 40^2 - 156\n\\]\n\nThus, Emily subtracts \\(156\\) from \\(40^2\\) to calculate \\(38^2\\). Therefore, the number she subtracts is \\(\\boxed{156}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the equations of lines \\(a\\) and \\(b\\).\n\n1. **Find the slope of line \\(c\\):**\n\n   The equation of line \\(c\\) is \\(y = -2x + 3\\). The slope of line \\(c\\) is \\(-2\\).\n\n2. **Find the slope of line \\(b):**\n\n   Since line \\(b\\) is perpendicular to line \\(c\\), the slope of line \\(b\\) is the negative reciprocal of the slope of line \\(c\\). Therefore, the slope of line \\(b\\) is \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\).\n\n3. **Find the equation of line \\(b\\):**\n\n   Line \\(b\\) goes through the point \\((3, 1)\\) and has a slope of \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\). Using the point-slope form of a line, \\(y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)\\), we have:\n\n   \\[\n   y - 1 = \\frac{1}{2}(x - 3)\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying, we get:\n\n   \\[\n   y - 1 = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{3}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   y = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{3}{2} + 1\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   y = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{1}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   So, the equation of line \\(b\\) is \\(y = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{1}{2}\\).\n\n4. **Find the slope of line \\(a\\):**\n\n   Line \\(a\\) is parallel to line \\(b\\), so it has the same slope as line \\(b\\), which is \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\).\n\n5. **Find the equation of line \\(a\\):**\n\n   Line \\(a\\) goes through the point \\((1, 2)\\) and has a slope of \\(\\frac{1}{2}\\). Using the point-slope form, we have:\n\n   \\[\n   y - 2 = \\frac{1}{2}(x - 1)\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying, we get:\n\n   \\[\n   y - 2 = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{1}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   y = \\frac{1}{2}x - \\frac{1}{2} + 2\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   y = \\frac{1}{2}x + \\frac{3}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   So, the equation of line \\(a\\) is \\(y = \\frac{1}{2}x + \\frac{3}{2}\\).\n\n6. **Find the y-intercept of line \\(a\\):**\n\n   The y-intercept of line \\(a\\) is the constant term in its equation, which is \\(\\frac{3}{2}\\).\n\nTherefore, the y-intercept of line \\(a\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{3}{2}}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\frac{1}{x} + \\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{1}{z}\\) for \\(y\\), we start by substituting the given values \\(x = 25\\) and \\(z = 24\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{25} + \\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{1}{24}\n\\]\n\nNext, we isolate \\(\\frac{1}{y}\\) by subtracting \\(\\frac{1}{25}\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{1}{24} - \\frac{1}{25}\n\\]\n\nTo subtract these fractions, we need a common denominator. The least common multiple of 24 and 25 is 600. We rewrite each fraction with this common denominator:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{24} = \\frac{25}{600}, \\quad \\frac{1}{25} = \\frac{24}{600}\n\\]\n\nNow, perform the subtraction:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{y} = \\frac{25}{600} - \\frac{24}{600} = \\frac{1}{600}\n\\]\n\nTaking the reciprocal of both sides gives:\n\n\\[\ny = 600\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(y\\) is \\(\\boxed{600}\\).'
'To solve the quadratic equation \\(0 = -9x^2 - 3x + 2\\), we can use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = -9\\), \\(b = -3\\), and \\(c = 2\\).\n\nFirst, calculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = (-3)^2 - 4(-9)(2) = 9 + 72 = 81\n\\]\n\nSince the discriminant is positive, there are two real solutions. Now, apply the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-(-3) \\pm \\sqrt{81}}{2(-9)} = \\frac{3 \\pm 9}{-18}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two potential solutions:\n\n1. \\(x = \\frac{3 + 9}{-18} = \\frac{12}{-18} = -\\frac{2}{3}\\)\n2. \\(x = \\frac{3 - 9}{-18} = \\frac{-6}{-18} = \\frac{1}{3}\\)\n\nSince we are looking for the solution where \\(x > 0\\), the valid solution is:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{1}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{3}}\\).'
"According to Ohm's law, \\( V = IR \\). We are given that when \\( I = 40 \\) amperes and \\( R = 3 \\) ohms, the voltage \\( V \\) is:\n\n\\[ V = 40 \\times 3 = 120 \\text{ volts} \\]\n\nWe need to find the current \\( I \\) when the resistance \\( R \\) is 20 ohms, with the voltage remaining constant at 120 volts. Using Ohm's law again:\n\n\\[ V = IR \\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[ 120 = I \\times 20 \\]\n\nSolving for \\( I \\):\n\n\\[ I = \\frac{120}{20} = 6 \\text{ amperes} \\]\n\nTherefore, the amount of current when the resistor has a resistance of 20 ohms is \\( \\boxed{6} \\) amperes."
"To solve the inequality \\(\\frac{1}{5}|9+2a|<1\\), we first eliminate the fraction by multiplying both sides by 5:\n\n\\[\n|9+2a| < 5\n\\]\n\nThis absolute value inequality can be split into two separate inequalities:\n\n1. \\(9 + 2a < 5\\)\n2. \\(9 + 2a > -5\\)\n\nLet's solve each inequality separately.\n\n**For the first inequality:**\n\n\\[\n9 + 2a < 5\n\\]\n\nSubtract 9 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2a < 5 - 9\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2a < -4\n\\]\n\nDivide by 2:\n\n\\[\na < -2\n\\]\n\n**For the second inequality:**\n\n\\[\n9 + 2a > -5\n\\]\n\nSubtract 9 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2a > -5 - 9\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2a > -14\n\\]\n\nDivide by 2:\n\n\\[\na > -7\n\\]\n\nCombining both inequalities, we have:\n\n\\[\n-7 < a < -2\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution in interval notation is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{(-7, -2)}\n\\]"

Let the roots be \\(p\\) and \\(q\\), both positive integers. By Vieta's formulas, we have:\n\n1. \\(p + q = -m\\)\n2. \\(pq = n = 28\\)\n\nWe need to find pairs \\((p, q)\\) such that \\(pq = 28\\). The positive integer factor pairs of 28 are:\n\n- \\( (1, 28) \\)\n- \\( (2, 14) \\)\n- \\( (4, 7) \\)\n- \\( (7, 4) \\)\n- \\( (14, 2) \\)\n- \\( (28, 1) \\)\n\nEach pair \\((p, q)\\) corresponds to a polynomial \\(x^2 - (p+q)x + 28\\). We need to ensure that both roots are positive integers, which they are by construction.\n\nThus, there are 6 such pairs, and therefore, there are 6 polynomials of the form \\(x^2 + mx + 28\\) with positive integer roots. 'To find the point on the line \\(5x - 9y = 42\\) where the \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) coordinates are additive inverses of each other, we set \\(y = -x\\).\n\nSubstitute \\(y = -x\\) into the equation of the line:\n\n\\[\n5x - 9(-x) = 42\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[\n5x + 9x = 42\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n14x = 42\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{42}{14} = 3\n\\]\n\nSince \\(y = -x\\), we have:\n\n\\[\ny = -3\n\\]\n\nThus, the coordinates of the point are \\((3, -3)\\).\n\nThe answer is \\((3, -3)\\).'
'To solve the equation \\((17^6 - 17^5) \\div 16 = 17^x\\), we start by simplifying the expression on the left side.\n\nFirst, factor out \\(17^5\\) from the terms inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\n17^6 - 17^5 = 17^5(17 - 1) = 17^5 \\cdot 16\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute this back into the original equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{17^5 \\cdot 16}{16} = 17^x\n\\]\n\nThe \\(16\\) in the numerator and denominator cancel each other out:\n\n\\[\n17^5 = 17^x\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we equate the exponents:\n\n\\[\nx = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
"To find the smallest distance between the origin and a point on the parabola \\( y = x^2 - 5 \\), we need to minimize the distance function from the origin to a point \\((x, y)\\) on the parabola. The distance \\( D \\) from the origin \\((0, 0)\\) to a point \\((x, y)\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^2 + y^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( y = x^2 - 5 \\) into the distance formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^2 + (x^2 - 5)^2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression inside the square root:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^2 + (x^2 - 5)^2} = \\sqrt{x^2 + (x^4 - 10x^2 + 25)}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{x^4 - 9x^2 + 25}\n\\]\n\nTo minimize \\( D \\), we minimize the expression under the square root:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = x^4 - 9x^2 + 25\n\\]\n\nTo find the critical points, we take the derivative of \\( f(x) \\) and set it to zero:\n\n\\[\nf'(x) = 4x^3 - 18x\n\\]\n\nSetting \\( f'(x) = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\n4x^3 - 18x = 0\n\\]\n\nFactoring out \\( 2x \\):\n\n\\[\n2x(2x^2 - 9) = 0\n\\]\n\nThis gives us:\n\n\\[\nx = 0 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad 2x^2 - 9 = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving \\( 2x^2 - 9 = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\n2x^2 = 9 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x^2 = \\frac{9}{2} \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = \\pm \\frac{3}{\\sqrt{2}} = \\pm \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\n\\]\n\nWe have three critical points: \\( x = 0 \\), \\( x = \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\), and \\( x = -\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\).\n\nEvaluate \\( f(x) \\) at these points:\n\n1. \\( x = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\nf(0) = 0^4 - 9 \\cdot 0^2 + 25 = 25\n\\]\n\n2. \\( x = \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\):\n\n\\[\nf\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right) = \\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^4 - 9\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^2 + 25\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{18}{4} = \\frac{9}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right)^4 = \\left(\\frac{9}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{81}{4}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf\\left(\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2}\\right) = \\frac{81}{4} - 9 \\cdot \\frac{9}{2} + 25 = \\frac{81}{4} - \\frac{81}{2} + 25\n\\]\n\nConvert to a common denominator:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{81}{4} - \\frac{162}{4} + \\frac{100}{4} = \\frac{19}{4}\n\\]\n\n3. \\( x = -\\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\) yields the same result as \\( x = \\frac{3\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\) due to symmetry.\n\nThe minimum value of \\( f(x) \\) is \\(\\frac{19}{4}\\), so the minimum distance \\( D \\) is:\n\n\\[\nD = \\sqrt{\\frac{19}{4}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{19}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( a = 19 \\) and \\( b = 2 \\), so \\( a + b = 19 + 2 = \\boxed{21} \\)."
'To solve the equation \\( x\\sqrt{x} - 5x - 9\\sqrt{x} = 35 \\), we start by making a substitution to simplify the expression. Let \\( y = \\sqrt{x} \\). Then \\( x = y^2 \\), and the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\ny^2 \\cdot y - 5y^2 - 9y = 35\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\ny^3 - 5y^2 - 9y = 35\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\ny^3 - 5y^2 - 9y - 35 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe need to find integer solutions for \\( y \\). We can test small integer values for \\( y \\):\n\n- For \\( y = 1 \\):\n  \\[\n  1^3 - 5 \\cdot 1^2 - 9 \\cdot 1 - 35 = 1 - 5 - 9 - 35 = -48 \\neq 0\n  \\]\n\n- For \\( y = 2 \\):\n  \\[\n  2^3 - 5 \\cdot 2^2 - 9 \\cdot 2 - 35 = 8 - 20 - 18 - 35 = -65 \\neq 0\n  \\]\n\n- For \\( y = 3 \\):\n  \\[\n  3^3 - 5 \\cdot 3^2 - 9 \\cdot 3 - 35 = 27 - 45 - 27 - 35 = -80 \\neq 0\n  \\]\n\n- For \\( y = 4 \\):\n  \\[\n  4^3 - 5 \\cdot 4^2 - 9 \\cdot 4 - 35 = 64 - 80 - 36 - 35 = -87 \\neq 0\n  \\]\n\n- For \\( y = 5 \\):\n  \\[\n  5^3 - 5 \\cdot 5^2 - 9 \\cdot 5 - 35 = 125 - 125 - 45 - 35 = -80 \\neq 0\n  \\]\n\n- For \\( y = 7 \\):\n  \\[\n  7^3 - 5 \\cdot 7^2 - 9 \\cdot 7 - 35 = 343 - 245 - 63 - 35 = 0\n  \\]\n\nThus, \\( y = 7 \\) is a solution. Since \\( y = \\sqrt{x} \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{x} = 7 \\implies x = 7^2 = 49\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the integer \\( x \\) that satisfies the equation is \\(\\boxed{49}\\).'
'To find \\( x^2y \\), we start with the given equations:\n\n1. \\( x^2 + y = 4 \\)\n2. \\( x^4 + y^2 = 10 \\)\n\nFrom equation (1), we can express \\( y \\) in terms of \\( x^2 \\):\n\n\\[ y = 4 - x^2 \\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( y \\) into equation (2):\n\n\\[ x^4 + (4 - x^2)^2 = 10 \\]\n\nExpand the square:\n\n\\[ x^4 + (16 - 8x^2 + x^4) = 10 \\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[ 2x^4 - 8x^2 + 16 = 10 \\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[ 2x^4 - 8x^2 + 6 = 0 \\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 2:\n\n\\[ x^4 - 4x^2 + 3 = 0 \\]\n\nLet \\( z = x^2 \\). Then the equation becomes:\n\n\\[ z^2 - 4z + 3 = 0 \\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in \\( z \\). Solve for \\( z \\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[ z = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -4 \\), and \\( c = 3 \\):\n\n\\[ z = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{(-4)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 3}}{2 \\cdot 1} \\]\n\\[ z = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 - 12}}{2} \\]\n\\[ z = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{4}}{2} \\]\n\\[ z = \\frac{4 \\pm 2}{2} \\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions for \\( z \\):\n\n\\[ z = \\frac{6}{2} = 3 \\]\n\\[ z = \\frac{2}{2} = 1 \\]\n\nRecall that \\( z = x^2 \\), so:\n\n1. If \\( x^2 = 3 \\), then from \\( y = 4 - x^2 \\), we have \\( y = 4 - 3 = 1 \\).\n2. If \\( x^2 = 1 \\), then from \\( y = 4 - x^2 \\), we have \\( y = 4 - 1 = 3 \\).\n\nNow, calculate \\( x^2y \\) for each case:\n\n- If \\( x^2 = 3 \\) and \\( y = 1 \\), then \\( x^2y = 3 \\times 1 = 3 \\).\n- If \\( x^2 = 1 \\) and \\( y = 3 \\), then \\( x^2y = 1 \\times 3 = 3 \\).\n\nIn both cases, \\( x^2y = 3 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^2y \\) is \\(\\boxed{3}\\).'
'To expand the product \\((x+1)^2 \\cdot x\\), we first expand \\((x+1)^2\\) and then multiply the result by \\(x\\).\n\nFirst, expand \\((x+1)^2\\):\n\\[\n(x+1)^2 = (x+1)(x+1) = x^2 + 2x + 1\n\\]\n\nNow, multiply the expanded form by \\(x\\):\n\\[\n(x^2 + 2x + 1) \\cdot x = x^2 \\cdot x + 2x \\cdot x + 1 \\cdot x\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\\[\nx^2 \\cdot x = x^3\n\\]\n\\[\n2x \\cdot x = 2x^2\n\\]\n\\[\n1 \\cdot x = x\n\\]\n\nCombine all the terms:\n\\[\nx^3 + 2x^2 + x\n\\]\n\nThus, the expanded form of \\((x+1)^2 \\cdot x\\) is \\(\\boxed{x^3 + 2x^2 + x}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to understand the relationship between the two arithmetic sequences.\n\nLet's denote the first sequence as \\( a_n \\) and the second sequence as \\( b_n \\).\n\nFor the first sequence:\n- The first term \\( a_1 = 0 \\).\n\nFor the second sequence:\n- The first term is \\( b_1 \\).\n- The common difference is \\( d_b \\).\n\nThe terms of the second sequence are:\n- \\( b_1 \\)\n- \\( b_2 = b_1 + d_b \\)\n- \\( b_3 = b_1 + 2d_b \\)\n- \\( b_4 = b_1 + 3d_b \\)\n- \\( b_5 = b_1 + 4d_b = 3 \\) (given)\n\nFor the first sequence:\n- The second term \\( a_2 = a_1 + b_1 = 0 + b_1 = b_1 \\).\n- The third term \\( a_3 = a_2 + b_2 = b_1 + (b_1 + d_b) = 2b_1 + d_b \\).\n- The fourth term \\( a_4 = a_3 + b_3 = 2b_1 + d_b + (b_1 + 2d_b) = 3b_1 + 3d_b \\).\n- The fifth term \\( a_5 = a_4 + b_4 = 3b_1 + 3d_b + (b_1 + 3d_b) = 4b_1 + 6d_b \\).\n\nWe know from the second sequence that:\n\\[ b_5 = b_1 + 4d_b = 3 \\]\n\nFrom this equation, we can express \\( b_1 \\) in terms of \\( d_b \\):\n\\[ b_1 = 3 - 4d_b \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( b_1 = 3 - 4d_b \\) into the expression for \\( a_5 \\):\n\\[ a_5 = 4b_1 + 6d_b = 4(3 - 4d_b) + 6d_b \\]\n\\[ a_5 = 12 - 16d_b + 6d_b \\]\n\\[ a_5 = 12 - 10d_b \\]\n\nSince \\( b_5 = 3 \\), we can solve for \\( d_b \\):\n\\[ b_1 + 4d_b = 3 \\]\n\\[ 3 - 4d_b + 4d_b = 3 \\]\n\\[ 3 = 3 \\]\n\nThis confirms our expression for \\( b_1 \\) is consistent. Now, we need to find \\( a_5 \\):\n\\[ a_5 = 12 - 10d_b \\]\n\nSince we don't have a specific value for \\( d_b \\) from the given information, we can only express \\( a_5 \\) in terms of \\( d_b \\). However, the problem implies that the sequences are consistent with the given conditions, so we assume \\( d_b = 0 \\) for simplicity, which gives:\n\\[ a_5 = 12 \\]\n\nThus, the fifth term of the first sequence is \\(\\boxed{12}\\)."

"Let John's age be \\(10a + b\\), where \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) are the digits of John's age. Then, his father's age is \\(10b + a\\).\n\nAccording to the problem, the positive difference between their ages is 27 years:\n\n\\[\n|(10b + a) - (10a + b)| = 27\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n|9b - 9a| = 27\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by 9 gives:\n\n\\[\n|b - a| = 3\n\\]\n\nAdditionally, the sum of the digits in each age is 5:\n\n\\[\na + b = 5\n\\]\n\nWe now have two equations:\n\n1. \\(b - a = 3\\) or \\(a - b = 3\\)\n2. \\(a + b = 5\\)\n\nLet's solve these equations:\n\n**Case 1:** \\(b - a = 3\\)\n\nFrom \\(b - a = 3\\), we have \\(b = a + 3\\).\n\nSubstitute \\(b = a + 3\\) into \\(a + b = 5\\):\n\n\\[\na + (a + 3) = 5\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2a + 3 = 5\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2a = 2\n\\]\n\n\\[\na = 1\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(a = 1\\) back into \\(b = a + 3\\):\n\n\\[\nb = 1 + 3 = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, John's age is \\(10a + b = 10(1) + 4 = 14\\) and his father's age is \\(10b + a = 10(4) + 1 = 41\\).\n\n**Case 2:** \\(a - b = 3\\)\n\nFrom \\(a - b = 3\\), we have \\(a = b + 3\\).\n\nSubstitute \\(a = b + 3\\) into \\(a + b = 5\\):\n\n\\[\n(b + 3) + b = 5\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2b + 3 = 5\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2b = 2\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = 1\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(b = 1\\) back into \\(a = b + 3\\):\n\n\\[\na = 1 + 3 = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, John's age is \\(10a + b = 10(4) + 1 = 41\\) and his father's age is \\(10b + a = 10(1) + 4 = 14\\).\n\nIn both cases, the father's age is 41. Therefore, the number of years in John's father's age is \\(\\boxed{41}\\)."
'To solve this problem, we need to consider the process of recycling the cans iteratively. We start with 125 aluminum cans and recycle them into new cans, then recycle those new cans, and so on, until we can no longer make a complete new can.\n\n1. **First Iteration:**\n   - Start with 125 cans.\n   - Since 5 cans are needed to make 1 new can, we can make \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{125}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 25 \\) new cans.\n   - After making 25 new cans, we have \\( 125 - 25 \\times 5 = 0 \\) leftover cans.\n\n2. **Second Iteration:**\n   - Now, we have 25 new cans.\n   - Recycle these 25 cans to make \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{25}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 5 \\) new cans.\n   - After making 5 new cans, we have \\( 25 - 5 \\times 5 = 0 \\) leftover cans.\n\n3. **Third Iteration:**\n   - Now, we have 5 new cans.\n   - Recycle these 5 cans to make \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{5}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 1 \\) new can.\n   - After making 1 new can, we have \\( 5 - 1 \\times 5 = 0 \\) leftover cans.\n\n4. **Fourth Iteration:**\n   - Now, we have 1 new can.\n   - Recycle this 1 can to make \\( \\left\\lfloor \\frac{1}{5} \\right\\rfloor = 0 \\) new cans.\n   - We cannot make any more new cans from 1 can.\n\nAdding up all the new cans made in each iteration, we have \\( 25 + 5 + 1 = 31 \\) new cans.\n\nTherefore, the total number of new cans that can eventually be made from 125 aluminum cans is \\(\\boxed{31}\\).'

'Given that \\(a, b, c, d\\) form an increasing arithmetic sequence, we can express them as:\n\\[\nb = a + k, \\quad c = a + 2k, \\quad d = a + 3k\n\\]\nfor some positive real number \\(k\\).\n\nAdditionally, since \\(a, b, d\\) form a geometric sequence, we have:\n\\[\nb^2 = ad\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the expressions for \\(b\\) and \\(d\\) from the arithmetic sequence:\n\\[\n(a + k)^2 = a(a + 3k)\n\\]\n\nExpanding both sides:\n\\[\na^2 + 2ak + k^2 = a^2 + 3ak\n\\]\n\nSubtract \\(a^2\\) from both sides:\n\\[\n2ak + k^2 = 3ak\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\\[\nk^2 = ak\n\\]\n\nSince \\(k\\) is positive, we can divide both sides by \\(k\\):\n\\[\nk = a\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\(k = a\\) back into the expressions for \\(b\\), \\(c\\), and \\(d\\):\n\\[\nb = a + a = 2a, \\quad c = a + 2a = 3a, \\quad d = a + 3a = 4a\n\\]\n\nWe need to find \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\):\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{d} = \\frac{a}{4a} = \\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{4}}\\).'

'Let \\( x = n + f \\), where \\( n \\) is an integer and \\( 0 \\leq f < 1 \\). Then \\( \\lceil x \\rceil = n + 1 \\) if \\( f > 0 \\) and \\( \\lceil x \\rceil = n \\) if \\( f = 0 \\).\n\nGiven the equation:\n\n\\[\n\\lceil x \\rceil + x = \\frac{23}{7}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( x = n + f \\):\n\n\\[\n\\lceil x \\rceil + n + f = \\frac{23}{7}\n\\]\n\nConsider the case \\( f > 0 \\), so \\( \\lceil x \\rceil = n + 1 \\):\n\n\\[\n(n + 1) + n + f = \\frac{23}{7}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2n + 1 + f = \\frac{23}{7}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf = \\frac{23}{7} - 2n - 1\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf = \\frac{23}{7} - \\frac{14}{7} - \\frac{14n}{7}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf = \\frac{9}{7} - \\frac{14n}{7}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( 0 \\leq f < 1 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n0 \\leq \\frac{9}{7} - \\frac{14n}{7} < 1\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by 7:\n\n\\[\n0 \\leq 9 - 14n < 7\n\\]\n\nSolving the inequalities:\n\n1. \\( 9 - 14n \\geq 0 \\)\n\n\\[\n9 \\geq 14n\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn \\leq \\frac{9}{14}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( n \\) is an integer, \\( n \\leq 0 \\).\n\n2. \\( 9 - 14n < 7 \\)\n\n\\[\n2 < 14n\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn > \\frac{1}{7}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( n \\) is an integer, \\( n \\geq 1 \\).\n\nThe only integer \\( n \\) that satisfies both conditions is \\( n = 1 \\).\n\nSubstitute \\( n = 1 \\) back into the expression for \\( f \\):\n\n\\[\nf = \\frac{9}{7} - \\frac{14 \\times 1}{7} = \\frac{9}{7} - 2 = \\frac{9}{7} - \\frac{14}{7} = -\\frac{5}{7}\n\\]\n\nSince \\( f \\) must be non-negative, this is incorrect. 'February typically has 28 days, except in a leap year when it has 29 days. Since Suzanne walks every third day, we need to determine how many days she will walk in February.\n\n1. **Non-Leap Year (28 days):**\n   - Days Suzanne walks: 1st, 4th, 7th, 10th, 13th, 16th, 19th, 22nd, 25th, 28th.\n   - Total number of days she walks: 10 days.\n   - Total miles walked: \\(10 \\times 4 = 40\\) miles.\n\n2. **Leap Year (29 days):**\n   - Days Suzanne walks: 1st, 4th, 7th, 10th, 13th, 16th, 19th, 22nd, 25th, 28th.\n   - Total number of days she walks: 10 days (since the 29th is not a multiple of 3).\n   - Total miles walked: \\(10 \\times 4 = 40\\) miles.\n\nIn both cases, the fewest number of miles Suzanne can walk in February is 40 miles. Therefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{40}\\).'
'To simplify and rationalize the expression \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{160}}{\\sqrt{252}} \\times \\frac{\\sqrt{245}}{\\sqrt{108}}\\), we start by simplifying each square root individually.\n\n1. **Simplify \\(\\sqrt{160}\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{160} = \\sqrt{16 \\times 10} = \\sqrt{16} \\times \\sqrt{10} = 4\\sqrt{10}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Simplify \\(\\sqrt{252}\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{252} = \\sqrt{4 \\times 63} = \\sqrt{4} \\times \\sqrt{63} = 2\\sqrt{63}\n   \\]\n   Further simplify \\(\\sqrt{63}\\):\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{63} = \\sqrt{9 \\times 7} = \\sqrt{9} \\times \\sqrt{7} = 3\\sqrt{7}\n   \\]\n   So, \\(\\sqrt{252} = 2 \\times 3\\sqrt{7} = 6\\sqrt{7}\\).\n\n3. **Simplify \\(\\sqrt{245}\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{245} = \\sqrt{49 \\times 5} = \\sqrt{49} \\times \\sqrt{5} = 7\\sqrt{5}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Simplify \\(\\sqrt{108}\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{108} = \\sqrt{36 \\times 3} = \\sqrt{36} \\times \\sqrt{3} = 6\\sqrt{3}\n   \\]\n\nNow substitute these simplified forms back into the original expression:\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{160}}{\\sqrt{252}} \\times \\frac{\\sqrt{245}}{\\sqrt{108}} = \\frac{4\\sqrt{10}}{6\\sqrt{7}} \\times \\frac{7\\sqrt{5}}{6\\sqrt{3}}\n\\]\n\nCombine the fractions:\n\\[\n= \\frac{4 \\times 7 \\times \\sqrt{10} \\times \\sqrt{5}}{6 \\times 6 \\times \\sqrt{7} \\times \\sqrt{3}}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\\[\n= \\frac{28 \\times \\sqrt{50}}{36 \\times \\sqrt{21}}\n\\]\n\nSimplify \\(\\sqrt{50}\\) and \\(\\sqrt{21}\\):\n\\[\n\\sqrt{50} = \\sqrt{25 \\times 2} = 5\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\\[\n\\sqrt{21} = \\sqrt{3 \\times 7}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back:\n\\[\n= \\frac{28 \\times 5\\sqrt{2}}{36 \\times \\sqrt{21}} = \\frac{140\\sqrt{2}}{36\\sqrt{21}}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\\[\n= \\frac{35\\sqrt{2}}{9\\sqrt{21}}\n\\]\n\nRationalize the denominator by multiplying the numerator and the denominator by \\(\\sqrt{21}\\):\n\\[\n= \\frac{35\\sqrt{2} \\times \\sqrt{21}}{9 \\times 21} = \\frac{35\\sqrt{42}}{189}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\\[\n= \\frac{35}{189} \\times \\sqrt{42}\n\\]\n\nThe greatest common divisor of 35 and 189 is 7, so divide both by 7:\n\\[\n= \\frac{5}{27} \\times \\sqrt{42}\n\\]\n\nThus, the completely simplified and rationalized expression is:\n\\[\n\\frac{5\\sqrt{42}}{27}\n\\]'
'To find the value of \\( b \\) in the parabola \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\) with the given conditions, we start by using the vertex form of a parabola. The vertex form is given by:\n\n\\[ y = a(x - h)^2 + k \\]\n\nwhere \\((h, k)\\) is the vertex of the parabola. Given that the vertex is \\((p, p)\\), we can write:\n\n\\[ y = a(x - p)^2 + p \\]\n\nExpanding this, we have:\n\n\\[ y = a(x^2 - 2px + p^2) + p \\]\n\\[ y = ax^2 - 2apx + ap^2 + p \\]\n\nComparing this with the standard form \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\), we identify:\n\n\\[ b = -2ap \\]\n\\[ c = ap^2 + p \\]\n\nWe are also given that the \\( y \\)-intercept is \\((0, -p)\\). This means that when \\( x = 0 \\), \\( y = -p \\). Substituting \\( x = 0 \\) into the standard form, we get:\n\n\\[ -p = a(0)^2 + b(0) + c \\]\n\\[ -p = c \\]\n\nFrom the expression for \\( c \\) we found earlier, we have:\n\n\\[ c = ap^2 + p \\]\n\nSetting this equal to \\(-p\\), we get:\n\n\\[ ap^2 + p = -p \\]\n\nSolving for \\( a \\), we subtract \\( p \\) from both sides:\n\n\\[ ap^2 = -2p \\]\n\nSince \\( p \\neq 0 \\), we can divide both sides by \\( p \\):\n\n\\[ ap = -2 \\]\n\nNow, substituting \\( ap = -2 \\) into the expression for \\( b \\):\n\n\\[ b = -2ap = -2(-2) = 4 \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To find the coefficient of \\(x^3\\) in the product of the polynomials \\(7x^4 - 3x^3 - 3x^2 - 8x + 1\\) and \\(8x^4 + 2x^3 - 7x^2 + 3x + 4\\), we need to consider the terms from each polynomial that can multiply together to produce an \\(x^3\\) term.\n\nThe possible combinations are:\n1. The constant term from the first polynomial (\\(1\\)) and the \\(x^3\\) term from the second polynomial (\\(2x^3\\)).\n2. The \\(x\\) term from the first polynomial (\\(-8x\\)) and the \\(x^2\\) term from the second polynomial (\\(-7x^2\\)).\n3. The \\(x^2\\) term from the first polynomial (\\(-3x^2\\)) and the \\(x\\) term from the second polynomial (\\(3x\\)).\n4. The \\(x^3\\) term from the first polynomial (\\(-3x^3\\)) and the constant term from the second polynomial (\\(4\\)).\n\nNow, we calculate each contribution:\n1. \\(1 \\cdot 2x^3 = 2x^3\\)\n2. \\(-8x \\cdot -7x^2 = 56x^3\\)\n3. \\(-3x^2 \\cdot 3x = -9x^3\\)\n4. \\(-3x^3 \\cdot 4 = -12x^3\\)\n\nAdding these contributions together gives:\n\\[ 2x^3 + 56x^3 - 9x^3 - 12x^3 = (2 + 56 - 9 - 12)x^3 = 37x^3 \\]\n\nThus, the coefficient of \\(x^3\\) in the product is \\(\\boxed{37}\\).'
'To find the sum of all values of \\( x \\) such that \\( f(x) = 0 \\), we need to solve the equation \\( f(x) = 0 \\) for each piece of the piecewise function.\n\n1. **For \\( x \\le 3 \\):**\n\n   The function is \\( f(x) = 2x + 1 \\).\n\n   Set \\( 2x + 1 = 0 \\) and solve for \\( x \\):\n\n   \\[\n   2x + 1 = 0 \\implies 2x = -1 \\implies x = -\\frac{1}{2}\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\( -\\frac{1}{2} \\le 3 \\), this solution is valid.\n\n2. **For \\( x > 3 \\):**\n\n   The function is \\( f(x) = 8 - 4x \\).\n\n   Set \\( 8 - 4x = 0 \\) and solve for \\( x \\):\n\n   \\[\n   8 - 4x = 0 \\implies 4x = 8 \\implies x = 2\n   \\]\n\n   However, \\( x = 2 \\) does not satisfy \\( x > 3 \\), so this solution is not valid.\n\nThe only valid solution is \\( x = -\\frac{1}{2} \\).\n\nThus, the sum of all values of \\( x \\) such that \\( f(x) = 0 \\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{1}{2}}\\).'
'To find the domain of the function \\( f(x) = \\frac{2x-7}{\\sqrt{x^2-5x+6}} \\), we need to determine the values of \\( x \\) for which the function is defined. The function is defined when the denominator is not zero and the expression under the square root is non-negative.\n\n1. **Non-zero denominator**: The denominator is \\(\\sqrt{x^2-5x+6}\\). For the square root to be defined and non-zero, \\(x^2-5x+6 > 0\\).\n\n2. **Solve the inequality \\(x^2-5x+6 > 0\\)**:\n   - Factor the quadratic: \\(x^2-5x+6 = (x-2)(x-3)\\).\n   - Solve the equation \\((x-2)(x-3) = 0\\) to find the critical points: \\(x = 2\\) and \\(x = 3\\).\n\n3. **Test intervals determined by the critical points**:\n   - Interval \\((-\\infty, 2)\\): Choose \\(x = 1\\), \\((1-2)(1-3) = (-1)(-2) = 2 > 0\\).\n   - Interval \\((2, 3)\\): Choose \\(x = 2.5\\), \\((2.5-2)(2.5-3) = (0.5)(-0.5) = -0.25 < 0\\).\n   - Interval \\((3, \\infty)\\): Choose \\(x = 4\\), \\((4-2)(4-3) = (2)(1) = 2 > 0\\).\n\n4. **Conclusion**: The expression \\(x^2-5x+6\\) is positive in the intervals \\((-\\infty, 2)\\) and \\((3, \\infty)\\).\n\nTherefore, the domain of the function \\( f(x) \\) is the union of these intervals, excluding the points where the denominator is zero:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{(-\\infty, 2) \\cup (3, \\infty)}\n\\]'
'To solve the equation \\(\\sqrt{x + \\sqrt{x + \\sqrt{x + \\ldots}}} = 5\\), we first recognize that the expression inside the square root is self-similar. This means we can set it equal to a variable, say \\(y\\), such that:\n\n\\[ y = \\sqrt{x + y}. \\]\n\nGiven that \\(y = 5\\), we substitute this into the equation:\n\n\\[ 5 = \\sqrt{x + 5}. \\]\n\nNext, we square both sides to eliminate the square root:\n\n\\[ 25 = x + 5. \\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we subtract 5 from both sides:\n\n\\[ x = 20. \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{20}\\).'
'To find the price that results in maximum revenue, we first need to express the revenue as a function of the price. Let \\( p \\) be the price decrease in multiples of $5. Then the new price of the smartphone is \\( 450 - 5p \\), and the number of smartphones sold is \\( 500 + 10p \\).\n\nThe revenue \\( R \\) as a function of \\( p \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nR(p) = (450 - 5p)(500 + 10p)\n\\]\n\nExpanding this expression, we have:\n\n\\[\nR(p) = 450 \\times 500 + 450 \\times 10p - 5p \\times 500 - 5p \\times 10p\n\\]\n\n\\[\nR(p) = 225000 + 4500p - 2500p - 50p^2\n\\]\n\n\\[\nR(p) = 225000 + 2000p - 50p^2\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic function in the form \\( R(p) = -50p^2 + 2000p + 225000 \\). The maximum revenue occurs at the vertex of this parabola. The vertex \\( p \\) of a parabola \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\np = -\\frac{b}{2a}\n\\]\n\nHere, \\( a = -50 \\) and \\( b = 2000 \\), so:\n\n\\[\np = -\\frac{2000}{2 \\times -50} = \\frac{2000}{100} = 20\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( p = 20 \\) back into the expression for the price, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\text{New price} = 450 - 5 \\times 20 = 450 - 100 = 350\n\\]\n\nThus, the price that results in maximum revenue is \\(\\boxed{350}\\) dollars.'
'To find the sum of all possible values of \\( s \\) such that the roots of the quadratic expression \\(\\frac{1}{2}x^2 + sx - \\frac{1}{2}\\) are integers, we start by considering the quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2}x^2 + sx - \\frac{1}{2} = 0\n\\]\n\nMultiplying the entire equation by 2 to eliminate the fractions, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 2sx - 1 = 0\n\\]\n\nFor the roots to be integers, the discriminant of this quadratic equation must be a perfect square. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = (2s)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-1) = 4s^2 + 4 = 4(s^2 + 1)\n\\]\n\nFor \\(\\Delta\\) to be a perfect square, \\(s^2 + 1\\) must be a perfect square. Let \\(s^2 + 1 = k^2\\) for some integer \\(k\\). Then:\n\n\\[\nk^2 - s^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nThis can be factored using the difference of squares:\n\n\\[\n(k - s)(k + s) = 1\n\\]\n\nThe integer solutions to this equation are \\((k - s, k + s) = (1, 1)\\) and \\((-1, -1)\\).\n\n1. For \\((k - s, k + s) = (1, 1)\\):\n   - \\(k - s = 1\\)\n   - \\(k + s = 1\\)\n\n   Solving these equations simultaneously, we add them:\n\n   \\[\n   2k = 2 \\implies k = 1\n   \\]\n\n   Substituting \\(k = 1\\) into \\(k - s = 1\\):\n\n   \\[\n   1 - s = 1 \\implies s = 0\n   \\]\n\n2. For \\((k - s, k + s) = (-1, -1)\\):\n   - \\(k - s = -1\\)\n   - \\(k + s = -1\\)\n\n   Solving these equations simultaneously, we add them:\n\n   \\[\n   2k = -2 \\implies k = -1\n   \\]\n\n   Substituting \\(k = -1\\) into \\(k - s = -1\\):\n\n   \\[\n   -1 - s = -1 \\implies s = 0\n   \\]\n\nThus, the only possible value for \\(s\\) is 0. Therefore, the sum of all possible values of \\(s\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{0}\n\\]'
'To find the value of \\(-a-b^2+3ab\\) given \\(a=-1\\) and \\(b=5\\), we substitute these values into the expression:\n\n\\[\n-a-b^2+3ab = -(-1) - (5)^2 + 3(-1)(5)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term:\n\n1. \\(-(-1) = 1\\)\n2. \\((5)^2 = 25\\)\n3. \\(3(-1)(5) = -15\\)\n\nSubstituting these results back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n1 - 25 - 15\n\\]\n\nNow, perform the arithmetic:\n\n\\[\n1 - 25 = -24\n\\]\n\\[\n-24 - 15 = -39\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{-39}\\).'
'To find the slope of the line containing the midpoints of the given segments, we first need to determine the coordinates of these midpoints.\n\n1. **Midpoint of the segment with endpoints \\((2, 4)\\) and \\((0, -2)\\):**\n\n   The formula for the midpoint \\((x_m, y_m)\\) of a segment with endpoints \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is:\n   \\[\n   (x_m, y_m) = \\left( \\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2} \\right)\n   \\]\n\n   Applying this formula:\n   \\[\n   \\left( \\frac{2 + 0}{2}, \\frac{4 + (-2)}{2} \\right) = \\left( \\frac{2}{2}, \\frac{2}{2} \\right) = (1, 1)\n   \\]\n\n2. **Midpoint of the segment with endpoints \\((5, 1)\\) and \\((1, 5)\\):**\n\n   Applying the midpoint formula again:\n   \\[\n   \\left( \\frac{5 + 1}{2}, \\frac{1 + 5}{2} \\right) = \\left( \\frac{6}{2}, \\frac{6}{2} \\right) = (3, 3)\n   \\]\n\n3. **Slope of the line through the midpoints \\((1, 1)\\) and \\((3, 3)\\):**\n\n   The formula for the slope \\(m\\) of a line through two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is:\n   \\[\n   m = \\frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}\n   \\]\n\n   Applying this formula:\n   \\[\n   m = \\frac{3 - 1}{3 - 1} = \\frac{2}{2} = 1\n   \\]\n\nThus, the slope of the line containing the midpoints of the given segments is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To find the future value of Paula's investment with quarterly compounding interest, we use the formula for compound interest:\n\n\\[\nA = P \\left(1 + \\frac{r}{n}\\right)^{nt}\n\\]\n\nwhere:\n- \\( A \\) is the amount of money accumulated after \\( n \\) years, including interest.\n- \\( P \\) is the principal amount (initial investment), which is \\$10,000.\n- \\( r \\) is the annual interest rate (decimal), which is 0.10 for 10%.\n- \\( n \\) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year, which is 4 for quarterly.\n- \\( t \\) is the time the money is invested for in years, which is 5.\n\nSubstituting the given values into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\left(1 + \\frac{0.10}{4}\\right)^{4 \\times 5}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\left(1 + 0.025\\right)^{20}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\left(1.025\\right)^{20}\n\\]\n\nNow, we calculate \\( (1.025)^{20} \\):\n\n\\[\n(1.025)^{20} \\approx 1.638616\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the future value \\( A \\) is:\n\n\\[\nA = 10000 \\times 1.638616 \\approx 16386.16\n\\]\n\nThus, Paula's investment is worth approximately \\$16,386.16 at the end of 5 years. Therefore, the answer is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{16386.16}\n\\]"
"To find the value of \\( x \\) that satisfies both equations, we need to solve the system of equations:\n\n1. \\( 18x^2 + 25x - 3 = 0 \\)\n2. \\( 4x^2 + 8x + 3 = 0 \\)\n\nSince both equations are quadratic, they can have at most two solutions each. We need to find a common solution to both equations.\n\nFirst, let's solve the second equation:\n\n\\[ 4x^2 + 8x + 3 = 0 \\]\n\nUsing the quadratic formula \\( x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 4 \\), \\( b = 8 \\), and \\( c = 3 \\):\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{-8 \\pm \\sqrt{8^2 - 4 \\cdot 4 \\cdot 3}}{2 \\cdot 4} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-8 \\pm \\sqrt{64 - 48}}{8} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-8 \\pm \\sqrt{16}}{8} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-8 \\pm 4}{8} \\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{-8 + 4}{8} = \\frac{-4}{8} = -\\frac{1}{2} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-8 - 4}{8} = \\frac{-12}{8} = -\\frac{3}{2} \\]\n\nNow, we need to check which of these solutions also satisfies the first equation:\n\nFor \\( x = -\\frac{1}{2} \\):\n\n\\[ 18\\left(-\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2 + 25\\left(-\\frac{1}{2}\\right) - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ 18 \\cdot \\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{25}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{18}{4} - \\frac{25}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{9}{2} - \\frac{25}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{9 - 25}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{-16}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ -8 - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ -11 \\neq 0 \\]\n\nSo, \\( x = -\\frac{1}{2} \\) is not a solution.\n\nFor \\( x = -\\frac{3}{2} \\):\n\n\\[ 18\\left(-\\frac{3}{2}\\right)^2 + 25\\left(-\\frac{3}{2}\\right) - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ 18 \\cdot \\frac{9}{4} - \\frac{75}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{162}{4} - \\frac{75}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{81}{2} - \\frac{75}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{81 - 75}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{6}{2} - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ 3 - 3 = 0 \\]\n\\[ 0 = 0 \\]\n\nThus, \\( x = -\\frac{3}{2} \\) satisfies both equations.\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{3}{2}}\\)."
'To solve for \\((p-1)(q-1)\\) given that \\(\\frac{1}{p} + \\frac{1}{q} = 1\\), we start by manipulating the given equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{p} + \\frac{1}{q} = 1\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{q + p}{pq} = 1\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by \\(pq\\) gives:\n\n\\[\nq + p = pq\n\\]\n\nWe want to find \\((p-1)(q-1)\\). Expanding this expression, we have:\n\n\\[\n(p-1)(q-1) = pq - p - q + 1\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(q + p = pq\\) into the expression, we get:\n\n\\[\npq - p - q + 1 = pq - (q + p) + 1\n\\]\n\nSince \\(q + p = pq\\), this simplifies to:\n\n\\[\npq - pq + 1 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\((p-1)(q-1)\\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To solve for \\(24x - 14y\\), we first need to find the values of \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) from the given system of equations:\n\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\n5x - 2y &= 7, \\\\\n3x + y &= 2.\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nWe can use the method of substitution or elimination. Here, we'll use elimination. First, let's eliminate \\(y\\) by making the coefficients of \\(y\\) in both equations equal. We can do this by multiplying the second equation by 2:\n\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\n5x - 2y &= 7, \\\\\n6x + 2y &= 4.\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nNow, add the two equations together to eliminate \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n(5x - 2y) + (6x + 2y) = 7 + 4.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n11x = 11.\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we divide both sides by 11:\n\n\\[\nx = 1.\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\(x = 1\\), substitute it back into the second original equation to solve for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n3(1) + y = 2.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3 + y = 2.\n\\]\n\nSubtract 3 from both sides:\n\n\\[\ny = 2 - 3 = -1.\n\\]\n\nNow we have \\(x = 1\\) and \\(y = -1\\). We can substitute these values into \\(24x - 14y\\):\n\n\\[\n24x - 14y = 24(1) - 14(-1).\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n24 + 14 = 38.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(24x - 14y\\) is \\(\\boxed{38}\\)."
'To simplify \\(\\frac{3}{\\sqrt[5]{16}} + \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\) and rationalize the denominator, we will handle each term separately.\n\n1. **Rationalizing \\(\\frac{3}{\\sqrt[5]{16}}\\):**\n\n   The denominator is \\(\\sqrt[5]{16}\\). We can express 16 as \\(2^4\\), so \\(\\sqrt[5]{16} = (2^4)^{1/5} = 2^{4/5}\\).\n\n   To rationalize, multiply the numerator and the denominator by \\(2^{1/5}\\) to make the denominator a whole number:\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{3}{2^{4/5}} \\cdot \\frac{2^{1/5}}{2^{1/5}} = \\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{1/5}}{2^{5/5}} = \\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{1/5}}{2} = \\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{1/5}}{2}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Rationalizing \\(\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}\\):**\n\n   Multiply the numerator and the denominator by \\(\\sqrt{3}\\):\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{\\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{3}\n   \\]\n\nNow, we combine the two rationalized terms:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{1/5}}{2} + \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{3}\n\\]\n\nTo combine these fractions, find a common denominator, which is 6:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{1/5}}{2} = \\frac{3 \\cdot 2^{1/5} \\cdot 3}{6} = \\frac{9 \\cdot 2^{1/5}}{6}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{3} = \\frac{\\sqrt{3} \\cdot 2}{6} = \\frac{2\\sqrt{3}}{6}\n\\]\n\nCombine the fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{9 \\cdot 2^{1/5} + 2\\sqrt{3}}{6}\n\\]\n\nThis expression is in the form \\(\\frac{a^2\\sqrt[5]{b} + b\\sqrt{a}}{ab}\\), where \\(a = 3\\) and \\(b = 2\\).\n\nThus, the sum \\(a + b = 3 + 2 = \\boxed{5}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( y \\) when \\( x = 6 \\) for the parabola \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\) with vertex \\((2, 3)\\) and passing through the point \\((4, 4)\\), we can use the vertex form of a parabola:\n\n\\[ y = a(x - h)^2 + k \\]\n\nwhere \\((h, k)\\) is the vertex of the parabola. Here, \\( h = 2 \\) and \\( k = 3 \\), so the equation becomes:\n\n\\[ y = a(x - 2)^2 + 3 \\]\n\nWe know the parabola passes through the point \\((4, 4)\\). Substituting \\( x = 4 \\) and \\( y = 4 \\) into the equation, we can solve for \\( a \\):\n\n\\[ 4 = a(4 - 2)^2 + 3 \\]\n\n\\[ 4 = a(2)^2 + 3 \\]\n\n\\[ 4 = 4a + 3 \\]\n\nSubtract 3 from both sides:\n\n\\[ 1 = 4a \\]\n\nDivide by 4:\n\n\\[ a = \\frac{1}{4} \\]\n\nNow that we have \\( a = \\frac{1}{4} \\), the equation of the parabola is:\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{1}{4}(x - 2)^2 + 3 \\]\n\nWe need to find the value of \\( y \\) when \\( x = 6 \\):\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{1}{4}(6 - 2)^2 + 3 \\]\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{1}{4}(4)^2 + 3 \\]\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{1}{4} \\times 16 + 3 \\]\n\n\\[ y = 4 + 3 \\]\n\n\\[ y = 7 \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( y \\) when \\( x = 6 \\) is \\(\\boxed{7}\\).'
'To find the point \\( T \\) such that \\( Q \\) is the midpoint of segment \\(\\overline{PT}\\), we use the midpoint formula. The midpoint \\( M \\) of a segment with endpoints \\( (x_1, y_1) \\) and \\( (x_2, y_2) \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nM = \\left( \\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\( P = (5, 3) \\) and \\( Q = (-3, 6) \\) is the midpoint, we set:\n\n\\[\nQ = \\left( \\frac{5 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{3 + y_2}{2} \\right) = (-3, 6)\n\\]\n\nWe solve for \\( x_2 \\) and \\( y_2 \\):\n\n1. For the x-coordinate:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{5 + x_2}{2} = -3\n   \\]\n   Multiply both sides by 2:\n   \\[\n   5 + x_2 = -6\n   \\]\n   Subtract 5 from both sides:\n   \\[\n   x_2 = -11\n   \\]\n\n2. For the y-coordinate:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{3 + y_2}{2} = 6\n   \\]\n   Multiply both sides by 2:\n   \\[\n   3 + y_2 = 12\n   \\]\n   Subtract 3 from both sides:\n   \\[\n   y_2 = 9\n   \\]\n\nThus, the coordinates of point \\( T \\) are \\((-11, 9)\\).\n\nTherefore, the point \\( T \\) is \\(\\boxed{(-11, 9)}\\).'
'To find the equation of the circle, we need to determine its center and radius. The center of the circle is given as \\((-1, 1)\\), and the radius can be determined using the point \\((1, 2)\\) that lies on the circle.\n\nThe distance between the center \\((-1, 1)\\) and the point \\((1, 2)\\) is the radius \\(r\\). We calculate it as follows:\n\n\\[\nr = \\sqrt{(1 - (-1))^2 + (2 - 1)^2} = \\sqrt{(1 + 1)^2 + (2 - 1)^2} = \\sqrt{2^2 + 1^2} = \\sqrt{4 + 1} = \\sqrt{5}\n\\]\n\nThe standard form of the equation of a circle with center \\((h, k)\\) and radius \\(r\\) is:\n\n\\[\n(x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the center \\((-1, 1)\\) and radius \\(\\sqrt{5}\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n(x + 1)^2 + (y - 1)^2 = 5\n\\]\n\nExpanding this equation:\n\n\\[\n(x + 1)^2 = x^2 + 2x + 1\n\\]\n\\[\n(y - 1)^2 = y^2 - 2y + 1\n\\]\n\nAdding these, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 2x + 1 + y^2 - 2y + 1 = 5\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + 2x - 2y + 2 = 5\n\\]\n\nSubtracting 5 from both sides gives:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + 2x - 2y + 2 - 5 = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 + 2x - 2y - 3 = 0\n\\]\n\nComparing this with the given form \\(x^2 + Ay^2 + Bx + Cy + D = 0\\), we identify:\n\n- \\(A = 1\\)\n- \\(B = 2\\)\n- \\(C = -2\\)\n- \\(D = -3\\)\n\nThus, \\(A + B + C + D = 1 + 2 - 2 - 3 = -2\\).\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(A + B + C + D\\) is \\(\\boxed{-2}\\).'
'To find the maximum value of \\( f^{-1}(x) \\), we need to determine the maximum \\( x \\) value for which \\( f(x) \\) is defined, given that \\( f(x) \\) is defined on \\( 1 \\le x \\le 6 \\).\n\nThe function \\( f(x) \\) is defined on the interval \\( 1 \\le x \\le 6 \\), and we need to find the range of \\( f(x) \\) within this interval. Observing the graph:\n\n- From \\( x = 1 \\) to \\( x = 3 \\), the function decreases from \\( f(1) = 2 \\) to \\( f(3) = 0 \\).\n- From \\( x = 3 \\) to \\( x = 5 \\), the function increases from \\( f(3) = 3 \\) to \\( f(5) = 2 \\).\n- From \\( x = 5 \\) to \\( x = 6 \\), the function increases from \\( f(5) = -2 \\) to \\( f(6) = 0 \\).\n\nThe range of \\( f(x) \\) is from \\(-2\\) to \\(3\\). The inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) will be defined for \\( y \\) values in this range, and it will map these \\( y \\) values back to the corresponding \\( x \\) values.\n\nThe maximum value of \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) corresponds to the maximum \\( x \\) value in the domain of \\( f(x) \\), which is \\( x = 6 \\). Therefore, the maximum value of \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
"To find Ben's minimum height, we need to determine the minimum value of the quadratic function \\( h(t) = 2t^2 - 5t + 29 \\).\n\nA quadratic function \\( at^2 + bt + c \\) has its minimum or maximum value at the vertex, which occurs at \\( t = -\\frac{b}{2a} \\). For this function, \\( a = 2 \\) and \\( b = -5 \\).\n\nCalculate the vertex:\n\n\\[\nt = -\\frac{-5}{2 \\times 2} = \\frac{5}{4}\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( t = \\frac{5}{4} \\) back into the function to find the minimum height:\n\n\\[\nh\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right) = 2\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right)^2 - 5\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right) + 29\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\n\\[\n2\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right)^2 = 2 \\times \\frac{25}{16} = \\frac{50}{16} = \\frac{25}{8}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-5\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right) = -\\frac{25}{4}\n\\]\n\nNow, add these results together with 29:\n\n\\[\nh\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right) = \\frac{25}{8} - \\frac{25}{4} + 29\n\\]\n\nConvert \\(-\\frac{25}{4}\\) to have a common denominator with \\(\\frac{25}{8}\\):\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{25}{4} = -\\frac{50}{8}\n\\]\n\nNow, add the fractions:\n\n\\[\nh\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right) = \\frac{25}{8} - \\frac{50}{8} + 29 = -\\frac{25}{8} + 29\n\\]\n\nConvert 29 to a fraction with a denominator of 8:\n\n\\[\n29 = \\frac{232}{8}\n\\]\n\nAdd the fractions:\n\n\\[\nh\\left(\\frac{5}{4}\\right) = -\\frac{25}{8} + \\frac{232}{8} = \\frac{207}{8}\n\\]\n\nConvert \\(\\frac{207}{8}\\) to a decimal:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{207}{8} = 25.875\n\\]\n\nRounding 25.875 to the nearest foot gives:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{26}\n\\]"
'Let the two consecutive odd whole numbers be \\( n \\) and \\( n + 2 \\). The product of these numbers is given by:\n\n\\[\nn(n + 2) = 255\n\\]\n\nExpanding the equation, we have:\n\n\\[\nn^2 + 2n = 255\n\\]\n\nRearranging the terms, we get a quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nn^2 + 2n - 255 = 0\n\\]\n\nTo solve this quadratic equation, we can use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 2 \\), and \\( c = -255 \\). Plugging in these values, we have:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{2^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-255)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{4 + 1020}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{1024}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-2 \\pm 32}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two possible solutions for \\( n \\):\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-2 + 32}{2} = \\frac{30}{2} = 15\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-2 - 32}{2} = \\frac{-34}{2} = -17\n\\]\n\nSince we are looking for odd whole numbers, we take the positive solution \\( n = 15 \\). Therefore, the two consecutive odd numbers are 15 and 17. The greater number is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{17}\n\\]'
'To evaluate \\( f(6) - f(4) \\) for the function \\( f(x) = (x-1)(x-3)(x-7)(x-9) \\), we first calculate \\( f(6) \\) and \\( f(4) \\) separately.\n\n**Step 1: Calculate \\( f(6) \\):**\n\n\\[\nf(6) = (6-1)(6-3)(6-7)(6-9)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 5 \\times 3 \\times (-1) \\times (-3)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 5 \\times 3 \\times 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 45\n\\]\n\n**Step 2: Calculate \\( f(4) \\):**\n\n\\[\nf(4) = (4-1)(4-3)(4-7)(4-9)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 3 \\times 1 \\times (-3) \\times (-5)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 3 \\times 1 \\times 3 \\times 5\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 45\n\\]\n\n**Step 3: Calculate \\( f(6) - f(4) \\):**\n\n\\[\nf(6) - f(4) = 45 - 45 = 0\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(6) - f(4) \\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
'To simplify the expression \\((u+4)(u-1) - (u-3)(u+6)\\), we start by expanding each of the products separately.\n\nFirst, expand \\((u+4)(u-1)\\):\n\\[\n(u+4)(u-1) = u(u-1) + 4(u-1) = u^2 - u + 4u - 4 = u^2 + 3u - 4.\n\\]\n\nNext, expand \\((u-3)(u+6)\\):\n\\[\n(u-3)(u+6) = u(u+6) - 3(u+6) = u^2 + 6u - 3u - 18 = u^2 + 3u - 18.\n\\]\n\nNow, subtract the second expansion from the first:\n\\[\n(u^2 + 3u - 4) - (u^2 + 3u - 18).\n\\]\n\nDistribute the negative sign:\n\\[\nu^2 + 3u - 4 - u^2 - 3u + 18.\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\\[\n(u^2 - u^2) + (3u - 3u) + (-4 + 18) = 0 + 0 + 14 = 14.\n\\]\n\nThus, the simplified expression is \\(\\boxed{14}\\).'
'To simplify the expression \\(\\sqrt{60x} \\cdot \\sqrt{12x} \\cdot \\sqrt{63x}\\), we can use the property of square roots that states \\(\\sqrt{a} \\cdot \\sqrt{b} = \\sqrt{a \\cdot b}\\).\n\nFirst, combine the square roots:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{60x} \\cdot \\sqrt{12x} \\cdot \\sqrt{63x} = \\sqrt{(60x) \\cdot (12x) \\cdot (63x)}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the product inside the square root:\n\n\\[\n60 \\cdot 12 \\cdot 63 = 45360\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{45360x^3}\n\\]\n\nNext, we simplify \\(\\sqrt{45360x^3}\\). Start by factoring 45360:\n\n\\[\n45360 = 2^4 \\cdot 3^4 \\cdot 5 \\cdot 7\n\\]\n\nNow, simplify the square root:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{45360x^3} = \\sqrt{2^4 \\cdot 3^4 \\cdot 5 \\cdot 7 \\cdot x^3}\n\\]\n\nSeparate the perfect squares from the non-perfect squares:\n\n\\[\n= \\sqrt{(2^2 \\cdot 3^2 \\cdot x)^2 \\cdot 5 \\cdot 7 \\cdot x}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\n\\[\n= 2^2 \\cdot 3^2 \\cdot x \\cdot \\sqrt{5 \\cdot 7 \\cdot x}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 4 \\cdot 9 \\cdot x \\cdot \\sqrt{35x}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= 36x \\cdot \\sqrt{35x}\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression in simplest radical form is:\n\n\\[\n36x \\sqrt{35x}\n\\]\n\nSo, the answer is \\(36x \\sqrt{35x}\\).'
'To evaluate \\( f(i) + f(1) + f(-1) + f(-i) \\), we need to apply the piecewise function \\( f(z) \\) to each of the complex numbers \\( i, 1, -1, \\) and \\( -i \\).\n\n1. **Evaluate \\( f(i) \\):**\n   - Since \\( i \\) is not a real number, we use the first case of the piecewise function: \\( f(z) = z^2 \\).\n   - Therefore, \\( f(i) = i^2 = -1 \\).\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(1) \\):**\n   - Since \\( 1 \\) is a real number, we use the second case of the piecewise function: \\( f(z) = z + 2 \\).\n   - Therefore, \\( f(1) = 1 + 2 = 3 \\).\n\n3. **Evaluate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n   - Since \\( -1 \\) is a real number, we use the second case of the piecewise function: \\( f(z) = z + 2 \\).\n   - Therefore, \\( f(-1) = -1 + 2 = 1 \\).\n\n4. **Evaluate \\( f(-i) \\):**\n   - Since \\( -i \\) is not a real number, we use the first case of the piecewise function: \\( f(z) = z^2 \\).\n   - Therefore, \\( f(-i) = (-i)^2 = -1 \\).\n\nNow, we sum these results:\n\\[\nf(i) + f(1) + f(-1) + f(-i) = (-1) + 3 + 1 + (-1) = 2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(i) + f(1) + f(-1) + f(-i) \\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
"To ensure that the graph of \\( y = f(x) \\) intersects every horizontal line at least once, the function must be surjective, meaning it covers all real numbers as outputs.\n\nLet's analyze the function:\n\n1. **For \\( x \\geq a \\):** The function is \\( f(x) = ax^2 \\). This is a quadratic function that opens upwards (since \\( a > 0 \\)) and has a minimum value at \\( x = 0 \\) if \\( a = 0 \\). However, since \\( x \\geq a \\), the minimum value occurs at \\( x = a \\), giving \\( f(a) = aa^2 = a^3 \\).\n\n2. **For \\( x < a \\):** The function is \\( f(x) = ax + 2a \\). This is a linear function with a slope of \\( a \\).\n\nTo ensure the function is surjective, the range of \\( f(x) \\) must be all real numbers. This means:\n\n- The quadratic part \\( ax^2 \\) for \\( x \\geq a \\) must cover all values from \\( a^3 \\) to \\( \\infty \\).\n- The linear part \\( ax + 2a \\) for \\( x < a \\) must cover all values from \\(-\\infty\\) to some value that connects with the quadratic part.\n\nFor the linear part to cover values down to \\(-\\infty\\), the slope \\( a \\) must be negative. However, if \\( a \\) is negative, the quadratic part \\( ax^2 \\) will not cover values up to \\(\\infty\\), as it will open downwards.\n\nThus, \\( a \\) must be positive for the quadratic part to cover values up to \\(\\infty\\). However, if \\( a \\) is positive, the linear part \\( ax + 2a \\) will not cover values down to \\(-\\infty\\).\n\nThe only way to ensure the function is surjective is to have the linear part cover all values from \\(-\\infty\\) to \\( a^3 \\) and the quadratic part cover all values from \\( a^3 \\) to \\(\\infty\\). This requires the linear part to have a slope of zero, meaning \\( a = 0 \\).\n\nHowever, if \\( a = 0 \\), the function becomes:\n\n- \\( f(x) = 0 \\) for \\( x \\geq 0 \\)\n- \\( f(x) = 2a = 0 \\) for \\( x < 0 \\)\n\nThis function is not surjective as it only outputs 0.\n\nTherefore, the largest value of \\( a \\) such that the graph of \\( y = f(x) \\) intersects every horizontal line at least once is \\( a = 0 \\), but this does not satisfy the condition of being surjective. Thus, there is no positive value of \\( a \\) that makes the function surjective. The function cannot be surjective for any real value of \\( a \\)."
'To simplify the expression \\((x^5 + 3x^2 + 3x^5) - (x^7 + 2x^2 + 6x^5)\\), we first distribute the negative sign across the terms in the second set of parentheses:\n\n\\[\nx^5 + 3x^2 + 3x^5 - x^7 - 2x^2 - 6x^5\n\\]\n\nNext, we combine like terms:\n\n- The \\(x^7\\) term: \\(-x^7\\)\n- The \\(x^5\\) terms: \\(x^5 + 3x^5 - 6x^5 = (1 + 3 - 6)x^5 = -2x^5\\)\n- The \\(x^2\\) terms: \\(3x^2 - 2x^2 = 1x^2 = x^2\\)\n\nPutting it all together, the simplified expression is:\n\n\\[\n-x^7 - 2x^5 + x^2\n\\]\n\nThus, the simplified expression is \\(-x^7 - 2x^5 + x^2\\).'
'To solve the equation \\((4x+11)(2x-8) = x(2x+7)\\), we first expand both sides.\n\nExpanding the left side:\n\\[\n(4x+11)(2x-8) = 4x(2x) + 4x(-8) + 11(2x) + 11(-8)\n\\]\n\\[\n= 8x^2 - 32x + 22x - 88\n\\]\n\\[\n= 8x^2 - 10x - 88\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\\[\nx(2x+7) = 2x^2 + 7x\n\\]\n\nNow, equate the expanded forms:\n\\[\n8x^2 - 10x - 88 = 2x^2 + 7x\n\\]\n\nSubtract \\(2x^2 + 7x\\) from both sides to set the equation to zero:\n\\[\n8x^2 - 10x - 88 - 2x^2 - 7x = 0\n\\]\n\\[\n6x^2 - 17x - 88 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\nwhere \\(a = 6\\), \\(b = -17\\), and \\(c = -88\\).\n\nFirst, calculate the discriminant:\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = (-17)^2 - 4 \\cdot 6 \\cdot (-88)\n\\]\n\\[\n= 289 + 2112\n\\]\n\\[\n= 2401\n\\]\n\nThe square root of 2401 is 49, so:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-(-17) \\pm 49}{2 \\cdot 6}\n\\]\n\\[\nx = \\frac{17 \\pm 49}{12}\n\\]\n\nThis gives two solutions:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{17 + 49}{12} = \\frac{66}{12} = \\frac{11}{2}\n\\]\n\\[\nx = \\frac{17 - 49}{12} = \\frac{-32}{12} = -\\frac{8}{3}\n\\]\n\nThe largest value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\frac{11}{2}\\).\n\nThus, the largest value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{11}{2}}\\).'
'To express \\(6x^2 + 17x + 5\\) in the form \\((Ax+1)(Bx+5)\\), we first expand the expression:\n\n\\[\n(Ax+1)(Bx+5) = ABx^2 + (5A + B)x + 5\n\\]\n\nBy comparing coefficients with \\(6x^2 + 17x + 5\\), we get the following system of equations:\n\n1. \\(AB = 6\\)\n2. \\(5A + B = 17\\)\n3. The constant term is already matched: \\(5 = 5\\).\n\nWe need to find integer values for \\(A\\) and \\(B\\) that satisfy these equations. From the first equation, the possible pairs \\((A, B)\\) that satisfy \\(AB = 6\\) are:\n\n- \\((1, 6)\\)\n- \\((2, 3)\\)\n- \\((3, 2)\\)\n- \\((6, 1)\\)\n- \\((-1, -6)\\)\n- \\((-2, -3)\\)\n- \\((-3, -2)\\)\n- \\((-6, -1)\\)\n\nWe test these pairs in the second equation \\(5A + B = 17\\):\n\n- For \\((A, B) = (1, 6)\\), \\(5(1) + 6 = 11\\), which is not 17.\n- For \\((A, B) = (2, 3)\\), \\(5(2) + 3 = 10 + 3 = 13\\), which is not 17.\n- For \\((A, B) = (3, 2)\\), \\(5(3) + 2 = 15 + 2 = 17\\), which satisfies the equation.\n- For \\((A, B) = (6, 1)\\), \\(5(6) + 1 = 30 + 1 = 31\\), which is not 17.\n\nThus, the pair \\((A, B) = (3, 2)\\) satisfies both equations. Therefore, \\(A = 3\\) and \\(B = 2\\).\n\nFinally, we calculate \\(AB\\):\n\n\\[\nAB = 3 \\times 2 = 6\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(AB\\) is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
"To solve the problem, we start by using Vieta's formulas for the quadratic equation \\(x^2 - mx + n = 0\\). According to Vieta's formulas, the sum of the roots \\(k\\) and \\(t\\) is equal to the coefficient of \\(x\\) with the opposite sign, and the product of the roots is equal to the constant term:\n\n\\[\nk + t = m\n\\]\n\\[\nkt = n\n\\]\n\nGiven that \\(m\\) and \\(n\\) are both prime numbers, we need to find values for \\(k\\) and \\(t\\) such that these conditions are satisfied. Since \\(n = kt\\) is a prime number, one of the roots must be 1 (since the only way to express a prime number as a product of two positive integers is \\(1 \\times n\\)). Therefore, we can set \\(t = 1\\) and \\(k = n\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(t = 1\\) into the equation for the sum of the roots, we have:\n\n\\[\nk + 1 = m\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(k = m - 1\\). Since \\(kt = n\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n(m - 1) \\cdot 1 = n\n\\]\n\nThis implies \\(n = m - 1\\). Since \\(n\\) is a prime number, and \\(n = m - 1\\), \\(m\\) must be the next integer after a prime number, which is also a prime number. The smallest such pair of consecutive integers where both are prime is \\(m = 3\\) and \\(n = 2\\).\n\nNow, substituting back, we have:\n\n- \\(m = 3\\)\n- \\(n = 2\\)\n- \\(k = n = 2\\)\n- \\(t = 1\\)\n\nFinally, we calculate \\(m^n + n^m + k^t + t^k\\):\n\n\\[\nm^n = 3^2 = 9\n\\]\n\\[\nn^m = 2^3 = 8\n\\]\n\\[\nk^t = 2^1 = 2\n\\]\n\\[\nt^k = 1^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nAdding these values together:\n\n\\[\nm^n + n^m + k^t + t^k = 9 + 8 + 2 + 1 = 20\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(m^n + n^m + k^t + t^k\\) is \\(\\boxed{20}\\)."
'Given that \\(2ab = 12\\), we want to evaluate \\(8a^2b^2\\).\n\nFirst, solve for \\(ab\\) from the given equation:\n\n\\[\n2ab = 12 \\implies ab = \\frac{12}{2} = 6\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\(8a^2b^2\\). Notice that:\n\n\\[\na^2b^2 = (ab)^2\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n8a^2b^2 = 8(ab)^2\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(ab = 6\\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n8a^2b^2 = 8 \\times 6^2 = 8 \\times 36 = 288\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(8a^2b^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{288}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\( x = 1 + \\frac{x}{1 + \\frac{x}{1 + \\frac{x}{1 + \\cdots}}} \\), we recognize that the expression is a continued fraction. We can set the entire continued fraction equal to \\( x \\), which gives us the equation:\n\n\\[\nx = 1 + \\frac{x}{x}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the right-hand side, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = 1 + \\frac{x}{x} = 1 + 1 = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
"Let's determine how much money Kim has. She can buy 40 oranges at \\(3x\\) cents each, so the total amount of money she has is:\n\n\\[ 40 \\times 3x = 120x \\text{ cents}. \\]\n\nIf the price of each orange rises to \\(4x\\) cents, we need to find out how many oranges she can buy with \\(120x\\) cents. Let \\(n\\) be the number of oranges she can buy at the new price. Then:\n\n\\[ n \\times 4x = 120x. \\]\n\nTo find \\(n\\), divide both sides of the equation by \\(4x\\):\n\n\\[ n = \\frac{120x}{4x} = \\frac{120}{4} = 30. \\]\n\nTherefore, Kim can buy \\(\\boxed{30}\\) oranges at the new price of \\(4x\\) cents each."
'To find the distance between the points \\((-5, 5)\\) and \\((5, -5)\\), we use the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given coordinates \\((-5, 5)\\) and \\((5, -5)\\) into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(5 - (-5))^2 + (-5 - 5)^2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying inside the parentheses:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(5 + 5)^2 + (-5 - 5)^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{10^2 + (-10)^2}\n\\]\n\nCalculating the squares:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{100 + 100}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{200}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying \\(\\sqrt{200}\\):\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{100 \\times 2} = \\sqrt{100} \\times \\sqrt{2} = 10\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the distance between the points is \\(\\boxed{10\\sqrt{2}}\\).'
'To factor the expression \\(36 - 4x^2\\) completely, we start by recognizing it as a difference of squares. The expression can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n36 - 4x^2 = (6)^2 - (2x)^2\n\\]\n\nThe difference of squares formula is given by:\n\n\\[\na^2 - b^2 = (a - b)(a + b)\n\\]\n\nApplying this formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n(6)^2 - (2x)^2 = (6 - 2x)(6 + 2x)\n\\]\n\nNext, we can factor out the greatest common factor from each binomial:\n\n\\[\n6 - 2x = 2(3 - x)\n\\]\n\\[\n6 + 2x = 2(3 + x)\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n(6 - 2x)(6 + 2x) = 2(3 - x) \\cdot 2(3 + x) = 4(3 - x)(3 + x)\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the completely factored form of \\(36 - 4x^2\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{4(3 - x)(3 + x)}\n\\]'

'To find \\( f^{-1}(c) \\), we start with the function \\( f(c) = \\frac{3}{2c-3} \\). We set \\( y = \\frac{3}{2c-3} \\) and solve for \\( c \\) in terms of \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{3}{2c-3}\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by \\( 2c-3 \\):\n\n\\[\ny(2c-3) = 3\n\\]\n\nDistribute \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n2yc - 3y = 3\n\\]\n\nAdd \\( 3y \\) to both sides:\n\n\\[\n2yc = 3 + 3y\n\\]\n\nDivide by \\( 2y \\):\n\n\\[\nc = \\frac{3 + 3y}{2y}\n\\]\n\nThus, the inverse function is:\n\n\\[\nf^{-1}(c) = \\frac{3 + 3c}{2c}\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to evaluate \\( f^{-1}(c) \\times c \\times f(c) \\):\n\n1. \\( f^{-1}(c) = \\frac{3 + 3c}{2c} \\)\n2. \\( f(c) = \\frac{3}{2c-3} \\)\n\nCalculate the product:\n\n\\[\nf^{-1}(c) \\times c \\times f(c) = \\left(\\frac{3 + 3c}{2c}\\right) \\times c \\times \\left(\\frac{3}{2c-3}\\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{3 + 3c}{2c} \\times \\frac{3c}{2c-3}\n\\]\n\nCancel \\( c \\) in the numerator and denominator:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{(3 + 3c) \\times 3}{2(2c-3)}\n\\]\n\nDistribute the 3:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{9 + 9c}{4c - 6}\n\\]\n\nThis fraction is already simplified. We compare it to the given form \\(\\frac{kc+l}{mc+n}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{9 + 9c}{4c - 6} = \\frac{kc + l}{mc + n}\n\\]\n\nFrom this, we identify:\n\n- \\( k = 9 \\)\n- \\( l = 9 \\)\n- \\( m = 4 \\)\n- \\( n = -6 \\)\n\nNow, calculate \\(\\frac{kn^2}{lm}\\):\n\n\\[\nkn^2 = 9 \\times (-6)^2 = 9 \\times 36 = 324\n\\]\n\n\\[\nlm = 9 \\times 4 = 36\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{kn^2}{lm} = \\frac{324}{36} = 9\n\\]\n\nThe value is \\(\\boxed{9}\\).'

'To solve for \\(2x - xy\\), we first need to find the values of \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) using the given equations:\n\n1. \\(x + y = 12\\)\n2. \\(x - y = 8\\)\n\nWe can solve these equations simultaneously. 'Let \\( r \\) be the number of rows and \\( s \\) be the number of seats per row in the original arrangement. We know that the total number of people is given by:\n\n\\[\nr \\times s = 450\n\\]\n\nIn the new arrangement, there are three fewer seats per row and five extra rows, so the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(r + 5)(s - 3) = 450\n\\]\n\nWe now have two equations:\n\n1. \\( rs = 450 \\)\n2. \\( (r + 5)(s - 3) = 450 \\)\n\nExpanding the second equation, we get:\n\n\\[\nrs - 3r + 5s - 15 = 450\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( rs = 450 \\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n450 - 3r + 5s - 15 = 450\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n-3r + 5s - 15 = 0\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\n5s = 3r + 15\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( s \\), we have:\n\n\\[\ns = \\frac{3r + 15}{5}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( s = \\frac{3r + 15}{5} \\) back into the first equation \\( rs = 450 \\):\n\n\\[\nr \\left(\\frac{3r + 15}{5}\\right) = 450\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by 5 to clear the fraction:\n\n\\[\nr(3r + 15) = 2250\n\\]\n\nExpanding gives:\n\n\\[\n3r^2 + 15r = 2250\n\\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 3:\n\n\\[\nr^2 + 5r = 750\n\\]\n\nRearrange to form a quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nr^2 + 5r - 750 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula \\( r = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 5 \\), and \\( c = -750 \\):\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{5^2 - 4 \\times 1 \\times (-750)}}{2 \\times 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 + 3000}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{3025}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{-5 \\pm 55}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives two possible solutions:\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{50}{2} = 25 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad r = \\frac{-60}{2} = -30\n\\]\n\nSince the number of rows cannot be negative, we have \\( r = 25 \\).\n\nThus, the auditorium has \\(\\boxed{25}\\) rows.'

'To solve the problem, we need to simplify each fraction by rationalizing the denominators and then combine them.\n\nFirst, consider the fraction \\(\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}}\\). To rationalize the denominator, multiply the numerator and the denominator by the conjugate of the denominator, \\(1 - 2\\sqrt{3}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2}{1 + 2\\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{1 - 2\\sqrt{3}}{1 - 2\\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{2(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}{(1 + 2\\sqrt{3})(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}\n\\]\n\nThe denominator simplifies using the difference of squares:\n\n\\[\n(1 + 2\\sqrt{3})(1 - 2\\sqrt{3}) = 1^2 - (2\\sqrt{3})^2 = 1 - 4 \\cdot 3 = 1 - 12 = -11\n\\]\n\nThus, the fraction becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2(1 - 2\\sqrt{3})}{-11} = \\frac{2 - 4\\sqrt{3}}{-11} = \\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nNext, consider the fraction \\(\\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}}\\). Again, rationalize the denominator by multiplying by the conjugate:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2 - \\sqrt{3}} \\cdot \\frac{2 + \\sqrt{3}}{2 + \\sqrt{3}} = \\frac{3(2 + \\sqrt{3})}{(2 - \\sqrt{3})(2 + \\sqrt{3})}\n\\]\n\nThe denominator simplifies as follows:\n\n\\[\n(2 - \\sqrt{3})(2 + \\sqrt{3}) = 2^2 - (\\sqrt{3})^2 = 4 - 3 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the fraction becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3(2 + \\sqrt{3})}{1} = 6 + 3\\sqrt{3}\n\\]\n\nNow, add the two simplified fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11} + (6 + 3\\sqrt{3})\n\\]\n\nTo combine these, express \\(6 + 3\\sqrt{3}\\) with a common denominator of 11:\n\n\\[\n6 + 3\\sqrt{3} = \\frac{66 + 33\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nAdd the fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3}}{11} + \\frac{66 + 33\\sqrt{3}}{11} = \\frac{-2 + 4\\sqrt{3} + 66 + 33\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{64 + 37\\sqrt{3}}{11}\n\\]\n\nThis is in the form \\(\\frac{A + B\\sqrt{3}}{C}\\) with \\(A = 64\\), \\(B = 37\\), and \\(C = 11\\). 'Given that the sum of two numbers \\( p \\) and \\( q \\) is equal to their product, we have the equation:\n\n\\[\np + q = pq\n\\]\n\nAdditionally, we are given that their difference is 7:\n\n\\[\np - q = 7\n\\]\n\nWe can solve these two equations simultaneously. First, solve for \\( p \\) and \\( q \\) using the system of equations:\n\n1. \\( p + q = pq \\)\n2. \\( p - q = 7 \\)\n\nAdd the two equations:\n\n\\[\n(p + q) + (p - q) = pq + 7\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2p = pq + 7\n\\]\n\nSubtract the second equation from the first:\n\n\\[\n(p + q) - (p - q) = pq - 7\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2q = pq - 7\n\\]\n\nNow, express \\( p \\) and \\( q \\) in terms of each other.
