'The car travels 45 feet in the first second, and each subsequent second it travels 5 feet less than the previous second. This forms an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a_1 = 45 \\) and the common difference \\( d = -5 \\).\n\nThe sequence of distances traveled each second is: 45, 40, 35, 30, ..., until the car stops.\n\nTo find the total distance traveled, we first need to determine the number of seconds it takes for the car to stop. The car stops when the distance traveled in a second becomes 0 or negative. We set up the equation for the \\( n \\)-th term of the sequence:\n\n\\[ a_n = a_1 + (n-1)d = 45 + (n-1)(-5) = 45 - 5(n-1) \\]\n\nSet \\( a_n = 0 \\) to find when the car stops:\n\n\\[ 0 = 45 - 5(n-1) \\]\n\\[ 5(n-1) = 45 \\]\n\\[ n-1 = 9 \\]\n\\[ n = 10 \\]\n\nThe car stops after 10 seconds. Now, we calculate the total distance traveled by summing the terms of the arithmetic sequence:\n\nThe sum \\( S_n \\) of the first \\( n \\) terms of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\n\\[ S_n = \\frac{n}{2} (a_1 + a_n) \\]\n\nSubstitute the known values:\n\n\\[ S_{10} = \\frac{10}{2} (45 + 0) = 5 \\times 45 = 225 \\]\n\nThus, the car travels a total of 225 feet from the time the brakes are applied to the time the car stops. The answer is \\(\\boxed{225}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to calculate the distance traveled by each horse and then determine how many revolutions the second horse needs to make to cover the same distance as the first horse.\n\n1. **Calculate the distance traveled by the first horse:**\n\n   The first horse is 64 feet from the center of the merry-go-round. The circumference of the circle it travels is given by the formula:\n   \\[\n   C = 2\\pi \\times \\text{radius} = 2\\pi \\times 64 = 128\\pi \\text{ feet}\n   \\]\n\n   The first horse makes 27 revolutions, so the total distance traveled is:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Distance} = 27 \\times 128\\pi = 3456\\pi \\text{ feet}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Calculate the number of revolutions for the second horse:**\n\n   The second horse is 16 feet from the center. The circumference of the circle it travels is:\n   \\[\n   C = 2\\pi \\times 16 = 32\\pi \\text{ feet}\n   \\]\n\n   Let \\( n \\) be the number of revolutions the second horse needs to make to travel the same distance as the first horse. We set up the equation:\n   \\[\n   n \\times 32\\pi = 3456\\pi\n   \\]\n\n   Solving for \\( n \\), we divide both sides by \\( 32\\pi \\):\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{3456\\pi}{32\\pi} = \\frac{3456}{32} = 108\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the second horse would need to make \\(\\boxed{108}\\) revolutions to travel the same distance as the first horse.'
"To find the value of \\( K \\) such that no pair of real numbers \\((x, y)\\) satisfies the system of equations:\n\n\\[\n6x + 4y = 7\n\\]\n\\[\nKx + 8y = 7\n\\]\n\nwe need to determine when the system of equations is inconsistent. This occurs when the lines represented by the equations are parallel but not coincident.\n\nFirst, let's write both equations in the form \\( y = mx + c \\) to find their slopes:\n\n1. For the first equation:\n   \\[\n   6x + 4y = 7 \\implies 4y = -6x + 7 \\implies y = -\\frac{3}{2}x + \\frac{7}{4}\n   \\]\n   The slope of the first line is \\( m_1 = -\\frac{3}{2} \\).\n\n2. For the second equation:\n   \\[\n   Kx + 8y = 7 \\implies 8y = -Kx + 7 \\implies y = -\\frac{K}{8}x + \\frac{7}{8}\n   \\]\n   The slope of the second line is \\( m_2 = -\\frac{K}{8} \\).\n\nFor the lines to be parallel, their slopes must be equal:\n\\[\n-\\frac{3}{2} = -\\frac{K}{8}\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( K \\), we multiply both sides by \\(-1\\) and then by 8:\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2} = \\frac{K}{8} \\implies K = 8 \\times \\frac{3}{2} = 12\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( K \\) that makes the system of equations inconsistent (parallel lines with different intercepts) is \\(\\boxed{12}\\)."
'To find the number of calories in a 12 fluid ounce bottle of Vitamin Water, we can set up a proportion based on the given information. We know that there are 125 calories in an 8 fluid ounce bottle. We want to find the number of calories, \\( x \\), in a 12 fluid ounce bottle.\n\nThe proportion is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{125 \\text{ calories}}{8 \\text{ fluid ounces}} = \\frac{x \\text{ calories}}{12 \\text{ fluid ounces}}\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( x \\), we cross-multiply:\n\n\\[\n125 \\times 12 = 8 \\times x\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1500 = 8x\n\\]\n\nNow, divide both sides by 8 to solve for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{1500}{8} = 187.5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, a 12 fluid ounce bottle of Vitamin Water contains 187.5 calories.'
'To simplify the expression \\(\\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}}}\\), we will work from the innermost radical outward.\n\n1. Start with the innermost expression: \\(x \\sqrt{x}\\).\n   - This can be rewritten as \\(x \\cdot x^{1/2} = x^{1 + 1/2} = x^{3/2}\\).\n\n2. Next, consider \\(\\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}} = \\root 3 \\of {x^{3/2}}\\).\n   - This is equivalent to \\((x^{3/2})^{1/3} = x^{(3/2) \\cdot (1/3)} = x^{1/2}\\).\n\n3. Now, consider the next layer: \\(x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}} = x \\cdot x^{1/2}\\).\n   - This simplifies to \\(x^{1 + 1/2} = x^{3/2}\\).\n\n4. Then, take the cube root: \\(\\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}} = \\root 3 \\of {x^{3/2}}\\).\n   - This is \\((x^{3/2})^{1/3} = x^{(3/2) \\cdot (1/3)} = x^{1/2}\\).\n\n5. Finally, consider the outermost expression: \\(x \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}} = x \\cdot x^{1/2}\\).\n   - This simplifies to \\(x^{1 + 1/2} = x^{3/2}\\).\n\n6. Take the cube root of the entire expression: \\(\\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\root 3 \\of {x \\sqrt{x}}}} = \\root 3 \\of {x^{3/2}}\\).\n   - This is \\((x^{3/2})^{1/3} = x^{(3/2) \\cdot (1/3)} = x^{1/2}\\).\n\nThus, the simplified form of the expression is \\(\\boxed{x^{1/2}}\\), which can also be written as \\(\\boxed{\\sqrt{x}}\\).'
"Let's denote the number of free hours each person gets as \\( f \\) and the cost per extra hour as \\( c \\) cents. \n\nFor Wells and Ted, the total hours used was 105, and their total cost was $10, which is 1000 cents. Since both used all their free hours, the total extra hours they used is \\( 105 - 2f \\). Therefore, the equation for Wells and Ted is:\n\n\\[\nc(105 - 2f) = 1000\n\\]\n\nFor Vino, who used 105 hours and paid $26 (or 2600 cents), the extra hours he used is \\( 105 - f \\). Therefore, the equation for Vino is:\n\n\\[\nc(105 - f) = 2600\n\\]\n\nNow, we have two equations:\n\n1. \\( c(105 - 2f) = 1000 \\)\n2. \\( c(105 - f) = 2600 \\)\n\nWe can solve these equations simultaneously. First, solve the second equation for \\( c \\):\n\n\\[\nc = \\frac{2600}{105 - f}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( c \\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2600}{105 - f}(105 - 2f) = 1000\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( f \\):\n\n\\[\n2600(105 - 2f) = 1000(105 - f)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n273000 - 5200f = 105000 - 1000f\n\\]\n\n\\[\n168000 = 4200f\n\\]\n\n\\[\nf = \\frac{168000}{4200} = 40\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\( f = 40 \\) back into the expression for \\( c \\):\n\n\\[\nc = \\frac{2600}{105 - 40} = \\frac{2600}{65} = 40\n\\]\n\nThus, the number of cents charged for each extra hour is \\(\\boxed{40}\\)."
'To find \\(\\frac{a}{d}\\), we can multiply the given fractions together:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} = \\frac{3}{5}, \\quad \\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{15}{6}, \\quad \\frac{c}{d} = 6\n\\]\n\nFirst, simplify \\(\\frac{b}{c}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{15}{6} = \\frac{5}{2}\n\\]\n\nNow, multiply the fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{d} = \\frac{a}{b} \\times \\frac{b}{c} \\times \\frac{c}{d} = \\frac{3}{5} \\times \\frac{5}{2} \\times 6\n\\]\n\nSimplify step by step:\n\n1. 'To find the constant \\( c \\) such that \\( x^2 + 25x + c \\) is the square of a binomial, we need to express it in the form \\( (x + a)^2 \\).\n\nExpanding \\( (x + a)^2 \\), we get:\n\\[\n(x + a)^2 = x^2 + 2ax + a^2\n\\]\n\nBy comparing coefficients with \\( x^2 + 25x + c \\), we have:\n- The coefficient of \\( x \\) gives us \\( 2a = 25 \\), so \\( a = \\frac{25}{2} \\).\n- The constant term gives us \\( a^2 = c \\).\n\nNow, we calculate \\( c \\):\n\\[\nc = a^2 = \\left(\\frac{25}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{625}{4}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( c \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{625}{4}}\\).'
'To find the shortest distance between the two circles, we first need to determine the distance between their centers and then subtract the sum of their radii.\n\nThe first circle is \\((x-9)^2 + (y-5)^2 = 6.25\\). The center of this circle is \\((9, 5)\\) and its radius is \\(\\sqrt{6.25} = 2.5\\).\n\nThe second circle is \\((x+6)^2 + (y+3)^2 = 49\\). The center of this circle is \\((-6, -3)\\) and its radius is \\(\\sqrt{49} = 7\\).\n\nNext, we calculate the distance between the centers of the two circles. The distance \\(d\\) between two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coordinates of the centers, we have:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{((-6) - 9)^2 + ((-3) - 5)^2} = \\sqrt{(-15)^2 + (-8)^2} = \\sqrt{225 + 64} = \\sqrt{289} = 17\n\\]\n\nThe shortest distance between the two circles is the distance between their centers minus the sum of their radii:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Shortest distance} = 17 - (2.5 + 7) = 17 - 9.5 = 7.5\n\\]\n\nThus, the shortest distance between the two circles is \\(\\boxed{7.5}\\) units.'

'To find \\( x^3 - y^3 \\), we can use the identity for the difference of cubes:\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2)\n\\]\n\nWe are given that \\( x-y = 1 \\). Therefore, we need to find \\( x^2 + xy + y^2 \\).\n\nWe are also given that \\( x^2 + y^2 = 7 \\).\n\nTo find \\( xy \\), we can use the identity:\n\n\\[\n(x-y)^2 = x^2 - 2xy + y^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\n\\[\n1^2 = x^2 - 2xy + y^2\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1 = 7 - 2xy\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( xy \\):\n\n\\[\n2xy = 7 - 1 = 6\n\\]\n\n\\[\nxy = 3\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x^2 + y^2 = 7 \\) and \\( xy = 3 \\) into the expression for \\( x^2 + xy + y^2 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + xy + y^2 = x^2 + y^2 + xy = 7 + 3 = 10\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute back into the expression for \\( x^3 - y^3 \\):\n\n\\[\nx^3 - y^3 = (x-y)(x^2 + xy + y^2) = 1 \\cdot 10 = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^3 - y^3 \\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
"To solve the equation \\( x \\cdot \\lfloor x \\rfloor = 27 \\) where \\( x \\) is positive, we need to find a positive \\( x \\) such that when multiplied by its floor value, the result is 27.\n\nLet's denote \\( \\lfloor x \\rfloor = n \\), where \\( n \\) is an integer. Then, we have:\n\\[ x \\cdot n = 27 \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{27}{n} \\]\n\nSince \\( n = \\lfloor x \\rfloor \\), it follows that:\n\\[ n \\leq x < n+1 \\]\n\nSubstituting \\( x = \\frac{27}{n} \\) into the inequality:\n\\[ n \\leq \\frac{27}{n} < n+1 \\]\n\nWe need to find integer values of \\( n \\) that satisfy this inequality.\n\n1. \\( n \\leq \\frac{27}{n} \\) implies:\n   \\[ n^2 \\leq 27 \\]\n   \\[ n \\leq \\sqrt{27} \\approx 5.196 \\]\n   So, \\( n \\) can be at most 5.\n\n2. \\( \\frac{27}{n} < n+1 \\) implies:\n   \\[ 27 < n(n+1) \\]\n   \\[ 27 < n^2 + n \\]\n\nLet's check integer values of \\( n \\) from 1 to 5:\n\n- For \\( n = 1 \\):\n  \\[ 27 < 1 \\cdot 2 = 2 \\] (False)\n\n- For \\( n = 2 \\):\n  \\[ 27 < 2 \\cdot 3 = 6 \\] (False)\n\n- For \\( n = 3 \\):\n  \\[ 27 < 3 \\cdot 4 = 12 \\] (False)\n\n- For \\( n = 4 \\):\n  \\[ 27 < 4 \\cdot 5 = 20 \\] (False)\n\n- For \\( n = 5 \\):\n  \\[ 27 < 5 \\cdot 6 = 30 \\] (True)\n\nThus, \\( n = 5 \\) is the only integer that satisfies both conditions. Therefore, \\( x = \\frac{27}{5} = 5.4 \\).\n\nThe value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{5.4}\\)."
'To find the least possible value of the sum \\( |x - 1| + |x - 1.5| + |x - 2| \\), we need to consider the behavior of the expression as \\( x \\) varies. The expression consists of three absolute value terms, each of which changes behavior at its respective point: 1, 1.5, and 2. \n\nThe critical points where the behavior of the absolute values changes are \\( x = 1 \\), \\( x = 1.5 \\), and \\( x = 2 \\). We will evaluate the sum at these points and in the intervals between them to find the minimum value.\n\n1. **Interval \\( x < 1 \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = 1 - x, \\quad |x - 1.5| = 1.5 - x, \\quad |x - 2| = 2 - x\n   \\]\n\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (1 - x) + (1.5 - x) + (2 - x) = 4.5 - 3x\n   \\]\n\n2. **Interval \\( 1 \\leq x < 1.5 \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = x - 1, \\quad |x - 1.5| = 1.5 - x, \\quad |x - 2| = 2 - x\n   \\]\n\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (x - 1) + (1.5 - x) + (2 - x) = 2.5 - x\n   \\]\n\n3. **Interval \\( 1.5 \\leq x < 2 \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = x - 1, \\quad |x - 1.5| = x - 1.5, \\quad |x - 2| = 2 - x\n   \\]\n\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (x - 1) + (x - 1.5) + (2 - x) = x - 1 + x - 1.5 + 2 - x = x - 1.5\n   \\]\n\n4. **Interval \\( x \\geq 2 \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   |x - 1| = x - 1, \\quad |x - 1.5| = x - 1.5, \\quad |x - 2| = x - 2\n   \\]\n\n   The sum is:\n   \\[\n   (x - 1) + (x - 1.5) + (x - 2) = 3x - 4.5\n   \\]\n\nNow, we evaluate the sum at the critical points:\n\n- At \\( x = 1 \\):\n  \\[\n  |1 - 1| + |1 - 1.5| + |1 - 2| = 0 + 0.5 + 1 = 1.5\n  \\]\n\n- At \\( x = 1.5 \\):\n  \\[\n  |1.5 - 1| + |1.5 - 1.5| + |1.5 - 2| = 0.5 + 0 + 0.5 = 1\n  \\]\n\n- At \\( x = 2 \\):\n  \\[\n  |2 - 1| + |2 - 1.5| + |2 - 2| = 1 + 0.5 + 0 = 1.5\n  \\]\n\nThe minimum value of the sum occurs at \\( x = 1.5 \\) and is \\( \\boxed{1} \\).'

Then Josh's rate was \\( \\frac{4}{5}r \\).\n\nThe distance Josh traveled is given by:\n\\[\n\\text{Distance Josh traveled} = \\left(\\frac{4}{5}r\\right)(2t) = \\frac{8}{5}rt\n\\]\n\nThe distance Mike traveled is:\n\\[\n\\text{Distance Mike traveled} = rt\n\\]\n\nSince they met after traveling a total of 13 miles, we have:\n\\[\n\\frac{8}{5}rt + rt = 13\n\\]\n\nCombine the terms:\n\\[\n\\frac{8}{5}rt + \\frac{5}{5}rt = \\frac{13}{5}rt = 13\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\( rt \\):\n\\[\n\\frac{13}{5}rt = 13 \\implies rt = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, Mike traveled 5 miles when they met. 'Given that \\( g(x) = f^{-1}(x) \\), this means that \\( g \\) is the inverse function of \\( f \\). Therefore, for any \\( x \\), we have:\n\n\\[ g(f(x)) = x \\quad \\text{and} \\quad f(g(x)) = x. \\]\n\nWe are given the values:\n\n- \\( g(-15) = 0 \\)\n- \\( g(0) = 3 \\)\n- \\( g(3) = 9 \\)\n- \\( g(9) = 20 \\)\n\nWe need to find \\( f(f(9)) \\).\n\nFrom \\( g(3) = 9 \\), we know that \\( f(9) = 3 \\) because \\( g \\) is the inverse of \\( f \\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\( f(f(9)) = f(3) \\).\n\nFrom \\( g(0) = 3 \\), we know that \\( f(3) = 0 \\).\n\nTherefore, \\( f(f(9)) = f(3) = 0 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(f(9)) \\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
'To expand the product \\((x-2)^2(x+2)^2\\), we can first expand each binomial squared and then multiply the results.\n\nFirst, expand \\((x-2)^2\\):\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 = (x-2)(x-2) = x^2 - 2x - 2x + 4 = x^2 - 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nNext, expand \\((x+2)^2\\):\n\\[\n(x+2)^2 = (x+2)(x+2) = x^2 + 2x + 2x + 4 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nNow, multiply the two results:\n\\[\n(x^2 - 4x + 4)(x^2 + 4x + 4)\n\\]\n\nWe will use the distributive property (FOIL method) to expand this product:\n\\[\n= x^2(x^2 + 4x + 4) - 4x(x^2 + 4x + 4) + 4(x^2 + 4x + 4)\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\\[\nx^2(x^2 + 4x + 4) = x^4 + 4x^3 + 4x^2\n\\]\n\\[\n-4x(x^2 + 4x + 4) = -4x^3 - 16x^2 - 16x\n\\]\n\\[\n4(x^2 + 4x + 4) = 4x^2 + 16x + 16\n\\]\n\nCombine all terms:\n\\[\nx^4 + 4x^3 + 4x^2 - 4x^3 - 16x^2 - 16x + 4x^2 + 16x + 16\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\\[\nx^4 + (4x^3 - 4x^3) + (4x^2 - 16x^2 + 4x^2) + (-16x + 16x) + 16\n\\]\n\\[\n= x^4 + 0x^3 - 8x^2 + 0x + 16\n\\]\n\\[\n= x^4 - 8x^2 + 16\n\\]\n\nThe nonzero coefficients of the resulting expression are \\(1\\), \\(-8\\), and \\(16\\). The product of these coefficients is:\n\\[\n1 \\times (-8) \\times 16 = -128\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the nonzero coefficients is \\(\\boxed{-128}\\).'
'Let the three consecutive positive even numbers be \\( x-2 \\), \\( x \\), and \\( x+2 \\). The sum of their squares is given by:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 + x^2 + (x+2)^2 = 12296\n\\]\n\nExpanding each square, we have:\n\n\\[\n(x-2)^2 = x^2 - 4x + 4\n\\]\n\\[\nx^2 = x^2\n\\]\n\\[\n(x+2)^2 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nAdding these expressions together:\n\n\\[\n(x^2 - 4x + 4) + x^2 + (x^2 + 4x + 4) = 12296\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the left side:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 + 8 = 12296\n\\]\n\nSubtract 8 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n3x^2 = 12288\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 3:\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 4096\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides:\n\n\\[\nx = 64\n\\]\n\nThus, the three consecutive even numbers are \\( 62 \\), \\( 64 \\), and \\( 66 \\).\n\nNow, we find the product of these numbers:\n\n\\[\n62 \\times 64 \\times 66\n\\]\n\nTo simplify the calculation, notice that:\n\n\\[\n62 \\times 66 = (64-2)(64+2) = 64^2 - 2^2 = 4096 - 4 = 4092\n\\]\n\nNow multiply by 64:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 64\n\\]\n\nBreaking it down:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 64 = (4092 \\times 60) + (4092 \\times 4)\n\\]\n\nCalculate each part:\n\n\\[\n4092 \\times 60 = 245520\n\\]\n\\[\n4092 \\times 4 = 16368\n\\]\n\nAdding these results:\n\n\\[\n245520 + 16368 = 261888\n\\]\n\nFinally, divide by 8:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{261888}{8} = 32736\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the three numbers divided by 8 is \\(\\boxed{32736}\\).'
'To find the number of positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which the sum \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 \\) is less than 20, we start by setting up the inequality:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 < 20\n\\]\n\nSubtract 20 from both sides to simplify:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 - 20 < 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x - 16 < 0\n\\]\n\nNext, we solve the quadratic equation \\( x^2 + 4x - 16 = 0 \\) to find the critical points. We use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 4 \\), and \\( c = -16 \\). Plugging in these values, we get:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{4^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-16)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 64}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{80}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 \\cdot 5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-4 \\pm 4\\sqrt{5}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = -2 \\pm 2\\sqrt{5}\n\\]\n\nThe roots are \\( x = -2 + 2\\sqrt{5} \\) and \\( x = -2 - 2\\sqrt{5} \\). Since we are interested in positive integer values of \\( x \\), we consider the interval between these roots where the quadratic is negative. The approximate value of \\( \\sqrt{5} \\) is about 2.236, so:\n\n\\[\nx = -2 + 2 \\times 2.236 \\approx -2 + 4.472 \\approx 2.472\n\\]\n\nSince we are looking for positive integer values of \\( x \\), we test integers less than 2.472, which are 1 and 2.\n\n- For \\( x = 1 \\):\n  \\[\n  x^2 + 4x + 4 = 1^2 + 4 \\times 1 + 4 = 1 + 4 + 4 = 9\n  \\]\n  \\( 9 < 20 \\), so \\( x = 1 \\) is valid.\n\n- For \\( x = 2 \\):\n  \\[\n  x^2 + 4x + 4 = 2^2 + 4 \\times 2 + 4 = 4 + 8 + 4 = 16\n  \\]\n  \\( 16 < 20 \\), so \\( x = 2 \\) is valid.\n\nThus, there are \\(\\boxed{2}\\) positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which the sum \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 \\) is less than 20.'
'We can use the difference of squares formula to evaluate \\(255^2 - 245^2\\). The difference of squares formula states:\n\n\\[\na^2 - b^2 = (a - b)(a + b)\n\\]\n\nIn this case, \\(a = 255\\) and \\(b = 245\\). First, subtract the first equation from the second:\n\n\\[\n(729x + 731y) - (725x + 727y) = 1508 - 1500\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\n4x + 4y = 8\n\\]\n\nDividing the entire equation by 4:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 2\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to express \\( x - y \\) in terms of \\( x + y \\). 'To evaluate the operation \\(\\frac{7}{30} @ \\frac{10}{21}\\), we use the definition of the operation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{m}{n} @ \\frac{p}{q} = (m)(p)\\left(\\frac{q}{n}\\right)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given fractions into the operation, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{30} @ \\frac{10}{21} = (7)(10)\\left(\\frac{21}{30}\\right)\n\\]\n\nFirst, calculate the product of the numerators:\n\n\\[\n7 \\times 10 = 70\n\\]\n\nNext, simplify the fraction \\(\\frac{21}{30}\\):\n\nThe greatest common divisor (GCD) of 21 and 30 is 3. 'To evaluate \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{5}} 125\\sqrt{5}\\), we start by expressing everything in terms of powers of 5.\n\nFirst, note that:\n\\[\n\\sqrt{5} = 5^{1/2}\n\\]\n\nWe want to express \\(125\\sqrt{5}\\) in terms of powers of 5. 'In an arithmetic sequence, the terms can be expressed as \\( a_n = a_1 + (n-1)d \\), where \\( a_1 \\) is the first term and \\( d \\) is the common difference.\n\nGiven that \\( \\frac{a_4}{a_2} = 3 \\), we can express \\( a_4 \\) and \\( a_2 \\) in terms of \\( a_1 \\) and \\( d \\):\n\n\\[\na_4 = a_1 + 3d\n\\]\n\\[\na_2 = a_1 + d\n\\]\n\nSubstituting these into the given ratio:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a_4}{a_2} = \\frac{a_1 + 3d}{a_1 + d} = 3\n\\]\n\nCross-multiplying gives:\n\n\\[\na_1 + 3d = 3(a_1 + d)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\n\\[\na_1 + 3d = 3a_1 + 3d\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\( 3d \\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\na_1 = 3a_1\n\\]\n\nSubtracting \\( a_1 \\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n0 = 2a_1\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( a_1 = 0 \\).\n\nNow, we need to find \\( \\frac{a_5}{a_3} \\). Express \\( a_5 \\) and \\( a_3 \\) in terms of \\( a_1 \\) and \\( d \\):\n\n\\[\na_5 = a_1 + 4d = 0 + 4d = 4d\n\\]\n\\[\na_3 = a_1 + 2d = 0 + 2d = 2d\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate the ratio:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a_5}{a_3} = \\frac{4d}{2d} = 2\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( \\frac{a_5}{a_3} \\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'The function \\( f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\) is an exponential function with base \\(\\frac{3}{7}\\), which is a positive number less than 1. The domain of the function is given as \\([0, \\infty)\\).\n\nTo find the range of \\( f(x) \\), we analyze the behavior of the function as \\( x \\) varies over its domain:\n\n1. **At \\( x = 0 \\):** \n   \\[\n   f(0) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^0 = 1\n   \\]\n\n2. **As \\( x \\to \\infty \\):**\n   Since the base \\(\\frac{3}{7}\\) is less than 1, raising it to larger and larger powers will make the value of the function approach 0. Thus, \n   \\[\n   \\lim_{x \\to \\infty} \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x = 0\n   \\]\n\n3. **For \\( x > 0 \\):**\n   The function \\( f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\) will take on values between 0 and 1, since \\(\\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x\\) is always positive and decreases as \\( x \\) increases.\n\nTherefore, the range of the function \\( f(x) = \\left(\\frac{3}{7}\\right)^x \\) is \\((0, 1]\\). The function can take any value greater than 0 and up to 1, but never actually reaches 0.\n\nThus, the range of the function is \\(\\boxed{(0, 1]}\\).'
"To find the sum of the areas of all the circles, we first need to determine the area of each circle and then sum them up. The diameters of the circles are given as 16 inches, 8 inches, 4 inches, and so on, with each diameter being half of the previous one. \n\nThe radius of each circle is half of its diameter. Therefore, the radii of the circles are 8 inches, 4 inches, 2 inches, and so on. The area \\( A \\) of a circle is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi r^2\n\\]\n\nFor the first circle with a radius of 8 inches, the area is:\n\n\\[\nA_1 = \\pi \\times 8^2 = 64\\pi\n\\]\n\nFor the second circle with a radius of 4 inches, the area is:\n\n\\[\nA_2 = \\pi \\times 4^2 = 16\\pi\n\\]\n\nFor the third circle with a radius of 2 inches, the area is:\n\n\\[\nA_3 = \\pi \\times 2^2 = 4\\pi\n\\]\n\nThis pattern continues, with each subsequent circle having an area that is one-fourth of the previous circle's area. Therefore, the areas form a geometric series:\n\n\\[\nA_1 + A_2 + A_3 + \\cdots = 64\\pi + 16\\pi + 4\\pi + \\cdots\n\\]\n\nThis is a geometric series with the first term \\( a = 64\\pi \\) and a common ratio \\( r = \\frac{1}{4} \\).\n\nThe sum \\( S \\) of an infinite geometric series is given by:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{a}{1 - r}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values, we get:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{64\\pi}{1 - \\frac{1}{4}} = \\frac{64\\pi}{\\frac{3}{4}} = \\frac{64\\pi \\times 4}{3} = \\frac{256\\pi}{3}\n\\]\n\nTo express this sum to the nearest whole number, we approximate \\(\\pi\\) as 3.14159:\n\n\\[\nS \\approx \\frac{256 \\times 3.14159}{3} \\approx \\frac{804.24704}{3} \\approx 268.08235\n\\]\n\nRounding to the nearest whole number, the sum of the areas of all the circles is approximately \\(\\boxed{268}\\) square inches."
'To find the difference between the sum of the first 2003 even counting numbers and the sum of the first 2003 odd counting numbers, we start by calculating each sum separately.\n\nThe first 2003 even counting numbers are:  \n\\[ 2, 4, 6, \\ldots, 2 \\times 2003 = 4006. \\]\n\nThe sum of the first \\( n \\) even numbers is given by the formula:  \n\\[ S_{\\text{even}} = 2 + 4 + 6 + \\cdots + 2n = 2(1 + 2 + 3 + \\cdots + n) = 2 \\cdot \\frac{n(n+1)}{2} = n(n+1). \\]\n\nFor \\( n = 2003 \\), the sum of the first 2003 even numbers is:  \n\\[ S_{\\text{even}} = 2003 \\times 2004. \\]\n\nThe first 2003 odd counting numbers are:  \n\\[ 1, 3, 5, \\ldots, 2 \\times 2003 - 1 = 4005. \\]\n\nThe sum of the first \\( n \\) odd numbers is given by the formula:  \n\\[ S_{\\text{odd}} = 1 + 3 + 5 + \\cdots + (2n-1) = n^2. \\]\n\nFor \\( n = 2003 \\), the sum of the first 2003 odd numbers is:  \n\\[ S_{\\text{odd}} = 2003^2. \\]\n\nNow, we find the difference between these two sums:  \n\\[ \\text{Difference} = S_{\\text{even}} - S_{\\text{odd}} = 2003 \\times 2004 - 2003^2. \\]\n\nWe can factor out \\( 2003 \\) from both terms:  \n\\[ \\text{Difference} = 2003 \\times (2004 - 2003) = 2003 \\times 1 = 2003. \\]\n\nThus, the difference between the sum of the first 2003 even counting numbers and the sum of the first 2003 odd counting numbers is \\(\\boxed{2003}\\).'
'To evaluate \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8})\\), we start by expressing everything in terms of powers of 2.\n\nFirst, note that \\(\\sqrt{8} = 8^{1/2} = (2^3)^{1/2} = 2^{3/2}\\).\n\nNext, express \\(64\\sqrt{8}\\) in terms of powers of 2:\n\\[\n64 = 2^6 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad \\sqrt{8} = 2^{3/2}.\n\\]\nThus,\n\\[\n64\\sqrt{8} = 2^6 \\cdot 2^{3/2} = 2^{6 + 3/2} = 2^{12/2 + 3/2} = 2^{15/2}.\n\\]\n\nNow, we have:\n\\[\n\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8}) = \\log_{2^{3/2}}(2^{15/2}).\n\\]\n\nUsing the change of base formula for logarithms, \\(\\log_b(a^c) = \\frac{c}{\\log_b(b)}\\), we get:\n\\[\n\\log_{2^{3/2}}(2^{15/2}) = \\frac{15/2}{3/2} = \\frac{15}{3} = 5.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\log_{\\sqrt{8}}(64\\sqrt{8})\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
'If \\( c \\) and \\( d \\) are inversely proportional, then their product is constant. This means we can write the relationship as:\n\n\\[ c \\cdot d = k \\]\n\nwhere \\( k \\) is a constant. Given that \\( c = 9 \\) when \\( d = 8 \\), we can find \\( k \\) as follows:\n\n\\[ 9 \\cdot 8 = k \\]\n\\[ k = 72 \\]\n\nNow, we need to find the value of \\( d \\) when \\( c = 6 \\). "In an arithmetic sequence, the difference between consecutive terms is constant. "Heisenberg's Uncertainty Principle is given by the inequality:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta p \\cdot \\Delta x \\geq \\frac{h}{4\\pi}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(\\Delta p\\) is the error in the measurement of momentum, \\(\\Delta x\\) is the error in the measurement of position, and \\(h\\) is Planck's constant.\n\nInitially, let's assume the errors are \\(\\Delta p_0\\) and \\(\\Delta x_0\\) such that:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta p_0 \\cdot \\Delta x_0 = \\frac{h}{4\\pi}\n\\]\n\nNow, if the error in the measurement of momentum is halved, the new error in momentum is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta p = \\frac{\\Delta p_0}{2}\n\\]\n\nTo maintain the equality in the uncertainty principle, the new error in position \\(\\Delta x\\) must satisfy:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\Delta p_0}{2} \\cdot \\Delta x = \\frac{h}{4\\pi}\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(\\Delta x\\), we get:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta x = \\frac{h}{4\\pi} \\cdot \\frac{2}{\\Delta p_0} = 2 \\Delta x_0\n\\]\n\nThus, the new error in the measurement of position is twice the original error. The increase in the error of position is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta x - \\Delta x_0 = 2\\Delta x_0 - \\Delta x_0 = \\Delta x_0\n\\]\n\nThe percentage increase in the error of position is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\Delta x_0}{\\Delta x_0} \\times 100\\% = 100\\%\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the minimum error in the measurement of its position increases by \\(\\boxed{100\\%}\\)."
'To solve for the integer values of \\( x \\) such that \\(|x^2 - 16|\\) is a prime number, we need to consider two cases: \\( x^2 - 16 = p \\) and \\( 16 - x^2 = p \\), where \\( p \\) is a prime number.\n\n**Case 1:** \\( x^2 - 16 = p \\)\n\nHere, \\( x^2 = p + 16 \\). Since \\( p \\) is a prime number, we need to check small values of \\( p \\) to see if \\( x^2 \\) becomes a perfect square.\n\n- If \\( p = 2 \\), then \\( x^2 = 18 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 3 \\), then \\( x^2 = 19 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 5 \\), then \\( x^2 = 21 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 7 \\), then \\( x^2 = 23 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 11 \\), then \\( x^2 = 27 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 13 \\), then \\( x^2 = 29 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n\nNone of these values work, so we move to the next case.\n\n**Case 2:** \\( 16 - x^2 = p \\)\n\nHere, \\( x^2 = 16 - p \\). Again, \\( p \\) is a prime number, so we check small values of \\( p \\).\n\n- If \\( p = 2 \\), then \\( x^2 = 14 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 3 \\), then \\( x^2 = 13 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 5 \\), then \\( x^2 = 11 \\), which is not a perfect square.\n- If \\( p = 7 \\), then \\( x^2 = 9 \\), which is a perfect square. Thus, \\( x = \\pm 3 \\).\n\nThe integer values of \\( x \\) for which \\(|x^2 - 16|\\) is a prime number are \\( x = 3 \\) and \\( x = -3 \\).\n\nThe product of these integer values is:\n\\[\n3 \\times (-3) = -9\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the two integer values for \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{-9}\\).'
'To find \\( f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) \\), we first need to determine the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) of \\( f(x) = \\frac{2}{x+1} \\).\n\n1. Start by setting \\( y = f(x) = \\frac{2}{x+1} \\).\n2. Solve for \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\):\n   \\[\n   y = \\frac{2}{x+1}\n   \\]\n   Multiply both sides by \\( x+1 \\):\n   \\[\n   y(x+1) = 2\n   \\]\n   Expand and rearrange:\n   \\[\n   yx + y = 2\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   yx = 2 - y\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{2 - y}{y}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the inverse function is \\( f^{-1}(y) = \\frac{2-y}{y} \\).\n\nNow, evaluate \\( f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) \\):\n\\[\nf^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) = \\frac{2 - \\frac{1}{5}}{\\frac{1}{5}}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n\\[\n= \\frac{\\frac{10}{5} - \\frac{1}{5}}{\\frac{1}{5}}\n\\]\n\\[\n= \\frac{\\frac{9}{5}}{\\frac{1}{5}}\n\\]\n\\[\n= \\frac{9}{5} \\times \\frac{5}{1}\n\\]\n\\[\n= 9\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( f^{-1}\\left(\\frac{1}{5}\\right) \\) is \\(\\boxed{9}\\).'
'To find the distance between the vertex of the parabola given by the equation \\( y = x^2 + 2x - 6 \\) and the point \\( (4, 5) \\), we first need to determine the vertex of the parabola.\n\nThe equation of the parabola is in the form \\( y = ax^2 + bx + c \\), where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 2 \\), and \\( c = -6 \\). The x-coordinate of the vertex of a parabola in this form is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{b}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{2}{2 \\times 1} = -1\n\\]\n\nNow, we substitute \\( x = -1 \\) back into the equation to find the y-coordinate of the vertex:\n\n\\[\ny = (-1)^2 + 2(-1) - 6 = 1 - 2 - 6 = -7\n\\]\n\nThus, the vertex of the parabola is at the point \\( (-1, -7) \\).\n\nNext, we calculate the distance between the vertex \\( (-1, -7) \\) and the point \\( (4, 5) \\) using the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coordinates \\( (x_1, y_1) = (-1, -7) \\) and \\( (x_2, y_2) = (4, 5) \\):\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(4 - (-1))^2 + (5 - (-7))^2}\n\\]\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(4 + 1)^2 + (5 + 7)^2}\n\\]\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{5^2 + 12^2}\n\\]\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{25 + 144}\n\\]\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{169}\n\\]\n\\[\nd = 13\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the distance between the vertex of the parabola and the point \\( (4, 5) \\) is \\(\\boxed{13}\\).'
'To simplify the expression \\(7a^3(3a^2 - a) - 8a(2a - 4)\\), we need to distribute and combine like terms.\n\nFirst, distribute in the first term:\n\\[\n7a^3(3a^2 - a) = 7a^3 \\cdot 3a^2 - 7a^3 \\cdot a = 21a^5 - 7a^4\n\\]\n\nNext, distribute in the second term:\n\\[\n-8a(2a - 4) = -8a \\cdot 2a + 8a \\cdot 4 = -16a^2 + 32a\n\\]\n\nNow, combine all the terms:\n\\[\n21a^5 - 7a^4 - 16a^2 + 32a\n\\]\n\nThere are no like terms to combine further, so the simplified expression is:\n\\[\n21a^5 - 7a^4 - 16a^2 + 32a\n\\]'
'To find the product of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), we first need to solve the system of equations:\n\n1. \\( 2x - 3y = 8 \\)\n2. \\( 4x + 3y = -2 \\)\n\nWe can add these two equations to eliminate \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n(2x - 3y) + (4x + 3y) = 8 + (-2)\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n6x = 6\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by 6 gives:\n\n\\[\nx = 1\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = 1 \\) back into the first equation to solve for \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n2(1) - 3y = 8\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2 - 3y = 8\n\\]\n\nSubtract 2 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n-3y = 6\n\\]\n\nDivide by -3:\n\n\\[\ny = -2\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\( x = 1 \\) and \\( y = -2 \\), the product \\( xy \\) is:\n\n\\[\nxy = 1 \\times (-2) = -2\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\) is \\(\\boxed{-2}\\).'
'Let the two numbers be \\( x \\) and \\( y \\). We are given the equations:\n\n\\[ x + y = 12 \\]\n\\[ xy = 35 \\]\n\nWe need to find the positive difference between the numbers, which is \\( |x - y| \\).\n\nTo solve for \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), we can use the identity:\n\n\\[ (x - y)^2 = (x + y)^2 - 4xy \\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\n\\[ (x - y)^2 = 12^2 - 4 \\times 35 \\]\n\\[ (x - y)^2 = 144 - 140 \\]\n\\[ (x - y)^2 = 4 \\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we get:\n\n\\[ |x - y| = \\sqrt{4} = 2 \\]\n\nThus, the positive difference between the numbers is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'To find the positive difference between the sum of the first 20 positive multiples of 5 and the sum of the first 20 positive even integers, we need to calculate each sum separately and then find their difference.\n\n**Step 1: Sum of the first 20 positive multiples of 5**\n\nThe first 20 positive multiples of 5 are: 5, 10, 15, ..., 100. This is an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a = 5 \\) and the common difference \\( d = 5 \\).\n\nThe formula for the sum of the first \\( n \\) terms of an arithmetic sequence is:\n\n\\[\nS_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (2a + (n-1)d)\n\\]\n\nFor the first 20 multiples of 5:\n\n\\[\nS_{20} = \\frac{20}{2} \\times (2 \\times 5 + (20-1) \\times 5)\n\\]\n\n\\[\nS_{20} = 10 \\times (10 + 95) = 10 \\times 105 = 1050\n\\]\n\n**Step 2: Sum of the first 20 positive even integers**\n\nThe first 20 positive even integers are: 2, 4, 6, ..., 40. This is also an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a = 2 \\) and the common difference \\( d = 2 \\).\n\nUsing the same formula for the sum:\n\n\\[\nS_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (2a + (n-1)d)\n\\]\n\nFor the first 20 even integers:\n\n\\[\nS_{20} = \\frac{20}{2} \\times (2 \\times 2 + (20-1) \\times 2)\n\\]\n\n\\[\nS_{20} = 10 \\times (4 + 38) = 10 \\times 42 = 420\n\\]\n\n**Step 3: Calculate the positive difference**\n\nThe positive difference between the two sums is:\n\n\\[\n|1050 - 420| = 630\n\\]\n\nThus, the positive difference between the sum of the first 20 positive multiples of 5 and the sum of the first 20 positive even integers is \\(\\boxed{630}\\).'
'To solve the quadratic equation \\(x^2 - 8x - 49 = 0\\) by completing the square, we first focus on the quadratic and linear terms: \\(x^2 - 8x\\).\n\n1. **Complete the square:**\n\n   The coefficient of \\(x\\) is \\(-8\\). To complete the square, we take half of \\(-8\\), which is \\(-4\\), and then square it to get \\(16\\).\n\n2. **Rewrite the quadratic expression:**\n\n   \\[\n   x^2 - 8x = (x - 4)^2 - 16\n   \\]\n\n   Here, \\((x - 4)^2\\) is the completed square, and we subtract \\(16\\) to balance the equation.\n\n3. **Substitute back into the original equation:**\n\n   \\[\n   (x - 4)^2 - 16 - 49 = 0\n   \\]\n\n   Simplify the constant terms:\n\n   \\[\n   (x - 4)^2 - 65 = 0\n   \\]\n\n4. **Rewrite in the form \\((ax + b)^2 + c\\):**\n\n   Comparing \\((x - 4)^2 - 65\\) with \\((ax + b)^2 + c\\), we identify:\n\n   - \\(a = 1\\)\n   - \\(b = -4\\)\n   - \\(c = -65\\)\n\n5. **Calculate \\(ab\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   ab = 1 \\times (-4) = -4\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(ab\\) is \\(\\boxed{-4}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to evaluate the function \\( f(x) \\) for each given value and then sum the results.\n\n1. **Evaluate \\( f(\\sqrt[3]{-8}) \\):**\n\n   \\(\\sqrt[3]{-8} = -2\\), which is a rational number. Therefore, we use the first case of the function: \n   \\[\n   f(x) = |\\lfloor x \\rfloor|\n   \\]\n   Since \\(\\lfloor -2 \\rfloor = -2\\), we have:\n   \\[\n   f(\\sqrt[3]{-8}) = |-2| = 2\n   \\]\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(-\\pi) \\):**\n\n   \\(-\\pi\\) is an irrational number. Therefore, we use the second case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(x) = \\lceil x \\rceil^2\n   \\]\n   Since \\(\\lceil -\\pi \\rceil = -3\\), we have:\n   \\[\n   f(-\\pi) = (-3)^2 = 9\n   \\]\n\n3. **Evaluate \\( f(\\sqrt{50}) \\):**\n\n   \\(\\sqrt{50}\\) is an irrational number. Therefore, we use the second case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(x) = \\lceil x \\rceil^2\n   \\]\n   Since \\(\\sqrt{50} \\approx 7.07\\), we have \\(\\lceil \\sqrt{50} \\rceil = 8\\). Thus:\n   \\[\n   f(\\sqrt{50}) = 8^2 = 64\n   \\]\n\n4. **Evaluate \\( f\\left(\\frac{9}{2}\\right) \\):**\n\n   \\(\\frac{9}{2} = 4.5\\), which is a rational number. Therefore, we use the first case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(x) = |\\lfloor x \\rfloor|\n   \\]\n   Since \\(\\lfloor 4.5 \\rfloor = 4\\), we have:\n   \\[\n   f\\left(\\frac{9}{2}\\right) = |4| = 4\n   \\]\n\nFinally, we sum the results:\n\\[\nf(\\sqrt[3]{-8}) + f(-\\pi) + f(\\sqrt{50}) + f\\left(\\frac{9}{2}\\right) = 2 + 9 + 64 + 4 = 79\n\\]\n\nThus, the final answer is \\(\\boxed{79}\\).'
'To solve the inequality \\((x-4)^2 \\le 9\\), we start by considering the equivalent equation \\((x-4)^2 = 9\\). Solving this equation, we have:\n\n\\[\nx-4 = \\pm 3\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[\nx-4 = 3 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = 7\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx-4 = -3 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = 1\n\\]\n\nThe solutions to the equation \\((x-4)^2 = 9\\) are \\(x = 1\\) and \\(x = 7\\). The inequality \\((x-4)^2 \\le 9\\) describes the set of points between and including these solutions. Therefore, the solution to the inequality is:\n\n\\[\n1 \\le x \\le 7\n\\]\n\nThe length of the segment on the number line that satisfies this inequality is the distance between \\(x = 1\\) and \\(x = 7\\), which is:\n\n\\[\n7 - 1 = 6\n\\]\n\nThus, the length of the segment is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
"To find the function \\( k(x) \\) such that \\( f(x) \\) is its own inverse, we need to ensure that \\( f(f(x)) = x \\) for all \\( x \\) in the domain of \\( f \\).\n\nGiven the piecewise function:\n\\[ f(x) =\n\\begin{cases}\nk(x) & \\text{if } x > 0, \\\\\n-\\frac{1}{2x} & \\text{if } x < 0, \\\\\n0 & \\text{if } x = 0.\n\\end{cases}\n\\]\n\nWe need to consider the cases for \\( x > 0 \\), \\( x < 0 \\), and \\( x = 0 \\).\n\n1. **Case \\( x > 0 \\):**\n\n   For \\( f(x) = k(x) \\), we need \\( f(f(x)) = x \\). This means:\n   \\[\n   f(k(x)) = x.\n   \\]\n   Since \\( x > 0 \\), \\( k(x) > 0 \\) and thus \\( f(k(x)) = k(k(x)) \\). Therefore, we need:\n   \\[\n   k(k(x)) = x.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Case \\( x < 0 \\):**\n\n   For \\( f(x) = -\\frac{1}{2x} \\), we need \\( f(f(x)) = x \\). This means:\n   \\[\n   f\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = x.\n   \\]\n   Since \\(-\\frac{1}{2x} > 0\\), we have:\n   \\[\n   k\\left(-\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = x.\n   \\]\n\n3. **Case \\( x = 0 \\):**\n\n   For \\( f(x) = 0 \\), we need \\( f(f(x)) = x \\). This means:\n   \\[\n   f(0) = 0,\n   \\]\n   which is already satisfied.\n\nNow, let's solve for \\( k(x) \\) such that \\( k(k(x)) = x \\) for \\( x > 0 \\).\n\nAssume \\( k(x) = \\frac{1}{2x} \\). Then:\n\\[\nk(k(x)) = k\\left(\\frac{1}{2x}\\right) = \\frac{1}{2\\left(\\frac{1}{2x}\\right)} = x.\n\\]\n\nThis satisfies the condition \\( k(k(x)) = x \\).\n\nTherefore, the function \\( k(x) \\) is:\n\\[\nk(x) = \\frac{1}{2x}.\n\\]"
'To solve for \\( f(g(f(g(f(8))))) \\), we need to evaluate the functions step by step:\n\n1. **Start with \\( f(8) \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(x) = \\sqrt{x} \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad f(8) = \\sqrt{8} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Next, evaluate \\( g(f(8)) = g(2\\sqrt{2}) \\):**\n   \\[\n   g(x) = x^2 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad g(2\\sqrt{2}) = (2\\sqrt{2})^2 = 4 \\times 2 = 8\n   \\]\n\n3. **Then, evaluate \\( f(g(f(8))) = f(8) \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(8) = \\sqrt{8} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Next, evaluate \\( g(f(g(f(8)))) = g(2\\sqrt{2}) \\):**\n   \\[\n   g(2\\sqrt{2}) = (2\\sqrt{2})^2 = 8\n   \\]\n\n5. **Finally, evaluate \\( f(g(f(g(f(8))))) = f(8) \\):**\n   \\[\n   f(8) = \\sqrt{8} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the final result is:\n\\[\nf(g(f(g(f(8))))) = 2\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{2\\sqrt{2}}\\).'
'To find the least value of \\( b \\) such that \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\le 0 \\), we first need to solve the equation \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 = 0 \\) to find the roots. This will help us determine the intervals where the inequality holds.\n\nThe quadratic equation is:\n\n\\[\nb^2 + 2b - 15 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe can solve this using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-B \\pm \\sqrt{B^2 - 4AC}}{2A}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( A = 1 \\), \\( B = 2 \\), and \\( C = -15 \\). Plugging in these values, we get:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{2^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-15)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{4 + 60}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm \\sqrt{64}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 \\pm 8}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us the roots:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 + 8}{2} = 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{-2 - 8}{2} = -5\n\\]\n\nThe roots of the equation are \\( b = 3 \\) and \\( b = -5 \\). The quadratic \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\) is a parabola that opens upwards (since the coefficient of \\( b^2 \\) is positive). Therefore, the inequality \\( b^2 + 2b - 15 \\le 0 \\) holds between the roots, i.e., for \\( -5 \\le b \\le 3 \\).\n\nThus, the least value of \\( b \\) that satisfies the inequality is \\( \\boxed{-5} \\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to account for the time difference between New York and Denver and the duration of the train journey.\n\n1. **Time Difference**: When it is noon in New York, it is 10 a.m. in Denver. This means Denver is 2 hours behind New York.\n\n2. **Departure Time**: The train leaves New York at 2 p.m. New York time. In Denver time, this would be 2 p.m. - 2 hours = 12 p.m. (noon).\n\n3. **Travel Duration**: The train journey takes 45 hours.\n\n4. **Arrival Time in Denver**: We add the 45-hour travel duration to the Denver departure time (12 p.m.):\n   - 12 p.m. (noon) + 24 hours = 12 p.m. (noon) the next day\n   - 12 p.m. + 21 hours = 9 a.m.\n\nTherefore, the train arrives in Denver at 9 a.m. Denver time.'
"To solve this problem, we need to understand the transformations applied to the function \\( f(x) \\) and how they affect the function's properties.\n\n1. **Shift 2 units to the right**: This transformation changes the function to \\( f(x-2) \\).\n\n2. **Stretch vertically by a factor of 2**: This transformation changes the function to \\( 2f(x) \\).\n\nThe problem states that after these transformations, the resulting graph is identical to the original graph. This means:\n\n\\[ 2f(x-2) = f(x) \\]\n\nWe are also given that \\( f(0) = 0.1 \\).\n\nTo find \\( f(10) \\), we can use the functional equation \\( 2f(x-2) = f(x) \\).\n\nLet's calculate a few values to identify a pattern:\n\n- Start with \\( f(0) = 0.1 \\).\n\n- Use the equation \\( 2f(x-2) = f(x) \\) to find \\( f(2) \\):\n  \\[\n  2f(0) = f(2) \\implies 2 \\times 0.1 = f(2) \\implies f(2) = 0.2\n  \\]\n\n- Use the equation again to find \\( f(4) \\):\n  \\[\n  2f(2) = f(4) \\implies 2 \\times 0.2 = f(4) \\implies f(4) = 0.4\n  \\]\n\n- Use the equation again to find \\( f(6) \\):\n  \\[\n  2f(4) = f(6) \\implies 2 \\times 0.4 = f(6) \\implies f(6) = 0.8\n  \\]\n\n- Use the equation again to find \\( f(8) \\):\n  \\[\n  2f(6) = f(8) \\implies 2 \\times 0.8 = f(8) \\implies f(8) = 1.6\n  \\]\n\n- Finally, use the equation to find \\( f(10) \\):\n  \\[\n  2f(8) = f(10) \\implies 2 \\times 1.6 = f(10) \\implies f(10) = 3.2\n  \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(10) \\) is \\(\\boxed{3.2}\\)."
'Alice finishes the 100-meter race 5 seconds before Beatrice, who takes 25 seconds to complete it. Therefore, Alice takes \\(25 - 5 = 20\\) seconds to run 100 meters.\n\nTo find out how long it takes Alice to run 50 meters, we use the fact that her speed is constant. If she takes 20 seconds to run 100 meters, her speed is \\(\\frac{100 \\text{ meters}}{20 \\text{ seconds}} = 5 \\text{ meters per second}\\).\n\nTo run 50 meters at this speed, the time taken is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{50 \\text{ meters}}{5 \\text{ meters per second}} = 10 \\text{ seconds}\n\\]\n\nThus, it would take Alice 10 seconds to run 50 meters. The answer is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
'For the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + mx + (m+n) = 0\\) to have one real solution, the discriminant must be zero. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) of a quadratic equation \\(ax^2 + bx + c = 0\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = b^2 - 4ac\n\\]\n\nIn this case, \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = m\\), and \\(c = m+n\\). Therefore, the discriminant is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = m^2 - 4(1)(m+n) = m^2 - 4m - 4n\n\\]\n\nSetting the discriminant to zero for the equation to have one real solution:\n\n\\[\nm^2 - 4m - 4n = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in terms of \\(m\\). For there to be a unique value of \\(m\\), the discriminant of this quadratic equation must also be zero. The discriminant of \\(m^2 - 4m - 4n = 0\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta_m = (-4)^2 - 4(1)(-4n) = 16 + 16n\n\\]\n\nSetting this discriminant to zero:\n\n\\[\n16 + 16n = 0\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(n\\):\n\n\\[\n16n = -16 \\\\\nn = -1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(n\\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we first need to find the sum of the first ten positive integers. The sum is given by:\n\n\\[ 1 + 2 + 3 + \\ldots + 10 = \\frac{10 \\times 11}{2} = 55. \\]\n\nMarsha's sum is a square number, which means she omitted one of these integers to achieve a sum that is a perfect square. Let's denote the omitted integer as \\( x \\). Therefore, the sum of the remaining integers is:\n\n\\[ 55 - x. \\]\n\nWe need to find an integer \\( x \\) such that \\( 55 - x \\) is a perfect square. Let's check each possibility:\n\n- If \\( x = 1 \\), then \\( 55 - 1 = 54 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 2 \\), then \\( 55 - 2 = 53 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 3 \\), then \\( 55 - 3 = 52 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 4 \\), then \\( 55 - 4 = 51 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 5 \\), then \\( 55 - 5 = 50 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 6 \\), then \\( 55 - 6 = 49 \\), which is \\( 7^2 \\) (a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 7 \\), then \\( 55 - 7 = 48 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 8 \\), then \\( 55 - 8 = 47 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 9 \\), then \\( 55 - 9 = 46 \\) (not a perfect square).\n- If \\( x = 10 \\), then \\( 55 - 10 = 45 \\) (not a perfect square).\n\nThe only value of \\( x \\) that results in a perfect square is \\( x = 6 \\). Therefore, Marsha did not include the number 6 in her sum. \n\nThe answer is 6."
'To solve the equation \\(\\log_{64^{\\frac{1}{3}}}4^x=1\\), we start by simplifying the base of the logarithm. \n\nThe base is \\(64^{\\frac{1}{3}}\\). We know that \\(64 = 4^3\\), so:\n\n\\[\n64^{\\frac{1}{3}} = (4^3)^{\\frac{1}{3}} = 4^{3 \\cdot \\frac{1}{3}} = 4^1 = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{4}4^x = 1\n\\]\n\nThe property of logarithms \\(\\log_b b^y = y\\) tells us that:\n\n\\[\n\\log_{4}4^x = x\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the equation simplifies to:\n\n\\[\nx = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x\\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'To find \\( f^{-1}(f^{-1}(6)) \\), we first need to determine \\( f^{-1}(6) \\). Since \\( f(2) = 6 \\), it follows that \\( f^{-1}(6) = 2 \\).\n\nNext, we need to find \\( f^{-1}(2) \\). Since \\( f(1) = 2 \\), it follows that \\( f^{-1}(2) = 1 \\).\n\nTherefore, \\( f^{-1}(f^{-1}(6)) = f^{-1}(2) = 1 \\).\n\nThe answer is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
"To find \\( a + b \\), we start by using the fact that the roots of the polynomial \\( p(x) = x^2 + ax + b \\) are given as \\( 2a \\) and \\( b \\).\n\nBy Vieta's formulas, the sum of the roots of the polynomial is equal to the negation of the coefficient of \\( x \\), which gives us:\n\\[\n2a + b = -a\n\\]\nRearranging this equation, we get:\n\\[\n3a + b = 0 \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)}\n\\]\n\nSimilarly, the product of the roots is equal to the constant term \\( b \\), which gives us:\n\\[\n(2a)(b) = b\n\\]\nAssuming \\( b \\neq 0 \\) (since the roots are distinct), we can divide both sides by \\( b \\) to obtain:\n\\[\n2a = 1\n\\]\nSolving for \\( a \\), we find:\n\\[\na = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( a = \\frac{1}{2} \\) into Equation 1, we have:\n\\[\n3\\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right) + b = 0\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{2} + b = 0\n\\]\n\\[\nb = -\\frac{3}{2}\n\\]\n\nFinally, we calculate \\( a + b \\):\n\\[\na + b = \\frac{1}{2} + \\left(-\\frac{3}{2}\\right) = \\frac{1}{2} - \\frac{3}{2} = -1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\)."
"Let's denote the weight of a treek as \\( T \\), the weight of a squig as \\( S \\), and the weight of a goolee as \\( G \\).\n\nFrom the problem, we have the following equations:\n\n1. \\( 10T = 3S + G \\)\n2. \\( 2T + G = S \\)\n\nWe need to find the number of treeks that equal the weight of one squig, i.e., we need to find \\( \\frac{S}{T} \\).\n\nFirst, let's solve the second equation for \\( G \\):\n\n\\[ G = S - 2T \\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( G \\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[ 10T = 3S + (S - 2T) \\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[ 10T = 4S - 2T \\]\n\nAdd \\( 2T \\) to both sides:\n\n\\[ 12T = 4S \\]\n\nDivide both sides by 4:\n\n\\[ 3T = S \\]\n\nThus, the weight of one squig is equal to the weight of 3 treeks. Therefore, the combined weight of 3 treeks equals the weight of one squig. The answer is \\(\\boxed{3}\\)."
"Let's denote the number of clowns as \\( c \\) and the number of horses as \\( h \\).\n\nEach clown has 2 legs and 1 head, and each horse has 4 legs and 1 head. We have the following system of equations based on the given information:\n\n1. The total number of heads is 10:\n   \\[\n   c + h = 10\n   \\]\n\n2. The total number of legs is 30:\n   \\[\n   2c + 4h = 30\n   \\]\n\nWe can solve this system of equations to find the values of \\( c \\) and \\( h \\).\n\nFirst, solve the first equation for \\( c \\):\n\\[\nc = 10 - h\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( c = 10 - h \\) into the second equation:\n\\[\n2(10 - h) + 4h = 30\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( h \\):\n\\[\n20 - 2h + 4h = 30\n\\]\n\\[\n20 + 2h = 30\n\\]\n\\[\n2h = 10\n\\]\n\\[\nh = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, there are 5 horses in the parade. Therefore, the number of horses you saw is \\(\\boxed{5}\\)."
"Let's denote the weight of \\( B \\) as \\( b \\), the weight of \\( A \\) as \\( a \\), and the weight of \\( C \\) as \\( c \\).\n\nAccording to the problem, the weight of \\( A \\) is \\( 40\\% \\) greater than the weight of \\( B \\). This can be expressed as:\n\\[\na = b + 0.4b = 1.4b\n\\]\n\nAdditionally, the weight of \\( A \\) is \\( 30\\% \\) less than the weight of \\( C \\). This can be expressed as:\n\\[\na = c - 0.3c = 0.7c\n\\]\n\nNow, we have two equations:\n1. \\( a = 1.4b \\)\n2. \\( a = 0.7c \\)\n\nSince both expressions equal \\( a \\), we can set them equal to each other:\n\\[\n1.4b = 0.7c\n\\]\n\nTo find the ratio of the weight of \\( B \\) to the weight of \\( C \\), solve for \\( \\frac{b}{c} \\):\n\\[\n\\frac{b}{c} = \\frac{0.7}{1.4}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the fraction:\n\\[\n\\frac{0.7}{1.4} = \\frac{7}{14} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the ratio of the weight of \\( B \\) to the weight of \\( C \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{2}}\\)."
'To find the sum of all numbers \\( a \\) for which the graphs of \\( y = x^2 + a \\) and \\( y = ax \\) intersect exactly once, we need to set the equations equal to each other and analyze the resulting equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + a = ax\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms, we get:\n\n\\[\nx^2 - ax + a = 0\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in \\( x \\). For the graphs to intersect exactly once, the quadratic equation must have exactly one solution. This occurs when the discriminant of the quadratic equation is zero. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 - ax + a = 0\\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = b^2 - 4ac = (-a)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot a = a^2 - 4a\n\\]\n\nSetting the discriminant equal to zero for the quadratic to have exactly one solution:\n\n\\[\na^2 - 4a = 0\n\\]\n\nFactoring the equation:\n\n\\[\na(a - 4) = 0\n\\]\n\nThis gives the solutions:\n\n\\[\na = 0 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad a = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, the values of \\( a \\) for which the graphs intersect exactly once are \\( a = 0 \\) and \\( a = 4 \\). The sum of these values is:\n\n\\[\n0 + 4 = 4\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum of all numbers \\( a \\) for which the graphs intersect exactly once is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To solve the inequality \\((2x+10)(x+3) < (3x+9)(x+8)\\), we first expand both sides.\n\nExpanding the left side:\n\\[\n(2x+10)(x+3) = 2x(x) + 2x(3) + 10(x) + 10(3) = 2x^2 + 6x + 10x + 30 = 2x^2 + 16x + 30\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\\[\n(3x+9)(x+8) = 3x(x) + 3x(8) + 9(x) + 9(8) = 3x^2 + 24x + 9x + 72 = 3x^2 + 33x + 72\n\\]\n\nNow, we set up the inequality:\n\\[\n2x^2 + 16x + 30 < 3x^2 + 33x + 72\n\\]\n\nSubtract the left side from the right side to bring all terms to one side:\n\\[\n0 < 3x^2 + 33x + 72 - 2x^2 - 16x - 30\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\\[\n0 < x^2 + 17x + 42\n\\]\n\nWe need to solve the inequality:\n\\[\nx^2 + 17x + 42 > 0\n\\]\n\nFirst, find the roots of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + 17x + 42 = 0\\) using the quadratic formula:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\nwhere \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = 17\\), and \\(c = 42\\).\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = 17^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 42 = 289 - 168 = 121\n\\]\n\nThe square root of 121 is 11, so the roots are:\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-17 \\pm 11}{2}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the roots:\n\\[\nx_1 = \\frac{-17 + 11}{2} = \\frac{-6}{2} = -3\n\\]\n\\[\nx_2 = \\frac{-17 - 11}{2} = \\frac{-28}{2} = -14\n\\]\n\nThe roots of the quadratic are \\(x = -3\\) and \\(x = -14\\). The quadratic \\(x^2 + 17x + 42\\) is a parabola opening upwards (since the coefficient of \\(x^2\\) is positive). The inequality \\(x^2 + 17x + 42 > 0\\) is satisfied outside the interval between the roots.\n\nThus, the solution in interval notation is:\n\\[\n(-\\infty, -14) \\cup (-3, \\infty)\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution to the inequality is \\((- \\infty, -14) \\cup (-3, \\infty)\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to calculate the future value of the investment using compound interest. The formula for compound interest is:\n\n\\[ A = P \\left(1 + \\frac{r}{n}\\right)^{nt} \\]\n\nwhere:\n- \\( A \\) is the amount of money accumulated after n years, including interest.\n- \\( P \\) is the principal amount (initial investment).\n- \\( r \\) is the annual interest rate (decimal).\n- \\( n \\) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year.\n- \\( t \\) is the time the money is invested for in years.\n\nIn this problem:\n- \\( P = 24,000 \\) dollars.\n- The interest rate \\( r = 0.01 \\) (1% bi-monthly).\n- Since the interest is compounded bi-monthly, \\( n = 6 \\) (because there are 6 two-month periods in a year).\n- The investment is for \\( t = 5 \\) years.\n\nPlug these values into the formula:\n\n\\[ A = 24000 \\left(1 + \\frac{0.01}{1}\\right)^{6 \\times 5} \\]\n\n\\[ A = 24000 \\left(1.01\\right)^{30} \\]\n\nNow, calculate \\( (1.01)^{30} \\):\n\n\\[ (1.01)^{30} \\approx 1.347848 \\]\n\nNow, calculate the total amount \\( A \\):\n\n\\[ A = 24000 \\times 1.347848 \\]\n\n\\[ A \\approx 32,348.35 \\]\n\nRounding to the nearest whole number, the total amount in the investment at the end of five years is approximately \\(\\boxed{32,348}\\) dollars.'
"To find the real values of \\( x \\) that are not in the domain of the function \\( f(x) = \\frac{1}{|x^2+3x-4|+|x^2+9x+20|} \\), we need to determine when the denominator is equal to zero. This occurs when:\n\n\\[\n|x^2 + 3x - 4| + |x^2 + 9x + 20| = 0\n\\]\n\nSince the absolute value of any expression is non-negative, the only way for their sum to be zero is if both expressions inside the absolute values are zero:\n\n1. \\( |x^2 + 3x - 4| = 0 \\)\n2. \\( |x^2 + 9x + 20| = 0 \\)\n\nThis implies:\n\n1. \\( x^2 + 3x - 4 = 0 \\)\n2. \\( x^2 + 9x + 20 = 0 \\)\n\nLet's solve each quadratic equation:\n\n1. For \\( x^2 + 3x - 4 = 0 \\), we use the quadratic formula:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n   \\]\n   where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 3 \\), and \\( c = -4 \\). Thus,\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{3^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-4)}}{2 \\cdot 1} = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{9 + 16}}{2} = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{25}}{2} = \\frac{-3 \\pm 5}{2}\n   \\]\n   This gives the solutions \\( x = 1 \\) and \\( x = -4 \\).\n\n2. For \\( x^2 + 9x + 20 = 0 \\), we again use the quadratic formula:\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{-9 \\pm \\sqrt{9^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 20}}{2 \\cdot 1} = \\frac{-9 \\pm \\sqrt{81 - 80}}{2} = \\frac{-9 \\pm \\sqrt{1}}{2}\n   \\]\n   This gives the solutions \\( x = -4 \\) and \\( x = -5 \\).\n\nThe values of \\( x \\) that make either of the quadratic expressions zero are \\( x = 1, -4, -5 \\).\n\nTherefore, the real values of \\( x \\) that are not in the domain of \\( f(x) \\) are \\( \\boxed{1, -4, -5} \\)."
'To find the value of \\( f(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) \\) for the function \\( f(x) = x^{(x+1)}(x+2)^{(x+3)} \\), we will evaluate each term separately.\n\n1. **Evaluate \\( f(0) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(0) = 0^{(0+1)}(0+2)^{(0+3)} = 0^1 \\cdot 2^3 = 0 \\cdot 8 = 0\n   \\]\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = (-1)^{(-1+1)}(-1+2)^{(-1+3)} = (-1)^0 \\cdot 1^2 = 1 \\cdot 1 = 1\n   \\]\n\n3. **Evaluate \\( f(-2) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = (-2)^{(-2+1)}(-2+2)^{(-2+3)} = (-2)^{-1} \\cdot 0^1\n   \\]\n\n   Since any number raised to a power multiplied by zero is zero, we have:\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = \\frac{1}{-2} \\cdot 0 = 0\n   \\]\n\n4. **Evaluate \\( f(-3) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-3) = (-3)^{(-3+1)}(-3+2)^{(-3+3)} = (-3)^{-2} \\cdot (-1)^0\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   f(-3) = \\frac{1}{(-3)^2} \\cdot 1 = \\frac{1}{9} \\cdot 1 = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\nNow, we sum these values:\n\n\\[\nf(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) = 0 + 1 + 0 + \\frac{1}{9} = 1 + \\frac{1}{9} = \\frac{9}{9} + \\frac{1}{9} = \\frac{10}{9}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(0) + f(-1) + f(-2) + f(-3) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{10}{9}}\\).'
'We are given the following conditions:\n\n1. \\( a + b + c = 88 \\)\n2. \\( a - 5 = N \\)\n3. \\( b + 5 = N \\)\n4. \\( 5c = N \\)\n\nWe need to find the value of \\( N \\).\n\nFrom the second condition, we have:\n\\[ a = N + 5 \\]\n\nFrom the third condition, we have:\n\\[ b = N - 5 \\]\n\nFrom the fourth condition, we have:\n\\[ c = \\frac{N}{5} \\]\n\nSubstitute these expressions for \\( a \\), \\( b \\), and \\( c \\) into the first condition:\n\\[ (N + 5) + (N - 5) + \\frac{N}{5} = 88 \\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\\[ N + 5 + N - 5 + \\frac{N}{5} = 88 \\]\n\\[ 2N + \\frac{N}{5} = 88 \\]\n\nTo eliminate the fraction, multiply the entire equation by 5:\n\\[ 5(2N) + N = 440 \\]\n\\[ 10N + N = 440 \\]\n\\[ 11N = 440 \\]\n\nDivide both sides by 11 to solve for \\( N \\):\n\\[ N = \\frac{440}{11} \\]\n\\[ N = 40 \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( N \\) is \\(\\boxed{40}\\).'
"To solve this problem, we need to use the properties of a geometric sequence. In a geometric sequence, each term is obtained by multiplying the previous term by a constant ratio, \\( r \\).\n\nLet's denote the first term of the sequence as \\( a \\). Then, the terms of the sequence can be expressed as follows:\n- The third term is \\( ar^2 = 1053 \\).\n- The ninth term is \\( ar^8 = \\frac{13}{9} \\).\n\nWe need to find the seventh term, which is \\( ar^6 \\).\n\nFirst, let's find the common ratio \\( r \\) by using the given terms. We have:\n\\[\n\\frac{ar^8}{ar^2} = \\frac{\\frac{13}{9}}{1053}\n\\]\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[\nr^6 = \\frac{\\frac{13}{9}}{1053}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the right-hand side:\n\\[\n1053 = 3 \\times 351 = 3 \\times 3 \\times 117 = 3^2 \\times 39 = 3^2 \\times 3 \\times 13 = 3^3 \\times 13\n\\]\nThus, \n\\[\nr^6 = \\frac{13}{9 \\times 1053} = \\frac{13}{9 \\times 3^3 \\times 13} = \\frac{1}{9 \\times 27} = \\frac{1}{243}\n\\]\n\nNow, solve for \\( r \\):\n\\[\nr^6 = \\frac{1}{243} = \\frac{1}{3^5}\n\\]\nThus, \\( r = \\frac{1}{3} \\).\n\nNow, we can find the seventh term \\( ar^6 \\):\n\\[\nar^6 = ar^2 \\cdot r^4 = 1053 \\cdot \\left(\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^4\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( \\left(\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^4 \\):\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^4 = \\frac{1}{81}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the seventh term is:\n\\[\nar^6 = 1053 \\cdot \\frac{1}{81} = \\frac{1053}{81}\n\\]\n\nSimplify \\( \\frac{1053}{81} \\):\n\\[\n1053 \\div 81 = 13\n\\]\n\nThus, the seventh term is \\(\\boxed{13}\\)."
'To evaluate \\(\\left(\\dfrac{-2i}{5}\\right)^2\\), we first square the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\dfrac{-2i}{5}\\right)^2 = \\dfrac{(-2i)^2}{5^2}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\((-2i)^2\\):\n\n\\[\n(-2i)^2 = (-2)^2 \\cdot i^2 = 4 \\cdot (-1) = -4\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate \\(5^2\\):\n\n\\[\n5^2 = 25\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these results back into the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\dfrac{(-2i)^2}{5^2} = \\dfrac{-4}{25}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\left(\\dfrac{-2i}{5}\\right)^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\dfrac{4}{25}}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\), we start with the given equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} = 7\n\\]\n\nWe want to express \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\) in terms of \\( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} \\). We can use the identity:\n\n\\[\n\\left( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} \\right)^2 = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nExpanding the left side, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\left( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} \\right)^2 = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given value:\n\n\\[\n7^2 = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n49 = x^4 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^4}\n\\]\n\nSubtract 2 from both sides to solve for \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\):\n\n\\[\nx^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} = 49 - 2 = 47\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x^4 + \\frac{1}{x^4} \\) is \\(\\boxed{47}\\).'

'To compute \\(32^2 - 18^2\\), we can use the difference of squares formula, which states:\n\n\\[\na^2 - b^2 = (a-b)(a+b)\n\\]\n\nIn this case, \\(a = 32\\) and \\(b = 18\\). Applying the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n32^2 - 18^2 = (32 - 18)(32 + 18)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each part:\n\n\\[\n32 - 18 = 14\n\\]\n\\[\n32 + 18 = 50\n\\]\n\nNow, multiply these results:\n\n\\[\n14 \\times 50 = 700\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(32^2 - 18^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{700}\\).'
'To find the fiftieth term of the arithmetic sequence, we first need to determine the common difference and the first term of the sequence.\n\nThe general formula for the \\(n\\)-th term of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\\[ a_n = a_1 + (n-1)d \\]\nwhere \\(a_n\\) is the \\(n\\)-th term, \\(a_1\\) is the first term, and \\(d\\) is the common difference.\n\nWe know:\n- The second term \\(a_2 = 2\\)\n- The ninth term \\(a_9 = 30\\)\n\nUsing the formula for the second term:\n\\[ a_2 = a_1 + (2-1)d = a_1 + d = 2 \\]\n\nUsing the formula for the ninth term:\n\\[ a_9 = a_1 + (9-1)d = a_1 + 8d = 30 \\]\n\nNow, we have the system of equations:\n1. \\( a_1 + d = 2 \\)\n2. \\( a_1 + 8d = 30 \\)\n\nSubtract the first equation from the second to eliminate \\(a_1\\):\n\\[ (a_1 + 8d) - (a_1 + d) = 30 - 2 \\]\n\\[ 7d = 28 \\]\n\\[ d = 4 \\]\n\nSubstitute \\(d = 4\\) back into the first equation to find \\(a_1\\):\n\\[ a_1 + 4 = 2 \\]\n\\[ a_1 = 2 - 4 \\]\n\\[ a_1 = -2 \\]\n\nNow, we can find the fiftieth term \\(a_{50}\\):\n\\[ a_{50} = a_1 + (50-1)d \\]\n\\[ a_{50} = -2 + 49 \\times 4 \\]\n\\[ a_{50} = -2 + 196 \\]\n\\[ a_{50} = 194 \\]\n\nTherefore, the fiftieth term of the sequence is \\(\\boxed{194}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to follow the transformations step by step and determine the new equation of the parabola after each transformation.\n\n1. **Original Equation**: The given equation of the parabola is \\( y = -(x+1)^2 + 1 \\).\n\n2. **Shift 1 Unit to the Right**: Shifting the graph 1 unit to the right involves replacing \\( x \\) with \\( x-1 \\) in the equation. Thus, the equation becomes:\n   \\[\n   y = -((x-1)+1)^2 + 1 = -(x)^2 + 1 = -x^2 + 1\n   \\]\n\n3. **Shift 5 Units Down**: Shifting the graph 5 units down involves subtracting 5 from the entire equation. Thus, the equation becomes:\n   \\[\n   y = -x^2 + 1 - 5 = -x^2 - 4\n   \\]\n\n4. **Rotate 180 Degrees About Its Vertex**: The vertex of the parabola \\( y = -x^2 - 4 \\) is at \\( (0, -4) \\). Rotating the parabola 180 degrees about its vertex changes the sign of the coefficient of \\( x^2 \\) (since it reflects the parabola over the vertex), resulting in:\n   \\[\n   y = x^2 - 4\n   \\]\n\nNow, we need to find the zeros of the resulting parabola \\( y = x^2 - 4 \\). Setting \\( y = 0 \\), we solve:\n\\[\nx^2 - 4 = 0\n\\]\n\\[\nx^2 = 4\n\\]\n\\[\nx = \\pm 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the zeros are \\( x = -2 \\) and \\( x = 2 \\). Therefore, \\( a = -2 \\) and \\( b = 2 \\), and we need to find \\( b - a \\):\n\\[\nb - a = 2 - (-2) = 2 + 2 = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( b-a \\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
"To solve the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + 5x + 8 = 0\\), we use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = 1\\), \\(b = 5\\), and \\(c = 8\\). Plugging these values into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{5^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot 8}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{25 - 32}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-5 \\pm \\sqrt{-7}}{2}\n\\]\n\nSince the discriminant is negative, the solutions are complex numbers. We can express \\(\\sqrt{-7}\\) as \\(i\\sqrt{7}\\), where \\(i\\) is the imaginary unit. Thus, the solutions are:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-5 \\pm i\\sqrt{7}}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[\nx_1 = \\frac{-5 + i\\sqrt{7}}{2} \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x_2 = \\frac{-5 - i\\sqrt{7}}{2}\n\\]\n\nBoth solutions are in the form \\(x = a + bi\\), where \\(a = -\\frac{5}{2}\\) and \\(b = \\pm \\frac{\\sqrt{7}}{2}\\).\n\nWe need to find \\(a + b^2\\). Let's calculate \\(b^2\\) for \\(b = \\frac{\\sqrt{7}}{2}\\):\n\n\\[\nb^2 = \\left(\\frac{\\sqrt{7}}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{7}{4}\n\\]\n\nNow, calculate \\(a + b^2\\):\n\n\\[\na + b^2 = -\\frac{5}{2} + \\frac{7}{4}\n\\]\n\nTo add these, convert \\(-\\frac{5}{2}\\) to a fraction with a denominator of 4:\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{5}{2} = -\\frac{10}{4}\n\\]\n\nNow add:\n\n\\[\na + b^2 = -\\frac{10}{4} + \\frac{7}{4} = -\\frac{3}{4}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(a + b^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{3}{4}}\\)."
'To find the total number of chimes the clock will strike in a twelve-hour period, we need to sum the number of chimes for each hour from 1 to 12.\n\nThe number of chimes at each hour is equal to the hour number. Therefore, the total number of chimes is the sum of the first 12 positive integers:\n\n\\[ 1 + 2 + 3 + \\ldots + 12. \\]\n\nThis is an arithmetic series where the first term \\(a = 1\\), the last term \\(l = 12\\), and the number of terms \\(n = 12\\).\n\nThe sum \\(S\\) of an arithmetic series can be calculated using the formula:\n\n\\[ S = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (a + l). \\]\n\nSubstituting the values, we get:\n\n\\[ S = \\frac{12}{2} \\times (1 + 12) = 6 \\times 13 = 78. \\]\n\nTherefore, the total number of chimes the clock will strike in a twelve-hour period is \\(\\boxed{78}\\).'
"To determine the number of endpoints in Figure 5, we need to understand the pattern of how endpoints increase from one figure to the next.\n\nLet's analyze the pattern:\n\n- **Figure 1**: The initial Y shape has 3 endpoints.\n- **Figure 2**: Each endpoint of Figure 1 is replaced by a smaller Y, adding 2 new endpoints for each original endpoint. Thus, Figure 2 has \\(3 + 3 \\times 2 = 9\\) endpoints.\n- **Figure 3**: Each endpoint of Figure 2 is replaced by a smaller Y, adding 2 new endpoints for each original endpoint. Thus, Figure 3 has \\(9 + 9 \\times 2 = 27\\) endpoints.\n\nWe can see a pattern forming: each figure has 3 times the number of endpoints as the previous figure. This is because each endpoint is replaced by a Y, which has 3 endpoints, effectively tripling the number of endpoints.\n\nUsing this pattern, we can calculate the number of endpoints for the subsequent figures:\n\n- **Figure 4**: \\(27 \\times 3 = 81\\) endpoints.\n- **Figure 5**: \\(81 \\times 3 = 243\\) endpoints.\n\nTherefore, Figure 5 will have \\(\\boxed{243}\\) endpoints."
'To find the area of the circle, we first need to determine the radius. Since points \\(A(-1, -2)\\) and \\(B(3, 2)\\) are the endpoints of a diameter, we can find the length of the diameter using the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coordinates of points \\(A\\) and \\(B\\):\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(3 - (-1))^2 + (2 - (-2))^2} = \\sqrt{(3 + 1)^2 + (2 + 2)^2} = \\sqrt{4^2 + 4^2} = \\sqrt{16 + 16} = \\sqrt{32} = 4\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThe diameter of the circle is \\(4\\sqrt{2}\\), so the radius \\(r\\) is half of the diameter:\n\n\\[\nr = \\frac{4\\sqrt{2}}{2} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThe area \\(A\\) of the circle is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi r^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the radius:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi (2\\sqrt{2})^2 = \\pi (4 \\times 2) = 8\\pi\n\\]\n\nThus, the area of the circle is \\(\\boxed{8\\pi}\\) square units.'
"To find the positive value of \\( b \\) such that the equation \\(\\frac{3}{x} + \\frac{x}{3} = b\\) has exactly one solution, we need to analyze the behavior of the function \\( f(x) = \\frac{3}{x} + \\frac{x}{3} \\).\n\nFirst, let's find the derivative of \\( f(x) \\) to determine the critical points and the nature of the function:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = \\frac{3}{x} + \\frac{x}{3}\n\\]\n\nThe derivative \\( f'(x) \\) is:\n\n\\[\nf'(x) = -\\frac{3}{x^2} + \\frac{1}{3}\n\\]\n\nSetting \\( f'(x) = 0 \\) to find the critical points:\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{3}{x^2} + \\frac{1}{3} = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{3}{x^2} = -\\frac{1}{3}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{x^2} = \\frac{1}{3}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx^2 = 9\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 3 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad x = -3\n\\]\n\nNext, we determine the nature of these critical points by evaluating the second derivative \\( f''(x) \\):\n\n\\[\nf''(x) = \\frac{6}{x^3}\n\\]\n\nEvaluating \\( f''(x) \\) at \\( x = 3 \\):\n\n\\[\nf''(3) = \\frac{6}{27} = \\frac{2}{9} > 0\n\\]\n\nThis indicates that \\( x = 3 \\) is a local minimum.\n\nEvaluating \\( f''(x) \\) at \\( x = -3 \\):\n\n\\[\nf''(-3) = \\frac{6}{-27} = -\\frac{2}{9} < 0\n\\]\n\nThis indicates that \\( x = -3 \\) is a local maximum.\n\nSince \\( x = 3 \\) is a local minimum, the function \\( f(x) \\) will have exactly one solution for \\( b \\) if \\( b \\) is equal to the minimum value of \\( f(x) \\).\n\nCalculate \\( f(3) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(3) = \\frac{3}{3} + \\frac{3}{3} = 1 + 1 = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the positive value of \\( b \\) such that the equation \\(\\frac{3}{x} + \\frac{x}{3} = b\\) has exactly one solution is \\(\\boxed{2}\\)."
'To find the number of non-congruent right triangles with one leg of length 162, we use the Pythagorean theorem. Let the sides of the triangle be \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\), where \\(c\\) is the hypotenuse and \\(a = 162\\). We need to find integer values of \\(b\\) and \\(c\\) such that:\n\n\\[\n162^2 + b^2 = c^2\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\(162^2\\):\n\n\\[\n162^2 = 26244\n\\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[\n26244 + b^2 = c^2 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad c^2 - b^2 = 26244\n\\]\n\nThis can be factored using the difference of squares:\n\n\\[\n(c-b)(c+b) = 26244\n\\]\n\nWe need to find pairs \\((c-b, c+b)\\) such that their product is 26244. Since \\(c\\) and \\(b\\) are integers, both \\(c-b\\) and \\(c+b\\) must be even, so we consider the factorization of 26244.\n\nFirst, find the prime factorization of 26244:\n\n\\[\n26244 = 2^2 \\times 3^4 \\times 11^2\n\\]\n\nThe number of factors of 26244 is:\n\n\\[\n(2+1)(4+1)(2+1) = 3 \\times 5 \\times 3 = 45\n\\]\n\nSince both \\(c-b\\) and \\(c+b\\) must be even, we consider only even factors. The number of even factors is half of the total number of factors, which is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{45}{2} = 22.5\n\\]\n\nSince we need integer factors, we consider 22 even factor pairs. Each pair \\((c-b, c+b)\\) corresponds to a unique triangle, as each pair gives a unique \\(b\\) and \\(c\\).\n\nThus, the number of non-congruent right triangles with one leg of length 162 is \\(\\boxed{22}\\).'

Therefore, the result Eric should obtain is \\(\\boxed{368}\\) kilowatts."
'To simplify \\((5-3i)(-4+3i)\\), we use the distributive property (also known as the FOIL method for binomials):\n\n\\[\n(5-3i)(-4+3i) = 5(-4) + 5(3i) - 3i(-4) - 3i(3i)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term separately:\n\n1. \\(5(-4) = -20\\)\n2. \\(5(3i) = 15i\\)\n3. \\(-3i(-4) = 12i\\)\n4. \\(-3i(3i) = -9i^2\\)\n\nSince \\(i^2 = -1\\), we have:\n\n\\(-9i^2 = -9(-1) = 9\\)\n\nNow, combine all the terms:\n\n\\[\n-20 + 15i + 12i + 9\n\\]\n\nCombine the real parts and the imaginary parts:\n\nReal part: \\(-20 + 9 = -11\\)\n\nImaginary part: \\(15i + 12i = 27i\\)\n\nThus, the simplified expression is:\n\n\\[\n-11 + 27i\n\\]\n\nSo, \\((5-3i)(-4+3i) = -11 + 27i\\).'
'To find the value of \\(x^3 - 2x + 1\\) given that \\(x^2 - x - 1 = 0\\), we can use the fact that \\(x\\) is a root of the quadratic equation.\n\nFirst, solve for \\(x^2\\) from the equation \\(x^2 - x - 1 = 0\\):\n\\[\nx^2 = x + 1\n\\]\n\nNow, we want to find \\(x^3 - 2x + 1\\). Start by expressing \\(x^3\\) in terms of \\(x\\) using the expression for \\(x^2\\):\n\\[\nx^3 = x \\cdot x^2 = x(x + 1) = x^2 + x\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(x^2 = x + 1\\) into the expression for \\(x^3\\):\n\\[\nx^3 = (x + 1) + x = 2x + 1\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\(x^3 = 2x + 1\\) into the expression \\(x^3 - 2x + 1\\):\n\\[\nx^3 - 2x + 1 = (2x + 1) - 2x + 1 = 1 + 1 = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(x^3 - 2x + 1\\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
"To solve the equation \\( x = \\frac{1}{2 + \\frac{1}{x-2}} \\), we start by simplifying the expression on the right-hand side. Let's rewrite the equation:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{1}{2 + \\frac{1}{x-2}}. \\]\n\nFirst, simplify the denominator:\n\n\\[ 2 + \\frac{1}{x-2} = \\frac{2(x-2) + 1}{x-2} = \\frac{2x - 4 + 1}{x-2} = \\frac{2x - 3}{x-2}. \\]\n\nNow, substitute this back into the equation:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{1}{\\frac{2x - 3}{x-2}}. \\]\n\nThis is equivalent to:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{x-2}{2x-3}. \\]\n\nCross-multiply to eliminate the fraction:\n\n\\[ x(2x - 3) = x - 2. \\]\n\nExpand the left side:\n\n\\[ 2x^2 - 3x = x - 2. \\]\n\nRearrange all terms to one side:\n\n\\[ 2x^2 - 3x - x + 2 = 0, \\]\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n\\[ 2x^2 - 4x + 2 = 0. \\]\n\nDivide the entire equation by 2 to simplify:\n\n\\[ x^2 - 2x + 1 = 0. \\]\n\nThis is a perfect square trinomial:\n\n\\[ (x - 1)^2 = 0. \\]\n\nThus, the solution is:\n\n\\[ x - 1 = 0 \\]\n\n\\[ x = 1. \\]\n\nTherefore, the positive solution to the equation is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."
