'To find the value of \\( f(-2) + f(-1) + f(0) \\), we first need to evaluate each function value separately.\n\nThe function is given by:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = \\frac{3x-2}{x-2}\n\\]\n\n1. **Evaluate \\( f(-2) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-2) = \\frac{3(-2) - 2}{-2 - 2} = \\frac{-6 - 2}{-4} = \\frac{-8}{-4} = 2\n   \\]\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = \\frac{3(-1) - 2}{-1 - 2} = \\frac{-3 - 2}{-3} = \\frac{-5}{-3} = \\frac{5}{3}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Evaluate \\( f(0) \\):**\n\n   \\[\n   f(0) = \\frac{3(0) - 2}{0 - 2} = \\frac{-2}{-2} = 1\n   \\]\n\nNow, we sum these values:\n\n\\[\nf(-2) + f(-1) + f(0) = 2 + \\frac{5}{3} + 1\n\\]\n\nTo add these, we convert the integers to fractions with a common denominator:\n\n\\[\n2 = \\frac{6}{3}, \\quad 1 = \\frac{3}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{6}{3} + \\frac{5}{3} + \\frac{3}{3} = \\frac{6 + 5 + 3}{3} = \\frac{14}{3}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( f(-2) + f(-1) + f(0) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{14}{3}}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( c \\), we can use the fact that the parabola passes through the points \\((2, 3)\\) and \\((4, 3)\\). This means that when \\( x = 2 \\) and \\( x = 4 \\), the value of \\( y \\) is 3.\n\nFirst, substitute the point \\((2, 3)\\) into the equation \\( y = x^2 + bx + c \\):\n\n\\[\n3 = 2^2 + 2b + c\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3 = 4 + 2b + c\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2b + c = -1 \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)}\n\\]\n\nNext, substitute the point \\((4, 3)\\) into the equation:\n\n\\[\n3 = 4^2 + 4b + c\n\\]\n\n\\[\n3 = 16 + 4b + c\n\\]\n\n\\[\n4b + c = -13 \\quad \\text{(Equation 2)}\n\\]\n\nNow, we have a system of two equations:\n\n1. \\( 2b + c = -1 \\)\n2. \\( 4b + c = -13 \\)\n\nSubtract Equation 1 from Equation 2 to eliminate \\( c \\):\n\n\\[\n(4b + c) - (2b + c) = -13 - (-1)\n\\]\n\n\\[\n4b + c - 2b - c = -13 + 1\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2b = -12\n\\]\n\n\\[\nb = -6\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\( b = -6 \\) back into Equation 1 to find \\( c \\):\n\n\\[\n2(-6) + c = -1\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-12 + c = -1\n\\]\n\n\\[\nc = 11\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( c \\) is \\(\\boxed{11}\\).'
'To find the square of the length of \\(\\overline{AB}\\), we start by using the information that the origin is the midpoint of \\(\\overline{AB}\\). Let the coordinates of points \\(A\\) and \\(B\\) be \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\), respectively. Since the origin is the midpoint, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2}\\right) = (0, 0)\n\\]\n\nThis gives us the equations:\n\n\\[\nx_1 + x_2 = 0 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad y_1 + y_2 = 0\n\\]\n\nSince \\(x_1 + x_2 = 0\\), we have \\(x_2 = -x_1\\).\n\nBoth points \\(A\\) and \\(B\\) lie on the parabola \\(y = 3x^2 - 5x - 3\\). Therefore, the \\(y\\)-coordinates are:\n\n\\[\ny_1 = 3x_1^2 - 5x_1 - 3\n\\]\n\\[\ny_2 = 3x_2^2 - 5x_2 - 3\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(x_2 = -x_1\\) into the equation for \\(y_2\\), we get:\n\n\\[\ny_2 = 3(-x_1)^2 - 5(-x_1) - 3 = 3x_1^2 + 5x_1 - 3\n\\]\n\nUsing the condition \\(y_1 + y_2 = 0\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n(3x_1^2 - 5x_1 - 3) + (3x_1^2 + 5x_1 - 3) = 0\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we find:\n\n\\[\n6x_1^2 - 6 = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\n6x_1^2 = 6\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx_1^2 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(x_1 = 1\\) or \\(x_1 = -1\\). Consequently, \\(x_2 = -1\\) or \\(x_2 = 1\\).\n\nNow, we calculate the coordinates of \\(A\\) and \\(B\\):\n\n- If \\(x_1 = 1\\), then \\(x_2 = -1\\).\n  - \\(y_1 = 3(1)^2 - 5(1) - 3 = 3 - 5 - 3 = -5\\)\n  - \\(y_2 = 3(-1)^2 + 5(-1) - 3 = 3 - 5 - 3 = -5\\)\n\nThe coordinates of \\(A\\) and \\(B\\) are \\((1, -5)\\) and \\((-1, -5)\\).\n\nThe length of \\(\\overline{AB}\\) is calculated using the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nAB = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the coordinates:\n\n\\[\nAB = \\sqrt{((-1) - 1)^2 + ((-5) - (-5))^2} = \\sqrt{(-2)^2 + 0^2} = \\sqrt{4} = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, the square of the length of \\(\\overline{AB}\\) is:\n\n\\[\nAB^2 = 2^2 = 4\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the square of the length of \\(\\overline{AB}\\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To find a nonzero solution to the equation \\(\\sqrt{4c - 5c^2} = 0\\), we first set the expression inside the square root equal to zero:\n\n\\[ 4c - 5c^2 = 0. \\]\n\nWe can factor this equation:\n\n\\[ c(4 - 5c) = 0. \\]\n\nThis gives us two possible solutions:\n\n1. \\( c = 0 \\)\n2. \\( 4 - 5c = 0 \\)\n\nSince we are looking for a nonzero solution, we solve the second equation:\n\n\\[ 4 - 5c = 0 \\]\n\n\\[ 5c = 4 \\]\n\n\\[ c = \\frac{4}{5}. \\]\n\nThus, the nonzero solution to the equation is \\( c = \\frac{4}{5} \\).'
"If the stamp's offer price doubles every three years, we can calculate the future offer price by considering the number of three-year periods in 12 years. \n\nFirst, determine the number of three-year periods in 12 years:\n\\[ \\frac{12}{3} = 4 \\]\n\nSince the offer price doubles every three years, it will double 4 times in 12 years. \n\nThe current offer price is double the original price of \\$1.25, which is:\n\\[ 2 \\times 1.25 = \\$2.50 \\]\n\nNow, calculate the offer price after 12 more years by doubling the current offer price 4 times:\n\\[ 2.50 \\times 2^4 = 2.50 \\times 16 = \\$40.00 \\]\n\nTherefore, in 12 more years, Mike will be offered \\(\\boxed{40}\\) dollars for the stamp."

'To find the value of \\( k \\) such that points \\( A(9, 1) \\), \\( B(19, k) \\), and \\( C(7, 0) \\) are collinear, we need to ensure that the slopes between each pair of points are equal.\n\nFirst, calculate the slope between points \\( A(9, 1) \\) and \\( C(7, 0) \\):\n\n\\[\n\\text{slope of } AC = \\frac{0 - 1}{7 - 9} = \\frac{-1}{-2} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate the slope between points \\( A(9, 1) \\) and \\( B(19, k) \\):\n\n\\[\n\\text{slope of } AB = \\frac{k - 1}{19 - 9} = \\frac{k - 1}{10}\n\\]\n\nFor the points to be collinear, the slopes must be equal:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{k - 1}{10} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nCross-multiply to solve for \\( k \\):\n\n\\[\n2(k - 1) = 10\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2k - 2 = 10\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2k = 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\nk = 6\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( k \\) is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
'To simplify \\((x\\sqrt{x^3})^4\\), we first simplify the expression inside the parentheses.\n\nThe expression \\(x\\sqrt{x^3}\\) can be rewritten using the property of exponents for square roots: \\(\\sqrt{x^3} = x^{3/2}\\). Therefore, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[ x \\cdot x^{3/2} = x^{1} \\cdot x^{3/2} = x^{1 + 3/2} = x^{5/2}. \\]\n\nNow, we raise this expression to the fourth power:\n\n\\[ (x^{5/2})^4 = x^{(5/2) \\cdot 4} = x^{20/2} = x^{10}. \\]\n\nThus, the exponent of \\(x\\) in the simplified expression is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
"The relationship between pressure and volume for a gas at constant temperature is given by Boyle's Law, which states that the pressure of a gas is inversely proportional to its volume. Mathematically, this can be expressed as:\n\n\\[ P_1 V_1 = P_2 V_2 \\]\n\nwhere \\( P_1 \\) and \\( V_1 \\) are the initial pressure and volume, and \\( P_2 \\) and \\( V_2 \\) are the final pressure and volume.\n\nGiven:\n- Initial pressure, \\( P_1 = 4 \\) kPa\n- Initial volume, \\( V_1 = 3.67 \\) liters\n- Final volume, \\( V_2 = 1.835 \\) liters\n\nWe need to find the final pressure, \\( P_2 \\).\n\nUsing Boyle's Law:\n\n\\[ 4 \\, \\text{kPa} \\times 3.67 \\, \\text{liters} = P_2 \\times 1.835 \\, \\text{liters} \\]\n\nSolving for \\( P_2 \\):\n\n\\[ P_2 = \\frac{4 \\times 3.67}{1.835} \\]\n\n\\[ P_2 = \\frac{14.68}{1.835} \\]\n\n\\[ P_2 \\approx 8 \\, \\text{kPa} \\]\n\nTherefore, the new pressure in the 1.835 liter container is approximately 8 kPa."
'To find \\(\\left[f^{-1}(1)\\right]^{-1}\\), we first need to determine the inverse function \\(f^{-1}(x)\\) of \\(f(x) = \\frac{4x+1}{3}\\).\n\n1. Start by setting \\(y = f(x)\\):\n   \\[\n   y = \\frac{4x+1}{3}\n   \\]\n\n2. Solve for \\(x\\) in terms of \\(y\\):\n   \\[\n   3y = 4x + 1\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   4x = 3y - 1\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{3y - 1}{4}\n   \\]\n\n3. Thus, the inverse function is:\n   \\[\n   f^{-1}(x) = \\frac{3x - 1}{4}\n   \\]\n\nNext, we evaluate \\(f^{-1}(1)\\):\n\\[\nf^{-1}(1) = \\frac{3(1) - 1}{4} = \\frac{3 - 1}{4} = \\frac{2}{4} = \\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nFinally, we find \\(\\left[f^{-1}(1)\\right]^{-1}\\):\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^{-1} = 2\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\left[f^{-1}(1)\\right]^{-1}\\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the smallest integer \\( b > 2011 \\) such that the difference between the \\((b+1)^{th}\\) and \\(b^{th}\\) triangular numbers is itself a triangular number.\n\nThe formula for the \\(n^{th}\\) triangular number is given by:\n\n\\[\nT(n) = \\frac{n(n+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\nThe difference between the \\((b+1)^{th}\\) and \\(b^{th}\\) triangular numbers is:\n\n\\[\nT(b+1) - T(b) = \\frac{(b+1)(b+2)}{2} - \\frac{b(b+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying this expression, we have:\n\n\\[\nT(b+1) - T(b) = \\frac{(b+1)(b+2) - b(b+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{b^2 + 3b + 2 - b^2 - b}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{2b + 2}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n= b + 1\n\\]\n\nWe need \\( b + 1 \\) to be a triangular number, say \\( T(x) \\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nb + 1 = \\frac{x(x+1)}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{x(x+1)}{2} - 1\n\\]\n\nWe need to find the smallest \\( b > 2011 \\). Therefore, we solve:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x(x+1)}{2} - 1 > 2011\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x(x+1)}{2} > 2012\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx(x+1) > 4024\n\\]\n\nTo find the smallest \\( x \\), we solve the inequality:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x - 4024 > 0\n\\]\n\nUsing the quadratic formula to approximate the roots of \\( x^2 + x - 4024 = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 4 \\times 4024}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-1 \\pm \\sqrt{16097}}{2}\n\\]\n\nApproximating \\( \\sqrt{16097} \\approx 126.85 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\nx \\approx \\frac{-1 + 126.85}{2} \\approx 62.925\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x \\) must be an integer, we take \\( x = 63 \\).\n\nVerify:\n\n\\[\nx = 63 \\Rightarrow T(63) = \\frac{63 \\times 64}{2} = 2016\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( b + 1 = 2016 \\) and \\( b = 2015 \\).\n\nSince \\( b > 2011 \\), the smallest integer \\( b \\) satisfying the condition is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{2015}\n\\]'
"To find the sixth term of the arithmetic sequence, we first need to determine the common difference of the sequence. Let's denote the first term of the sequence as \\( a \\) and the common difference as \\( d \\).\n\nThe formula for the \\( n \\)-th term of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\\[\na_n = a + (n-1)d\n\\]\n\nGiven that the fourth term is 200, we have:\n\\[\na + 3d = 200\n\\]\n\nGiven that the eighth term is 500, we have:\n\\[\na + 7d = 500\n\\]\n\nWe now have a system of two equations:\n1. \\( a + 3d = 200 \\)\n2. \\( a + 7d = 500 \\)\n\nSubtract the first equation from the second to eliminate \\( a \\):\n\\[\n(a + 7d) - (a + 3d) = 500 - 200\n\\]\n\\[\n4d = 300\n\\]\n\\[\nd = 75\n\\]\n\nNow that we have the common difference, we can substitute \\( d = 75 \\) back into the first equation to find \\( a \\):\n\\[\na + 3(75) = 200\n\\]\n\\[\na + 225 = 200\n\\]\n\\[\na = 200 - 225\n\\]\n\\[\na = -25\n\\]\n\nNow, we can find the sixth term using the formula for the \\( n \\)-th term:\n\\[\na_6 = a + 5d\n\\]\n\\[\na_6 = -25 + 5(75)\n\\]\n\\[\na_6 = -25 + 375\n\\]\n\\[\na_6 = 350\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sixth term of the sequence is \\(\\boxed{350}\\)."
'To solve the quadratic equation \\(0 = -21x^2 - 11x + 40\\), we can use the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(a = -21\\), \\(b = -11\\), and \\(c = 40\\).\n\nFirst, calculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[\nb^2 - 4ac = (-11)^2 - 4(-21)(40) = 121 + 3360 = 3481\n\\]\n\nNext, find the square root of the discriminant:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{3481} = 59\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute the values into the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-(-11) \\pm 59}{2(-21)} = \\frac{11 \\pm 59}{-42}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two potential solutions:\n\n1. \\(x = \\frac{11 + 59}{-42} = \\frac{70}{-42} = -\\frac{10}{6} = -\\frac{5}{3}\\)\n\n2. \\(x = \\frac{11 - 59}{-42} = \\frac{-48}{-42} = \\frac{48}{42} = \\frac{8}{7}\\)\n\nSince we are looking for the solution where \\(x > 0\\), we choose:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{8}{7}\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{8}{7}}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\left(\\frac{1}{9}\\right)^x = 3^{x+3}\\), we start by expressing \\(\\frac{1}{9}\\) as a power of 3. We know that \\(9 = 3^2\\), so \\(\\frac{1}{9} = 3^{-2}\\). Therefore, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(3^{-2})^x = 3^{x+3}\n\\]\n\nUsing the property of exponents \\((a^m)^n = a^{mn}\\), we can rewrite the left side as:\n\n\\[\n3^{-2x} = 3^{x+3}\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we can set the exponents equal to each other:\n\n\\[\n-2x = x + 3\n\\]\n\nNow, solve for \\(x\\):\n\n1. Add \\(2x\\) to both sides:\n\n   \\[\n   0 = 3x + 3\n   \\]\n\n2. Subtract 3 from both sides:\n\n   \\[\n   -3 = 3x\n   \\]\n\n3. Divide both sides by 3:\n\n   \\[\n   x = -1\n   \\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{-1}\\).'
"To find the value of \\( x \\) that satisfies both equations, we need to solve the system of quadratic equations:\n\n1. \\( 9x^2 - 18x - 16 = 0 \\)\n2. \\( 15x^2 + 28x + 12 = 0 \\)\n\nFirst, let's solve the first equation:\n\n\\[ 9x^2 - 18x - 16 = 0 \\]\n\nWe can use the quadratic formula, \\( x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} \\), where \\( a = 9 \\), \\( b = -18 \\), and \\( c = -16 \\).\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[ b^2 - 4ac = (-18)^2 - 4 \\cdot 9 \\cdot (-16) = 324 + 576 = 900 \\]\n\nThe square root of 900 is 30. So, the solutions are:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{18 \\pm 30}{18} \\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{48}{18} = \\frac{8}{3} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-12}{18} = -\\frac{2}{3} \\]\n\nNext, let's solve the second equation:\n\n\\[ 15x^2 + 28x + 12 = 0 \\]\n\nAgain, use the quadratic formula, where \\( a = 15 \\), \\( b = 28 \\), and \\( c = 12 \\).\n\nCalculate the discriminant:\n\n\\[ b^2 - 4ac = 28^2 - 4 \\cdot 15 \\cdot 12 = 784 - 720 = 64 \\]\n\nThe square root of 64 is 8. So, the solutions are:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{-28 \\pm 8}{30} \\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{-20}{30} = -\\frac{2}{3} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-36}{30} = -\\frac{6}{5} \\]\n\nThe common solution to both equations is \\( x = -\\frac{2}{3} \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) is \\(\\boxed{-\\frac{2}{3}}\\)."
"To find the value of the product \\(xy\\), we need to solve the system of equations:\n\n1. \\(2x - 9y = 14\\)\n2. \\(6x = 42 + y\\)\n\nFirst, let's solve the second equation for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[ 6x = 42 + y \\]\n\nSubtract 42 from both sides:\n\n\\[ y = 6x - 42 \\]\n\nNow, substitute this expression for \\(y\\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[ 2x - 9(6x - 42) = 14 \\]\n\nDistribute the \\(-9\\):\n\n\\[ 2x - 54x + 378 = 14 \\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[ -52x + 378 = 14 \\]\n\nSubtract 378 from both sides:\n\n\\[ -52x = 14 - 378 \\]\n\n\\[ -52x = -364 \\]\n\nDivide both sides by \\(-52\\):\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{-364}{-52} = \\frac{364}{52} = \\frac{91}{13} \\]\n\nNow that we have \\(x\\), substitute it back into the expression for \\(y\\):\n\n\\[ y = 6x - 42 \\]\n\n\\[ y = 6\\left(\\frac{91}{13}\\right) - 42 \\]\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{546}{13} - 42 \\]\n\nConvert 42 to a fraction with a denominator of 13:\n\n\\[ 42 = \\frac{546}{13} \\]\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{546}{13} - \\frac{546}{13} = 0 \\]\n\nNow, we have \\(x = \\frac{91}{13}\\) and \\(y = 0\\).\n\nThe product \\(xy\\) is:\n\n\\[ xy = \\left(\\frac{91}{13}\\right)(0) = 0 \\]\n\nThus, the value of the product \\(xy\\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\)."
'To determine the values of \\( c \\) for which the quadratic equation \\( 3x^2 + 7x + c = 0 \\) has two real roots, we need to ensure that the discriminant of the quadratic is positive. The discriminant \\(\\Delta\\) of a quadratic equation \\( ax^2 + bx + c = 0 \\) is given by:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = b^2 - 4ac\n\\]\n\nFor the equation \\( 3x^2 + 7x + c = 0 \\), we have \\( a = 3 \\), \\( b = 7 \\), and \\( c = c \\). Thus, the discriminant is:\n\n\\[\n\\Delta = 7^2 - 4 \\cdot 3 \\cdot c = 49 - 12c\n\\]\n\nFor the quadratic to have two real roots, the discriminant must be positive:\n\n\\[\n49 - 12c > 0\n\\]\n\nSolving this inequality for \\( c \\), we get:\n\n\\[\n49 > 12c \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad c < \\frac{49}{12}\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\(\\frac{49}{12}\\), we find:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{49}{12} \\approx 4.0833\n\\]\n\nSince \\( c \\) must be a positive integer, the possible values for \\( c \\) are \\( 1, 2, 3, \\) and \\( 4 \\).\n\nNow, we find the product of these values:\n\n\\[\n1 \\times 2 \\times 3 \\times 4 = 24\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of all positive integer values of \\( c \\) such that the quadratic equation has two real roots is \\(\\boxed{24}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\frac{\\sqrt[3]{2x-4}}{\\sqrt[3]{x+4}} = 2\\), we start by letting \\(a = \\sqrt[3]{2x-4}\\) and \\(b = \\sqrt[3]{x+4}\\). The equation then becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} = 2\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\na = 2b\n\\]\n\nSubstituting back the expressions for \\(a\\) and \\(b\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt[3]{2x-4} = 2\\sqrt[3]{x+4}\n\\]\n\nCubing both sides to eliminate the cube roots, we get:\n\n\\[\n2x - 4 = (2\\sqrt[3]{x+4})^3\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the right side:\n\n\\[\n2x - 4 = 8(x+4)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side:\n\n\\[\n2x - 4 = 8x + 32\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms to solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n2x - 8x = 32 + 4\n\\]\n\n\\[\n-6x = 36\n\\]\n\nDividing both sides by \\(-6\\):\n\n\\[\nx = -6\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{-6}\\).'
'To solve the equation \\(\\sqrt{3x+6} = x+2\\), we start by squaring both sides to eliminate the square root:\n\n\\[\n(\\sqrt{3x+6})^2 = (x+2)^2\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3x + 6 = x^2 + 4x + 4\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation to bring all terms to one side:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + 4x + 4 - 3x - 6 = 0\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x - 2 = 0\n\\]\n\nNext, we factor the quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nx^2 + x - 2 = (x + 2)(x - 1) = 0\n\\]\n\nSetting each factor equal to zero gives the potential solutions:\n\n\\[\nx + 2 = 0 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = -2\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx - 1 = 0 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = 1\n\\]\n\nWe must check each solution in the original equation to ensure they are valid, as squaring both sides can introduce extraneous solutions.\n\n1. Check \\(x = -2\\):\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{3(-2) + 6} = \\sqrt{0} = 0\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx + 2 = -2 + 2 = 0\n\\]\n\nBoth sides are equal, so \\(x = -2\\) is a valid solution.\n\n2. Check \\(x = 1\\):\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{3(1) + 6} = \\sqrt{9} = 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx + 2 = 1 + 2 = 3\n\\]\n\nBoth sides are equal, so \\(x = 1\\) is also a valid solution.\n\nThus, the solutions to the equation are \\(-2\\) and \\(1\\). Ordered from least to greatest, the solutions are:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{-2, 1}\n\\]'
"To find the distance between the original midpoint \\( M \\) and the new midpoint \\( M' \\), we first need to determine the coordinates of both midpoints.\n\nThe original midpoint \\( M \\) between points \\( A(a, b) \\) and \\( B(c, d) \\) is given by:\n\\[\nM = \\left( \\frac{a+c}{2}, \\frac{b+d}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nAfter moving point \\( A \\) vertically upwards by 20 units and horizontally to the right by 14 units, the new coordinates of \\( A \\) are:\n\\[\nA' = (a+14, b+20)\n\\]\n\nAfter moving point \\( B \\) vertically downwards by 4 units and horizontally to the left by 2 units, the new coordinates of \\( B \\) are:\n\\[\nB' = (c-2, d-4)\n\\]\n\nThe new midpoint \\( M' \\) between points \\( A' \\) and \\( B' \\) is:\n\\[\nM' = \\left( \\frac{(a+14) + (c-2)}{2}, \\frac{(b+20) + (d-4)}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the coordinates of \\( M' \\):\n\\[\nM' = \\left( \\frac{a + c + 12}{2}, \\frac{b + d + 16}{2} \\right)\n\\]\n\nNow, we calculate the distance between \\( M \\) and \\( M' \\):\n\\[\n\\text{Distance} = \\sqrt{\\left( \\frac{a+c+12}{2} - \\frac{a+c}{2} \\right)^2 + \\left( \\frac{b+d+16}{2} - \\frac{b+d}{2} \\right)^2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expressions inside the square root:\n\\[\n\\frac{a+c+12}{2} - \\frac{a+c}{2} = \\frac{12}{2} = 6\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{b+d+16}{2} - \\frac{b+d}{2} = \\frac{16}{2} = 8\n\\]\n\nThus, the distance is:\n\\[\n\\sqrt{6^2 + 8^2} = \\sqrt{36 + 64} = \\sqrt{100} = 10\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the distance between \\( M \\) and \\( M' \\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\)."
'To find out how many criminals Wonder Woman can capture in \\(4\\frac{1}{2}\\) hours, we first convert the mixed number into an improper fraction or a decimal. \n\n\\[ 4\\frac{1}{2} = 4 + \\frac{1}{2} = \\frac{9}{2} \\]\n\nWonder Woman captures 6 criminals in 1 hour. Therefore, in \\(\\frac{9}{2}\\) hours, she can capture:\n\n\\[ 6 \\times \\frac{9}{2} = \\frac{54}{2} = 27 \\]\n\nSo, Wonder Woman can capture 27 criminals in \\(4\\frac{1}{2}\\) hours.'
'To find the value of \\(3 \\ast 10\\) using the operation defined by \\(a \\ast b = 2a + 5b - ab\\), we substitute \\(a = 3\\) and \\(b = 10\\) into the expression:\n\n\\[\n3 \\ast 10 = 2(3) + 5(10) - (3)(10)\n\\]\n\nCalculating each term separately:\n\n- \\(2(3) = 6\\)\n- \\(5(10) = 50\\)\n- \\(3(10) = 30\\)\n\nSubstituting these values back into the expression, we have:\n\n\\[\n3 \\ast 10 = 6 + 50 - 30\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the expression:\n\n\\[\n3 \\ast 10 = 56 - 30 = 26\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(3 \\ast 10\\) is \\(\\boxed{26}\\).'
'To determine the degree of the polynomial \\( f(x) \\), we need to consider the degree of the product \\((x-1) \\cdot f(x)\\).\n\nThe given polynomial on the right-hand side is \\(3x^4 + x^3 - 25x^2 + 38x - 17\\), which is a polynomial of degree 4.\n\nSince \\((x-1)\\) is a polynomial of degree 1, and the product \\((x-1) \\cdot f(x)\\) is of degree 4, the degree of \\( f(x) \\) must be one less than the degree of the product. This is because multiplying a polynomial of degree \\( n \\) by a linear polynomial (degree 1) results in a polynomial of degree \\( n+1 \\).\n\nTherefore, the degree of \\( f(x) \\) is \\( 4 - 1 = 3 \\).\n\nThe degree of \\( f \\) is \\(\\boxed{3}\\).'
'To find \\(2x^2 + 2y^2\\), we start by solving the system of equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 3\n\\]\n\\[\nx - y = 4\n\\]\n\nWe can add these two equations to eliminate \\(y\\):\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 3 + 4\n\\]\n\\[\n2x = 7\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{7}{2}\n\\]\n\nNext, we substitute \\(x = \\frac{7}{2}\\) back into the equation \\(x + y = 3\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{7}{2} + y = 3\n\\]\n\nSubtract \\(\\frac{7}{2}\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\ny = 3 - \\frac{7}{2} = \\frac{6}{2} - \\frac{7}{2} = -\\frac{1}{2}\n\\]\n\nNow, we have \\(x = \\frac{7}{2}\\) and \\(y = -\\frac{1}{2}\\). We need to find \\(2x^2 + 2y^2\\):\n\n\\[\n2x^2 + 2y^2 = 2\\left(\\left(\\frac{7}{2}\\right)^2\\right) + 2\\left(\\left(-\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2\\right)\n\\]\n\nCalculate each square:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{7}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{49}{4}\n\\]\n\\[\n\\left(-\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{1}{4}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute these back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n2x^2 + 2y^2 = 2\\left(\\frac{49}{4}\\right) + 2\\left(\\frac{1}{4}\\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{98}{4} + \\frac{2}{4}\n\\]\n\\[\n= \\frac{100}{4}\n\\]\n\\[\n= 25\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(2x^2 + 2y^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{25}\\).'
'To find \\(\\text{D}(2,4,6)\\), we use the given formula:\n\n\\[\n\\text{D}(a,b,c) = \\frac{abc}{a+b+c}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 4\\), and \\(c = 6\\) into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\text{D}(2,4,6) = \\frac{2 \\cdot 4 \\cdot 6}{2 + 4 + 6}\n\\]\n\nFirst, calculate the product in the numerator:\n\n\\[\n2 \\cdot 4 \\cdot 6 = 48\n\\]\n\nNext, calculate the sum in the denominator:\n\n\\[\n2 + 4 + 6 = 12\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these values back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\text{D}(2,4,6) = \\frac{48}{12}\n\\]\n\nFinally, perform the division:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{48}{12} = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(\\text{D}(2,4,6) = \\boxed{4}\\).'
'To solve for \\( b \\) in the equation \\( 5^b + 5^b + 5^b + 5^b + 5^b = 625^{(b-1)} \\), we start by simplifying the left side of the equation. Notice that there are five terms of \\( 5^b \\), so we can factor this as:\n\n\\[\n5 \\times 5^b = 5^{b+1}\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n5^{b+1} = 625^{(b-1)}\n\\]\n\nNext, we express 625 as a power of 5. We know that:\n\n\\[\n625 = 5^4\n\\]\n\nTherefore, we can rewrite \\( 625^{(b-1)} \\) as:\n\n\\[\n(5^4)^{(b-1)} = 5^{4(b-1)}\n\\]\n\nNow, the equation is:\n\n\\[\n5^{b+1} = 5^{4(b-1)}\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we equate the exponents:\n\n\\[\nb+1 = 4(b-1)\n\\]\n\nExpanding the right side, we have:\n\n\\[\nb+1 = 4b - 4\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( b \\), we rearrange the terms:\n\n\\[\nb + 1 = 4b - 4\n\\]\n\nSubtract \\( b \\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\n1 = 3b - 4\n\\]\n\nAdd 4 to both sides:\n\n\\[\n5 = 3b\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 3:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{5}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( b \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{5}{3}}\\).'
'To find the common difference of the arithmetic series, we can use the formula for the sum of an arithmetic series:\n\n\\[\nS_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\left(2a + (n-1)d\\right)\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( S_n \\) is the sum of the series, \\( n \\) is the number of terms, \\( a \\) is the first term, and \\( d \\) is the common difference.\n\nGiven:\n- \\( S_{15} = -210 \\)\n- \\( n = 15 \\)\n- \\( a = 7 \\)\n\nSubstitute these values into the formula:\n\n\\[\n-210 = \\frac{15}{2} \\left(2 \\times 7 + (15-1)d\\right)\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n-210 = \\frac{15}{2} \\left(14 + 14d\\right)\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 2 to eliminate the fraction:\n\n\\[\n-420 = 15(14 + 14d)\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 15:\n\n\\[\n-28 = 14 + 14d\n\\]\n\nSubtract 14 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n-42 = 14d\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 14:\n\n\\[\nd = -3\n\\]\n\nThus, the common difference is \\(\\boxed{-3}\\).'
'To find the value of the expression \\(2x^2 + 3x + 4\\) given \\(x = -2\\), we substitute \\(-2\\) for \\(x\\) in the expression:\n\n\\[\n2(-2)^2 + 3(-2) + 4\n\\]\n\nFirst, calculate \\((-2)^2\\):\n\n\\[\n(-2)^2 = 4\n\\]\n\nNow substitute back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n2(4) + 3(-2) + 4\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\n\\[\n2 \\times 4 = 8\n\\]\n\\[\n3 \\times (-2) = -6\n\\]\n\nNow add these results together:\n\n\\[\n8 - 6 + 4\n\\]\n\nCalculate the sum:\n\n\\[\n8 - 6 = 2\n\\]\n\\[\n2 + 4 = 6\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
'To find the sum of all the odd integers between 500 and 700, we first identify the smallest and largest odd integers in this range.\n\nThe smallest odd integer greater than 500 is 501, and the largest odd integer less than 700 is 699.\n\nThe sequence of odd integers from 501 to 699 is an arithmetic sequence where the first term \\( a_1 = 501 \\), the last term \\( a_n = 699 \\), and the common difference \\( d = 2 \\).\n\nTo find the number of terms \\( n \\) in this sequence, we use the formula for the \\( n \\)-th term of an arithmetic sequence:\n\n\\[\na_n = a_1 + (n-1) \\cdot d\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[\n699 = 501 + (n-1) \\cdot 2\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( n \\):\n\n\\[\n699 = 501 + 2n - 2\n\\]\n\\[\n699 = 499 + 2n\n\\]\n\\[\n200 = 2n\n\\]\n\\[\nn = 100\n\\]\n\nThere are 100 terms in this sequence. The sum \\( S_n \\) of an arithmetic sequence is given by:\n\n\\[\nS_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\cdot (a_1 + a_n)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the known values:\n\n\\[\nS_{100} = \\frac{100}{2} \\cdot (501 + 699)\n\\]\n\\[\nS_{100} = 50 \\cdot 1200\n\\]\n\\[\nS_{100} = 60000\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of all the odd integers between 500 and 700 is \\(\\boxed{60000}\\).'
"Let the two prime numbers be \\( p \\) and \\( q \\). Since they are roots of the quadratic equation \\( x^2 - 12x + k = 0 \\), by Vieta's formulas, we have:\n\n1. \\( p + q = 12 \\)\n2. \\( pq = k \\)\n\nWe need to find two prime numbers whose sum is 12. The possible pairs of prime numbers are:\n\n- \\( (5, 7) \\)\n- \\( (7, 5) \\)\n\nBoth pairs satisfy the condition \\( p + q = 12 \\).\n\nNow, we calculate \\( k = pq \\):\n\nFor the pair \\( (5, 7) \\):\n\n\\[\npq = 5 \\times 7 = 35\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( k \\) is \\(\\boxed{35}\\)."
'To determine the value of \\( c \\) such that \\( x^2 + cx + 9c \\) is the square of a binomial, we need to express it in the form \\((x + a)^2\\).\n\nExpanding \\((x + a)^2\\), we get:\n\\[\n(x + a)^2 = x^2 + 2ax + a^2\n\\]\n\nComparing this with \\( x^2 + cx + 9c \\), we equate the coefficients:\n1. The coefficient of \\( x \\) gives us \\( 2a = c \\).\n2. The constant term gives us \\( a^2 = 9c \\).\n\nFrom the first equation, we have \\( a = \\frac{c}{2} \\).\n\nSubstitute \\( a = \\frac{c}{2} \\) into the second equation:\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{c}{2}\\right)^2 = 9c\n\\]\n\\[\n\\frac{c^2}{4} = 9c\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 4 to clear the fraction:\n\\[\nc^2 = 36c\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\\[\nc^2 - 36c = 0\n\\]\n\nFactor out \\( c \\):\n\\[\nc(c - 36) = 0\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two solutions:\n1. \\( c = 0 \\)\n2. \\( c = 36 \\)\n\nSince \\( c \\) is a nonzero constant, we discard \\( c = 0 \\) and are left with \\( c = 36 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( c \\) is \\(\\boxed{36}\\).'

'Let \\( d \\) be the number of dimes and \\( n \\) be the number of nickels. We have two equations based on the problem statement:\n\n1. The total number of coins is 11:\n   \\[\n   d + n = 11\n   \\]\n\n2. The total value of the coins is 75 cents. Since dimes are worth 10 cents and nickels are worth 5 cents, we have:\n   \\[\n   10d + 5n = 75\n   \\]\n\nWe can simplify the second equation by dividing everything by 5:\n\\[\n2d + n = 15\n\\]\n\nNow, we have the system of equations:\n\\[\n\\begin{align*}\nd + n &= 11 \\\\\n2d + n &= 15\n\\end{align*}\n\\]\n\nSubtract the first equation from the second equation to eliminate \\( n \\):\n\\[\n(2d + n) - (d + n) = 15 - 11\n\\]\n\\[\n2d + n - d - n = 4\n\\]\n\\[\nd = 4\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( d = 4 \\) back into the first equation:\n\\[\n4 + n = 11\n\\]\n\\[\nn = 7\n\\]\n\nTherefore, Hillary has \\(\\boxed{7}\\) nickels.'
'To find the value of \\( K \\), we need to determine the equation of the line parallel to \\( 3x - 7y = 65 \\) that passes through the point \\( (7, 4) \\).\n\nFirst, we find the slope of the given line \\( 3x - 7y = 65 \\). We can rewrite it in slope-intercept form \\( y = mx + b \\) by solving for \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n3x - 7y = 65 \\implies -7y = -3x + 65 \\implies y = \\frac{3}{7}x - \\frac{65}{7}\n\\]\n\nThe slope \\( m \\) of the line is \\( \\frac{3}{7} \\).\n\nSince parallel lines have the same slope, the line we are looking for also has a slope of \\( \\frac{3}{7} \\).\n\nUsing the point-slope form of a line equation, \\( y - y_1 = m(x - x_1) \\), where \\( (x_1, y_1) = (7, 4) \\), we have:\n\n\\[\ny - 4 = \\frac{3}{7}(x - 7)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\n\\[\ny - 4 = \\frac{3}{7}x - \\frac{21}{7}\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny - 4 = \\frac{3}{7}x - 3\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{3}{7}x + 1\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find the y-intercept \\( K \\) of this line, which occurs when \\( x = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{3}{7}(0) + 1 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( K \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'To find the $x$-intercept, set \\( y = 0 \\) in the equation \\(\\frac{x}{4} + \\frac{y}{12} = 1\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x}{4} = 1 \\implies x = 4\n\\]\n\nSo, the $x$-intercept \\( a = 4 \\).\n\nTo find the $y$-intercept, set \\( x = 0 \\) in the equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{y}{12} = 1 \\implies y = 12\n\\]\n\nSo, the $y$-intercept \\( b = 12 \\).\n\nNext, we find the slope \\( m \\) of the line. First, rewrite the equation in slope-intercept form \\( y = mx + c \\). Start by clearing the fractions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x}{4} + \\frac{y}{12} = 1 \\implies 3x + y = 12\n\\]\n\nRearrange to solve for \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\ny = -3x + 12\n\\]\n\nThus, the slope \\( m = -3 \\).\n\nNow, calculate \\( a + b + m \\):\n\n\\[\na + b + m = 4 + 12 - 3 = 13\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( a + b + m \\) is \\(\\boxed{13}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( c \\) that makes the radius of the circle equal to 1, we first need to rewrite the given equation of the circle in standard form. The equation is:\n\n\\[ x^2 - 10x + y^2 + 6y + c = 0. \\]\n\nWe complete the square for both the \\( x \\) and \\( y \\) terms.\n\n1. For the \\( x \\) terms: \\( x^2 - 10x \\).\n\n   - Take half of the coefficient of \\( x \\), which is \\(-10\\), and square it: \\(\\left(\\frac{-10}{2}\\right)^2 = 25\\).\n   - Add and subtract 25: \\( x^2 - 10x = (x - 5)^2 - 25 \\).\n\n2. For the \\( y \\) terms: \\( y^2 + 6y \\).\n\n   - Take half of the coefficient of \\( y \\), which is \\(6\\), and square it: \\(\\left(\\frac{6}{2}\\right)^2 = 9\\).\n   - Add and subtract 9: \\( y^2 + 6y = (y + 3)^2 - 9 \\).\n\nSubstitute these into the original equation:\n\n\\[ (x - 5)^2 - 25 + (y + 3)^2 - 9 + c = 0. \\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[ (x - 5)^2 + (y + 3)^2 - 34 + c = 0. \\]\n\nRearrange to the standard form of a circle:\n\n\\[ (x - 5)^2 + (y + 3)^2 = 34 - c. \\]\n\nThe standard form of a circle is \\((x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2\\), where \\( r \\) is the radius. We want the radius to be 1, so:\n\n\\[ r^2 = 1. \\]\n\nThus, we have:\n\n\\[ 34 - c = 1. \\]\n\nSolving for \\( c \\):\n\n\\[ c = 34 - 1 = 33. \\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( c \\) that makes the radius of the circle equal to 1 is \\(\\boxed{33}\\).'

According to the problem, the combined weight of the three dogs is 185 pounds. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n\n\\[\nx + x + (x + 20) = 185\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the equation, we have:\n\n\\[\n3x + 20 = 185\n\\]\n\nSubtract 20 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n3x = 165\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 3:\n\n\\[\nx = 55\n\\]\n\nThus, the weight of the largest dog is:\n\n\\[\nx + 20 = 55 + 20 = 75\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the largest dog weighs \\(\\boxed{75}\\) pounds.'
'To find the function \\( k(x) \\) such that \\( f \\) is its own inverse, we need to ensure that \\( f(f(x)) = x \\) for all \\( x \\) in the domain of \\( f \\).\n\nGiven:\n\\[ f(x) =\n\\begin{cases}\nk(x) & \\text{if } x > 2, \\\\\n2 + (x-2)^2 & \\text{if } x \\leq 2.\n\\end{cases}\n\\]\n\n1. **Case 1: \\( x \\leq 2 \\)**\n\n   For \\( x \\leq 2 \\), \\( f(x) = 2 + (x-2)^2 \\).\n\n   We need \\( f(f(x)) = x \\). So, we substitute \\( f(x) \\) into itself:\n   \\[\n   f(f(x)) = f(2 + (x-2)^2).\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\( 2 + (x-2)^2 \\geq 2 \\) for all \\( x \\leq 2 \\), we use the second case of \\( f \\):\n   \\[\n   f(2 + (x-2)^2) = 2 + ((2 + (x-2)^2) - 2)^2 = 2 + ((x-2)^2)^2.\n   \\]\n\n   For \\( f(f(x)) = x \\), we need:\n   \\[\n   2 + ((x-2)^2)^2 = x.\n   \\]\n\n   Solving this equation is complex, and it suggests that \\( k(x) \\) must be chosen to simplify this process.\n\n2. **Case 2: \\( x > 2 \\)**\n\n   For \\( x > 2 \\), \\( f(x) = k(x) \\).\n\n   We need \\( f(f(x)) = x \\). So, we substitute \\( f(x) \\) into itself:\n   \\[\n   f(f(x)) = f(k(x)).\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\( k(x) > 2 \\) for \\( x > 2 \\), we use the first case of \\( f \\):\n   \\[\n   f(k(x)) = k(k(x)).\n   \\]\n\n   For \\( f(f(x)) = x \\), we need:\n   \\[\n   k(k(x)) = x.\n   \\]\n\n   This implies that \\( k(x) \\) must be the inverse of itself for \\( x > 2 \\).\n\nTo satisfy both cases, we need \\( k(x) \\) such that:\n- \\( k(k(x)) = x \\) for \\( x > 2 \\).\n- \\( f(f(x)) = x \\) for \\( x \\leq 2 \\).\n\nA simple choice for \\( k(x) \\) is a linear function that is its own inverse, such as \\( k(x) = 4 - x \\). This choice satisfies \\( k(k(x)) = x \\) because:\n\\[\nk(k(x)) = k(4 - x) = 4 - (4 - x) = x.\n\\]\n\nThus, the function \\( k(x) \\) that makes \\( f \\) its own inverse is:\n\\[ k(x) = 4 - x. \\]'
'Let the two positive integers be \\( x \\) and \\( y \\). We are given that the sum of their product and their sum is 454:\n\n\\[\nxy + x + y = 454\n\\]\n\nWe want to find the largest possible value of the product of their sum and their product, which is:\n\n\\[\n(x+y)(xy)\n\\]\n\nTo solve this, we can rewrite the given equation by adding 1 to both sides:\n\n\\[\nxy + x + y + 1 = 455\n\\]\n\nThis can be factored as:\n\n\\[\n(x+1)(y+1) = 455\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find pairs \\((x+1, y+1)\\) such that their product is 455. The factor pairs of 455 are:\n\n\\[\n1 \\times 455, \\quad 5 \\times 91, \\quad 7 \\times 65, \\quad 13 \\times 35\n\\]\n\nFor each factor pair \\((a, b)\\), we have \\(x = a-1\\) and \\(y = b-1\\). We calculate the product \\((x+y)(xy)\\) for each pair:\n\n1. For \\((x+1, y+1) = (1, 455)\\), we have \\(x = 0\\), \\(y = 454\\):\n   \\[\n   (x+y) = 454, \\quad xy = 0 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad (x+y)(xy) = 0\n   \\]\n\n2. For \\((x+1, y+1) = (5, 91)\\), we have \\(x = 4\\), \\(y = 90\\):\n   \\[\n   (x+y) = 94, \\quad xy = 360 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad (x+y)(xy) = 94 \\times 360 = 33840\n   \\]\n\n3. 'To find the \\( y \\)-coordinate of the point where the line intersects the \\( y \\)-axis, we first need to determine the equation of the line passing through the points \\((-2, 6)\\) and \\((-4, -2)\\).\n\n1. **Calculate the slope (\\( m \\)) of the line:**\n\n   The formula for the slope \\( m \\) between two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is:\n   \\[\n   m = \\frac{y_2 - y_1}{x_2 - x_1}\n   \\]\n\n   Substituting the given points \\((-2, 6)\\) and \\((-4, -2)\\):\n   \\[\n   m = \\frac{-2 - 6}{-4 - (-2)} = \\frac{-8}{-2} = 4\n   \\]\n\n2. **Use the point-slope form to find the equation of the line:**\n\n   The point-slope form of a line is:\n   \\[\n   y - y_1 = m(x - x_1)\n   \\]\n\n   Using the point \\((-2, 6)\\) and the slope \\( m = 4 \\):\n   \\[\n   y - 6 = 4(x + 2)\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying:\n   \\[\n   y - 6 = 4x + 8\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   y = 4x + 14\n   \\]\n\n3. **Find the \\( y \\)-intercept:**\n\n   The \\( y \\)-intercept occurs where \\( x = 0 \\). Substitute \\( x = 0 \\) into the equation:\n   \\[\n   y = 4(0) + 14 = 14\n   \\]\n\nThus, the \\( y \\)-coordinate of the point where the line intersects the \\( y \\)-axis is \\(\\boxed{14}\\).'

"To find the amount in Alan's bank account after 10 years with annual compounding interest, we use the formula for compound interest:\n\n\\[ A = P \\left(1 + \\frac{r}{n}\\right)^{nt} \\]\n\nwhere:\n- \\( A \\) is the amount of money accumulated after n years, including interest.\n- \\( P \\) is the principal amount (initial investment), which is $500.\n- \\( r \\) is the annual interest rate (decimal), which is 0.03 for 3%.\n- \\( n \\) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year, which is 1 for annual compounding.\n- \\( t \\) is the number of years the money is invested for, which is 10.\n\nPlugging in the values, we get:\n\n\\[ A = 500 \\left(1 + \\frac{0.03}{1}\\right)^{1 \\times 10} \\]\n\\[ A = 500 \\left(1.03\\right)^{10} \\]\n\nNow, calculate \\( (1.03)^{10} \\):\n\n\\[ (1.03)^{10} \\approx 1.34391638 \\]\n\nThen, calculate \\( A \\):\n\n\\[ A \\approx 500 \\times 1.34391638 \\]\n\\[ A \\approx 671.95819 \\]\n\nRounding to the nearest dollar, the amount in Alan's bank account after 10 years is approximately \\(\\boxed{672}\\) dollars."

"To determine how many different values are represented by the given quantities, we need to evaluate each expression:\n\n1. \\(3^{-2}\\):\n   \\[\n   3^{-2} = \\frac{1}{3^2} = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\n2. \\(9^{-2}\\):\n   \\[\n   9^{-2} = \\left(3^2\\right)^{-2} = 3^{-4} = \\frac{1}{3^4} = \\frac{1}{81}\n   \\]\n\n3. \\(27^{-\\frac{2}{3}}\\):\n   \\[\n   27^{-\\frac{2}{3}} = \\left(3^3\\right)^{-\\frac{2}{3}} = 3^{-2} = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\n4. \\(9 \\cdot 81^{-1}\\):\n   \\[\n   81^{-1} = \\frac{1}{81} = \\left(3^4\\right)^{-1} = 3^{-4}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   9 \\cdot 81^{-1} = 9 \\cdot \\frac{1}{81} = \\frac{9}{81} = \\frac{1}{9}\n   \\]\n\n5. \\(243^{-\\frac{4}{5}}\\):\n   \\[\n   243 = 3^5\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   243^{-\\frac{4}{5}} = \\left(3^5\\right)^{-\\frac{4}{5}} = 3^{-4} = \\frac{1}{81}\n   \\]\n\nNow, let's list the values we have found:\n- \\(3^{-2} = \\frac{1}{9}\\)\n- \\(9^{-2} = \\frac{1}{81}\\)\n- \\(27^{-\\frac{2}{3}} = \\frac{1}{9}\\)\n- \\(9 \\cdot 81^{-1} = \\frac{1}{9}\\)\n- \\(243^{-\\frac{4}{5}} = \\frac{1}{81}\\)\n\nThe distinct values are \\(\\frac{1}{9}\\) and \\(\\frac{1}{81}\\).\n\nTherefore, there are \\(\\boxed{2}\\) different values represented by the given quantities."
'To rationalize the denominator of \\(\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{2}+\\sqrt{8}+\\sqrt{32}}\\), we first simplify the terms in the denominator:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{8} = \\sqrt{4 \\times 2} = 2\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{32} = \\sqrt{16 \\times 2} = 4\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the denominator becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\sqrt{2} + 2\\sqrt{2} + 4\\sqrt{2} = 7\\sqrt{2}\n\\]\n\nThe expression is now:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{7\\sqrt{2}}\n\\]\n\nTo rationalize the denominator, multiply the numerator and the denominator by \\(\\sqrt{2}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1 \\cdot \\sqrt{2}}{7\\sqrt{2} \\cdot \\sqrt{2}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{14}\n\\]\n\nThe expression \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{14}\\) is in the form \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{A}}{B}\\) where \\(A = 2\\) and \\(B = 14\\). "Let the first term of the arithmetic sequence be \\( a \\) and the common difference be \\( d \\). The terms of the sequence can be expressed as follows:\n\n- First term: \\( a \\)\n- Second term: \\( a + d \\)\n- Third term: \\( a + 2d \\)\n- Fourth term: \\( a + 3d \\)\n\nWe are given that the product of the first and third terms is 5:\n\n\\[\na(a + 2d) = 5\n\\]\n\nSince all terms are positive integers, we need to find integer solutions for \\( a \\) and \\( a + 2d \\) such that their product is 5. The possible pairs \\((a, a + 2d)\\) that satisfy this condition are:\n\n- \\( (1, 5) \\)\n- \\( (5, 1) \\)\n\nLet's consider each case:\n\n1. **Case 1: \\( a = 1 \\) and \\( a + 2d = 5 \\)**\n\n   \\[\n   a + 2d = 5 \\implies 1 + 2d = 5 \\implies 2d = 4 \\implies d = 2\n   \\]\n\n   The sequence is: \\( 1, 3, 5, 7, \\ldots \\)\n\n   The fourth term is \\( a + 3d = 1 + 3 \\times 2 = 7 \\).\n\n2. **Case 2: \\( a = 5 \\) and \\( a + 2d = 1 \\)**\n\n   \\[\n   a + 2d = 1 \\implies 5 + 2d = 1 \\implies 2d = -4 \\implies d = -2\n   \\]\n\n   The sequence is: \\( 5, 3, 1, -1, \\ldots \\)\n\n   The fourth term is \\( a + 3d = 5 + 3 \\times (-2) = -1 \\).\n\nSince all terms must be positive integers, the second case is not valid. Therefore, the only valid sequence is from the first case, and the fourth term is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{7}\n\\]"
'To find the height of the plant two weeks ago, we need to determine its height 14 days ago, given that it grows by 5% each day. \n\nLet \\( h \\) be the height of the plant 14 days ago. The height of the plant today is 452 cm, and it grows by 5% each day, which means it multiplies by a factor of 1.05 each day. Therefore, the relationship between the height 14 days ago and today is given by:\n\n\\[\nh \\times (1.05)^{14} = 452\n\\]\n\nTo find \\( h \\), we solve for it by dividing both sides by \\( (1.05)^{14} \\):\n\n\\[\nh = \\frac{452}{(1.05)^{14}}\n\\]\n\nNow, we calculate \\( (1.05)^{14} \\):\n\n\\[\n(1.05)^{14} \\approx 1.979\n\\]\n\nUsing this approximation, we find \\( h \\):\n\n\\[\nh \\approx \\frac{452}{1.979} \\approx 228.4\n\\]\n\nThus, the height of the plant two weeks ago was approximately \\( \\boxed{228.4} \\) centimeters.'
'To find the value of \\( x \\) that gives the minimum value for the quadratic expression \\( 9x^2 + 18x + 7 \\), we can use the formula for the vertex of a parabola. The expression is a quadratic in the form \\( ax^2 + bx + c \\), where \\( a = 9 \\), \\( b = 18 \\), and \\( c = 7 \\).\n\nThe \\( x \\)-coordinate of the vertex, which gives the minimum value for a parabola that opens upwards (since \\( a > 0 \\)), is given by the formula:\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{b}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values of \\( a \\) and \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{18}{2 \\times 9} = -\\frac{18}{18} = -1\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( x \\) that gives the minimum value for the expression \\( 9x^2 + 18x + 7 \\) is \\( x = -1 \\).'
"Let the two-digit integer be represented as \\(10a + b\\), where \\(a\\) is the tens digit and \\(b\\) is the units digit. According to the problem, the product of the digits is one-half of the integer:\n\n\\[\nab = \\frac{1}{2}(10a + b)\n\\]\n\nMultiplying both sides by 2 to eliminate the fraction, we get:\n\n\\[\n2ab = 10a + b\n\\]\n\nRearranging terms, we have:\n\n\\[\n2ab - b = 10a\n\\]\n\nFactoring out \\(b\\) from the left side:\n\n\\[\nb(2a - 1) = 10a\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(b\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nb = \\frac{10a}{2a - 1}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(b\\) must be a digit (an integer between 0 and 9), \\(\\frac{10a}{2a - 1}\\) must be an integer. We will test integer values of \\(a\\) from 1 to 9 to find the smallest two-digit integer.\n\n- For \\(a = 1\\):\n  \\[\n  b = \\frac{10 \\times 1}{2 \\times 1 - 1} = \\frac{10}{1} = 10 \\quad (\\text{not a valid digit})\n  \\]\n\n- For \\(a = 2\\):\n  \\[\n  b = \\frac{10 \\times 2}{2 \\times 2 - 1} = \\frac{20}{3} \\quad (\\text{not an integer})\n  \\]\n\n- For \\(a = 3\\):\n  \\[\n  b = \\frac{10 \\times 3}{2 \\times 3 - 1} = \\frac{30}{5} = 6\n  \\]\n\n  Here, \\(b = 6\\) is a valid digit. Thus, the integer is \\(10a + b = 10 \\times 3 + 6 = 36\\).\n\nLet's verify:\n\nThe product of the digits is \\(3 \\times 6 = 18\\), and one-half of the integer is \\(\\frac{36}{2} = 18\\). The condition is satisfied.\n\nTherefore, the smallest two-digit positive integer such that the product of its two digits is one-half the integer is \\(\\boxed{36}\\)."
'To find the intersection point \\( A \\) of the lines \\( 3y = x \\) and \\( 2x + 5y = 11 \\), we need to solve the system of equations:\n\n1. \\( 3y = x \\)\n2. \\( 2x + 5y = 11 \\)\n\nFirst, substitute \\( x = 3y \\) from the first equation into the second equation:\n\n\\[\n2(3y) + 5y = 11\n\\]\n\nSimplify and solve for \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\n6y + 5y = 11\n\\]\n\\[\n11y = 11\n\\]\n\\[\ny = 1\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( y = 1 \\) back into the equation \\( x = 3y \\) to find \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx = 3(1) = 3\n\\]\n\nThus, the coordinates of point \\( A \\) are \\( (3, 1) \\).\n\nThe sum of the coordinates of point \\( A \\) is:\n\n\\[\n3 + 1 = 4\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum of the coordinates of point \\( A \\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'
'To solve for \\( r^s \\cdot t \\), we start by simplifying the given expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^{r-2} \\cdot y^{2s} \\cdot z^{3t+1}}{x^{2r} \\cdot y^{s-4} \\cdot z^{2t-3}}\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten by subtracting the exponents of like bases:\n\n\\[\nx^{(r-2) - 2r} \\cdot y^{2s - (s-4)} \\cdot z^{(3t+1) - (2t-3)}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying each exponent, we have:\n\n- For \\( x \\): \\((r-2) - 2r = r - 2 - 2r = -r - 2\\)\n- For \\( y \\): \\(2s - (s-4) = 2s - s + 4 = s + 4\\)\n- For \\( z \\): \\((3t+1) - (2t-3) = 3t + 1 - 2t + 3 = t + 4\\)\n\nThus, the expression simplifies to:\n\n\\[\nx^{-r-2} \\cdot y^{s+4} \\cdot z^{t+4}\n\\]\n\nWe are given that this equals \\( xyz \\), which can be expressed as:\n\n\\[\nx^1 \\cdot y^1 \\cdot z^1\n\\]\n\nBy equating the exponents of corresponding bases, we get the following system of equations:\n\n1. \\(-r - 2 = 1\\)\n2. \\(s + 4 = 1\\)\n3. \\(t + 4 = 1\\)\n\nSolving these equations:\n\n1. \\(-r - 2 = 1 \\implies -r = 3 \\implies r = -3\\)\n2. \\(s + 4 = 1 \\implies s = 1 - 4 = -3\\)\n3. \\(t + 4 = 1 \\implies t = 1 - 4 = -3\\)\n\nNow, we need to find \\( r^s \\cdot t \\):\n\n\\[\nr^s \\cdot t = (-3)^{-3} \\cdot (-3)\n\\]\n\nCalculating \\( (-3)^{-3} \\):\n\n\\[\n(-3)^{-3} = \\frac{1}{(-3)^3} = \\frac{1}{-27} = -\\frac{1}{27}\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\nr^s \\cdot t = -\\frac{1}{27} \\cdot (-3) = \\frac{3}{27} = \\frac{1}{9}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( r^s \\cdot t \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{9}}\\).'
'To solve for \\( x \\) in the equation \\((2^{x+1})^3 \\cdot 4^x = 8192\\), we start by simplifying the expression.\n\nFirst, note that \\( 4^x = (2^2)^x = 2^{2x} \\). Therefore, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n(2^{x+1})^3 \\cdot 2^{2x} = 8192\n\\]\n\nSimplifying \\((2^{x+1})^3\\), we have:\n\n\\[\n(2^{x+1})^3 = 2^{3(x+1)} = 2^{3x+3}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting back, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n2^{3x+3} \\cdot 2^{2x} = 8192\n\\]\n\nCombine the exponents on the left side:\n\n\\[\n2^{3x+3 + 2x} = 8192\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n2^{5x+3} = 8192\n\\]\n\nNext, express 8192 as a power of 2. We find that:\n\n\\[\n8192 = 2^{13}\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n2^{5x+3} = 2^{13}\n\\]\n\nSince the bases are the same, we equate the exponents:\n\n\\[\n5x + 3 = 13\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( x \\), we subtract 3 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n5x = 10\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 5:\n\n\\[\nx = 2\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution is \\( x = \\boxed{2} \\).'
'To evaluate the expression \\(\\frac{x^1 \\cdot x^2 \\cdot x^3 \\cdots x^9}{x^2 \\cdot x^4 \\cdot x^6 \\cdots x^{12}}\\), we first need to simplify it.\n\nThe numerator is the product of powers of \\(x\\) from \\(x^1\\) to \\(x^9\\):\n\\[ x^1 \\cdot x^2 \\cdot x^3 \\cdot \\ldots \\cdot x^9 = x^{1+2+3+\\ldots+9}. \\]\n\nThe sum of the exponents in the numerator is the sum of the first 9 positive integers:\n\\[ 1 + 2 + 3 + \\ldots + 9 = \\frac{9 \\cdot 10}{2} = 45. \\]\nSo, the numerator simplifies to \\(x^{45}\\).\n\nThe denominator is the product of powers of \\(x\\) from \\(x^2\\) to \\(x^{12}\\) with even exponents:\n\\[ x^2 \\cdot x^4 \\cdot x^6 \\cdot x^8 \\cdot x^{10} \\cdot x^{12} = x^{2+4+6+8+10+12}. \\]\n\nThe sum of the exponents in the denominator is:\n\\[ 2 + 4 + 6 + 8 + 10 + 12 = 42. \\]\nSo, the denominator simplifies to \\(x^{42}\\).\n\nNow, the entire expression becomes:\n\\[ \\frac{x^{45}}{x^{42}} = x^{45-42} = x^3. \\]\n\nGiven \\(x = 5\\), we substitute to find the value:\n\\[ x^3 = 5^3 = 125. \\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{125}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the coordinates of the point \\((x, y)\\) that satisfy the given conditions.\n\n1. **Distance from the x-axis**: The point is 6 units from the x-axis. Since both coordinates are negative, the y-coordinate must be \\(-6\\) (since the distance from the x-axis is the absolute value of the y-coordinate).\n\n   So, \\(y = -6\\).\n\n2. **Distance from the point \\((8, 3)\\)**: The point is 15 units from \\((8, 3)\\). We use the distance formula:\n\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(x - 8)^2 + (-6 - 3)^2} = 15\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying, we have:\n\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(x - 8)^2 + (-9)^2} = 15\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(x - 8)^2 + 81} = 15\n   \\]\n\n   Squaring both sides:\n\n   \\[\n   (x - 8)^2 + 81 = 225\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   (x - 8)^2 = 144\n   \\]\n\n   Taking the square root of both sides:\n\n   \\[\n   x - 8 = \\pm 12\n   \\]\n\n   Solving for \\(x\\), we have two cases:\n\n   - \\(x - 8 = 12 \\Rightarrow x = 20\\)\n   - \\(x - 8 = -12 \\Rightarrow x = -4\\)\n\n   Since both coordinates must be negative, we choose \\(x = -4\\).\n\n3. **Distance from the origin**: Now, we find the distance from the origin \\((0, 0)\\) to the point \\((-4, -6)\\):\n\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{(-4)^2 + (-6)^2} = \\sqrt{16 + 36} = \\sqrt{52}\n   \\]\n\n   Therefore, \\(n = 52\\).\n\nThus, the value of \\(n\\) is \\(\\boxed{52}\\).'
'To solve for \\( a + b \\), we start with the given equations:\n\n1. \\( a^2b^3 = \\frac{32}{27} \\)\n2. \\( \\frac{a}{b^3} = \\frac{27}{4} \\)\n\nFrom the second equation, we can express \\( a \\) in terms of \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{27}{4}b^3\n\\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( a \\) into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{27}{4}b^3\\right)^2 b^3 = \\frac{32}{27}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the left side:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{729}{16}b^6 \\cdot b^3 = \\frac{32}{27}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\frac{729}{16}b^9 = \\frac{32}{27}\n\\]\n\nTo solve for \\( b^9 \\), multiply both sides by \\(\\frac{16}{729}\\):\n\n\\[\nb^9 = \\frac{32}{27} \\cdot \\frac{16}{729}\n\\]\n\nCalculate the right side:\n\n\\[\nb^9 = \\frac{32 \\times 16}{27 \\times 729} = \\frac{512}{19683}\n\\]\n\nNow, take the ninth root of both sides to solve for \\( b \\):\n\n\\[\nb = \\left(\\frac{512}{19683}\\right)^{1/9}\n\\]\n\nRecognize that:\n\n\\[\n512 = 2^9 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad 19683 = 3^9\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\nb = \\left(\\frac{2^9}{3^9}\\right)^{1/9} = \\frac{2}{3}\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\( b = \\frac{2}{3} \\) back into the expression for \\( a \\):\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{27}{4} \\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right)^3\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( \\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right)^3 \\):\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right)^3 = \\frac{8}{27}\n\\]\n\nSubstitute back:\n\n\\[\na = \\frac{27}{4} \\times \\frac{8}{27} = \\frac{8}{4} = 2\n\\]\n\nFinally, calculate \\( a + b \\):\n\n\\[\na + b = 2 + \\frac{2}{3} = \\frac{6}{3} + \\frac{2}{3} = \\frac{8}{3}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( a + b \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{8}{3}}\\).'
'To find the perimeter of the square, we first need to determine the side length of the square. The side length is the distance between the two given adjacent vertices, \\((1, -2)\\) and \\((-4, 10)\\).\n\nThe distance \\(d\\) between two points \\((x_1, y_1)\\) and \\((x_2, y_2)\\) is given by the distance formula:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(x_2 - x_1)^2 + (y_2 - y_1)^2}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given points \\((1, -2)\\) and \\((-4, 10)\\) into the formula, we have:\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{((-4) - 1)^2 + (10 - (-2))^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{(-5)^2 + (12)^2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{25 + 144}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = \\sqrt{169}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nd = 13\n\\]\n\nThe side length of the square is 13. Since a square has four equal sides, the perimeter \\(P\\) of the square is:\n\n\\[\nP = 4 \\times \\text{side length} = 4 \\times 13 = 52\n\\]\n\nThus, the perimeter of the square is \\(\\boxed{52}\\).'
'To find \\( S^2 \\), we first need to determine the sum of the \\( x \\)-coordinates of the midpoints of the sides of the triangle.\n\nLet the vertices of the triangle be \\( A(x_1, y_1) \\), \\( B(x_2, y_2) \\), and \\( C(x_3, y_3) \\). The sum of the \\( x \\)-coordinates of the vertices is given by:\n\n\\[\nx_1 + x_2 + x_3 = \\sqrt{13}\n\\]\n\nThe midpoints of the sides of the triangle are:\n\n- Midpoint of \\( AB \\): \\(\\left(\\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2}, \\frac{y_1 + y_2}{2}\\right)\\)\n- Midpoint of \\( BC \\): \\(\\left(\\frac{x_2 + x_3}{2}, \\frac{y_2 + y_3}{2}\\right)\\)\n- Midpoint of \\( CA \\): \\(\\left(\\frac{x_3 + x_1}{2}, \\frac{y_3 + y_1}{2}\\right)\\)\n\nThe sum of the \\( x \\)-coordinates of these midpoints is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x_1 + x_2}{2} + \\frac{x_2 + x_3}{2} + \\frac{x_3 + x_1}{2}\n\\]\n\nSimplifying this expression, we have:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{x_1 + x_2 + x_2 + x_3 + x_3 + x_1}{2}\n= \\frac{2x_1 + 2x_2 + 2x_3}{2}\n= x_1 + x_2 + x_3\n\\]\n\nSince \\( x_1 + x_2 + x_3 = \\sqrt{13} \\), the sum of the \\( x \\)-coordinates of the midpoints is also \\( \\sqrt{13} \\).\n\nThus, \\( S = \\sqrt{13} \\).\n\nFinally, we find \\( S^2 \\):\n\n\\[\nS^2 = (\\sqrt{13})^2 = 13\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( S^2 \\) is \\(\\boxed{13}\\).'
'To find the value of \\( C \\), we start by setting up equations based on the information given:\n\n1. The arithmetic mean of \\( A \\), \\( B \\), and \\( C \\) is 10:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{A + B + C}{3} = 10\n   \\]\n   Multiplying both sides by 3 gives:\n   \\[\n   A + B + C = 30\n   \\]\n\n2. The value of \\( A \\) is six less than the value of \\( B \\):\n   \\[\n   A = B - 6\n   \\]\n\n3. The value of \\( C \\) is three more than the value of \\( B \\):\n   \\[\n   C = B + 3\n   \\]\n\nSubstitute the expressions for \\( A \\) and \\( C \\) in terms of \\( B \\) into the equation for the sum:\n\\[\n(B - 6) + B + (B + 3) = 30\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\\[\nB - 6 + B + B + 3 = 30\n\\]\n\\[\n3B - 3 = 30\n\\]\n\nAdd 3 to both sides:\n\\[\n3B = 33\n\\]\n\nDivide by 3:\n\\[\nB = 11\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( B = 11 \\) back into the expression for \\( C \\):\n\\[\nC = B + 3 = 11 + 3 = 14\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( C \\) is \\(\\boxed{14}\\).'
"To find the \\(x\\)-intercepts of the lines, we set \\(y = 0\\) in each equation and solve for \\(x\\).\n\nFor the line \\(y = \\frac{1}{3}x + 7\\):\n\n\\[\n0 = \\frac{1}{3}x + 7\n\\]\n\nSubtract 7 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n-\\frac{1}{3}x = -7\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by \\(-3\\) to solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx = 21\n\\]\n\nSo, the \\(x\\)-intercept of the first line is \\(x = 21\\).\n\nFor the line \\(y = 2x + 5\\):\n\n\\[\n0 = 2x + 5\n\\]\n\nSubtract 5 from both sides:\n\n\\[\n2x = -5\n\\]\n\nDivide both sides by 2 to solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\nx = -\\frac{5}{2} = -2.5\n\\]\n\nSo, the \\(x\\)-intercept of the second line is \\(x = -2.5\\).\n\nNow, we find the sum of the \\(x\\)-coordinates of the \\(x\\)-intercepts:\n\n\\[\n21 + (-2.5) = 21 - 2.5 = 18.5\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of the \\(x\\)-coordinates of the two lines' \\(x\\)-intercepts is \\(\\boxed{18.5}\\)."
'To determine how many sticks of butter are needed, we first need to calculate how many pans of cookies Walter and Gretel need to bake to supply 216 cookies.\n\nEach pan makes 15 cookies. Therefore, the number of pans required is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{216}{15} = 14.4\n\\]\n\nSince they can only make full recipes, they need to make 15 pans of cookies (rounding up from 14.4).\n\nNext, we calculate the total amount of butter needed for 15 pans. The recipe requires 3 tablespoons of butter per pan. Therefore, for 15 pans, they need:\n\n\\[\n15 \\times 3 = 45 \\text{ tablespoons of butter}\n\\]\n\nThere are 8 tablespoons in a stick of butter, so the number of sticks needed is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{45}{8} = 5.625\n\\]\n\nSince they can only use whole sticks of butter, they will need 6 sticks of butter.\n\nThus, Walter and Gretel will need \\(\\boxed{6}\\) sticks of butter.'
'To find the positive difference between \\(120\\%\\) of 30 and \\(130\\%\\) of 20, we first calculate each percentage:\n\n1. Calculate \\(120\\%\\) of 30:\n   \\[\n   120\\% \\text{ of } 30 = \\frac{120}{100} \\times 30 = 1.2 \\times 30 = 36\n   \\]\n\n2. Calculate \\(130\\%\\) of 20:\n   \\[\n   130\\% \\text{ of } 20 = \\frac{130}{100} \\times 20 = 1.3 \\times 20 = 26\n   \\]\n\nNow, find the positive difference between these two results:\n\\[\n|36 - 26| = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the positive difference is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
'To solve the expression \\(3 \\ast (6 \\ast 8)\\), we need to evaluate it step by step using the operation defined by \\(P \\ast Q = \\frac{P+Q}{2}\\).\n\nFirst, evaluate the inner expression \\(6 \\ast 8\\):\n\\[\n6 \\ast 8 = \\frac{6 + 8}{2} = \\frac{14}{2} = 7\n\\]\n\nNext, use the result from the inner expression to evaluate \\(3 \\ast 7\\):\n\\[\n3 \\ast 7 = \\frac{3 + 7}{2} = \\frac{10}{2} = 5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(3 \\ast (6 \\ast 8)\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
'To solve this problem, we need to find the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) of the function \\( f(x) = ax + b \\) and then use the given relationship \\( g(x) = 2f^{-1}(x) \\).\n\n1. **Find the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\):**\n\n   The function \\( f(x) = ax + b \\) is a linear function. To find its inverse, we follow these steps:\n   \n   - Start with \\( y = ax + b \\).\n   - Solve for \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\):\n     \\[\n     y = ax + b \\implies ax = y - b \\implies x = \\frac{y - b}{a}\n     \\]\n   - Therefore, the inverse function is:\n     \\[\n     f^{-1}(x) = \\frac{x - b}{a}\n     \\]\n\n2. **Use the relationship \\( g(x) = 2f^{-1}(x) \\):**\n\n   We are given that \\( g(x) = 3x + 2 \\) and \\( g(x) = 2f^{-1}(x) \\). Substitute the expression for \\( f^{-1}(x) \\):\n   \\[\n   3x + 2 = 2 \\left( \\frac{x - b}{a} \\right)\n   \\]\n   Simplify the right side:\n   \\[\n   3x + 2 = \\frac{2(x - b)}{a}\n   \\]\n   Multiply both sides by \\( a \\) to eliminate the fraction:\n   \\[\n   a(3x + 2) = 2(x - b)\n   \\]\n   Distribute both sides:\n   \\[\n   3ax + 2a = 2x - 2b\n   \\]\n   Rearrange the equation to group terms involving \\( x \\) and constant terms:\n   \\[\n   3ax - 2x = -2a - 2b\n   \\]\n   Factor out \\( x \\) on the left side:\n   \\[\n   x(3a - 2) = -2a - 2b\n   \\]\n   For the equation to hold for all \\( x \\), the coefficients of \\( x \\) must be equal, and the constant terms must be equal. Therefore, we have:\n   \\[\n   3a - 2 = 0 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad -2a - 2b = 0\n   \\]\n\n3. **Solve the system of equations:**\n\n   From the first equation:\n   \\[\n   3a - 2 = 0 \\implies 3a = 2 \\implies a = \\frac{2}{3}\n   \\]\n\n   Substitute \\( a = \\frac{2}{3} \\) into the second equation:\n   \\[\n   -2\\left(\\frac{2}{3}\\right) - 2b = 0 \\implies -\\frac{4}{3} - 2b = 0\n   \\]\n   Solve for \\( b \\):\n   \\[\n   -2b = \\frac{4}{3} \\implies b = -\\frac{2}{3}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Calculate \\(\\frac{a+b}{2}\\):**\n\n   \\[\n   a = \\frac{2}{3}, \\quad b = -\\frac{2}{3}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   a + b = \\frac{2}{3} - \\frac{2}{3} = 0\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\frac{a+b}{2} = \\frac{0}{2} = 0\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{a+b}{2}\\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
"To find the sum of \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\), we start with the given equations:\n\n1. \\(a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 13\\)\n2. \\(ab + bc + ca = 6\\)\n\nWe want to find \\(a + b + c\\). Let's denote \\(s = a + b + c\\). We know the identity:\n\n\\[\n(a + b + c)^2 = a^2 + b^2 + c^2 + 2(ab + bc + ca)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values into this identity, we have:\n\n\\[\ns^2 = 13 + 2 \\times 6\n\\]\n\n\\[\ns^2 = 13 + 12 = 25\n\\]\n\nTaking the square root of both sides, we find:\n\n\\[\ns = \\sqrt{25} = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of \\(a\\), \\(b\\), and \\(c\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\)."
'Let the two numbers be \\( x \\) and \\( y \\). We are given the following equations:\n\n\\[\nx + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx - y = 9\n\\]\n\nTo find the values of \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), we can solve these equations simultaneously. First, add the two equations:\n\n\\[\n(x + y) + (x - y) = 25 + 9\n\\]\n\n\\[\n2x = 34\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 17\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute \\( x = 17 \\) back into the first equation:\n\n\\[\n17 + y = 25\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 25 - 17\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny = 8\n\\]\n\nNow that we have \\( x = 17 \\) and \\( y = 8 \\), we can find their product:\n\n\\[\nx \\cdot y = 17 \\cdot 8 = 136\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the two numbers is \\(\\boxed{136}\\).'
'To determine the domain of the function \\( q(x) = \\frac{\\sqrt{x}}{\\sqrt{1-x^2}} \\), we need to consider the restrictions imposed by the square roots and the denominator.\n\n1. **Square Root in the Numerator:**\n   - The expression \\(\\sqrt{x}\\) is defined for \\(x \\geq 0\\).\n\n2. **Square Root in the Denominator:**\n   - The expression \\(\\sqrt{1-x^2}\\) is defined for \\(1-x^2 \\geq 0\\), which simplifies to \\(-1 \\leq x \\leq 1\\).\n   - Additionally, since it is in the denominator, we require \\(1-x^2 > 0\\) to avoid division by zero. This simplifies to \\(-1 < x < 1\\).\n\nCombining these conditions:\n- From \\(\\sqrt{x}\\), we have \\(x \\geq 0\\).\n- From \\(\\sqrt{1-x^2}\\) being in the denominator, we have \\(-1 < x < 1\\).\n\nThe intersection of these conditions is \\(0 \\leq x < 1\\).\n\nTherefore, the domain of the function \\( q(x) \\) is \\([0, 1)\\).'
'To solve for \\(\\frac{2x+y}{3x-2y}\\) given that \\(4x = 3y\\), we first express \\(y\\) in terms of \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n4x = 3y \\implies y = \\frac{4}{3}x\n\\]\n\nNow substitute \\(y = \\frac{4}{3}x\\) into the expression \\(\\frac{2x+y}{3x-2y}\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x + y}{3x - 2y} = \\frac{2x + \\frac{4}{3}x}{3x - 2\\left(\\frac{4}{3}x\\right)}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the numerator:\n\n\\[\n2x + \\frac{4}{3}x = \\frac{6}{3}x + \\frac{4}{3}x = \\frac{10}{3}x\n\\]\n\nSimplify the denominator:\n\n\\[\n3x - 2\\left(\\frac{4}{3}x\\right) = 3x - \\frac{8}{3}x = \\frac{9}{3}x - \\frac{8}{3}x = \\frac{1}{3}x\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these back into the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\frac{10}{3}x}{\\frac{1}{3}x} = \\frac{10}{3} \\div \\frac{1}{3} = 10\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\frac{2x+y}{3x-2y}\\) is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'

"To determine the radius of the cookie, we need to rewrite the given equation in the standard form of a circle's equation, which is \\((x - h)^2 + (y - k)^2 = r^2\\), where \\((h, k)\\) is the center and \\(r\\) is the radius.\n\nThe given equation is:\n\\[ x^2 + y^2 - 6 = 6x + 2y. \\]\n\nFirst, let's rearrange the terms:\n\\[ x^2 - 6x + y^2 - 2y = 6. \\]\n\nNext, we complete the square for the \\(x\\) terms and the \\(y\\) terms.\n\nFor the \\(x\\) terms:\n\\[ x^2 - 6x \\]\nTo complete the square, take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), which is \\(-6\\), divide by 2 to get \\(-3\\), and then square it to get \\(9\\). Add and subtract \\(9\\):\n\\[ x^2 - 6x + 9 - 9. \\]\n\nFor the \\(y\\) terms:\n\\[ y^2 - 2y \\]\nTake half of the coefficient of \\(y\\), which is \\(-2\\), divide by 2 to get \\(-1\\), and then square it to get \\(1\\). Add and subtract \\(1\\):\n\\[ y^2 - 2y + 1 - 1. \\]\n\nNow, substitute these completed squares back into the equation:\n\\[ (x^2 - 6x + 9) + (y^2 - 2y + 1) = 6 + 9 + 1. \\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[ (x - 3)^2 + (y - 1)^2 = 16. \\]\n\nThe equation \\((x - 3)^2 + (y - 1)^2 = 16\\) is in the standard form of a circle's equation, where the center is \\((3, 1)\\) and the radius \\(r\\) is \\(\\sqrt{16} = 4\\).\n\nTherefore, the radius of the cookie is \\(\\boxed{4}\\)."

We are given the following relationships:\n\n1. \\( \\frac{r}{2} = y - 2 \\)\n2. \\( \\frac{r}{2} = \\frac{o}{3} \\)\n3. \\( \\frac{r}{2} = \\frac{w + 3}{3} \\)\n\nAdditionally, we know the total number of marbles is 35:\n\n\\[ r + y + o + w = 35 \\]\n\nLet's solve these equations step by step.\n\nFrom equation 1, we have:\n\n\\[ y = \\frac{r}{2} + 2 \\]\n\nFrom equation 2, we have:\n\n\\[ o = \\frac{3r}{2} \\]\n\nFrom equation 3, we have:\n\n\\[ w + 3 = \\frac{3r}{2} \\]\n\\[ w = \\frac{3r}{2} - 3 \\]\n\nSubstitute these expressions for \\( y \\), \\( o \\), and \\( w \\) into the total equation:\n\n\\[ r + \\left(\\frac{r}{2} + 2\\right) + \\frac{3r}{2} + \\left(\\frac{3r}{2} - 3\\right) = 35 \\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n\n\\[ r + \\frac{r}{2} + 2 + \\frac{3r}{2} + \\frac{3r}{2} - 3 = 35 \\]\n\n\\[ r + \\frac{r}{2} + \\frac{3r}{2} + \\frac{3r}{2} - 1 = 35 \\]\n\nCombine the terms involving \\( r \\):\n\n\\[ r + \\frac{r}{2} + \\frac{3r}{2} + \\frac{3r}{2} = 36 \\]\n\n\\[ r + \\frac{7r}{2} = 36 \\]\n\nConvert \\( r \\) to a fraction with a common denominator:\n\n\\[ \\frac{2r}{2} + \\frac{7r}{2} = 36 \\]\n\n\\[ \\frac{9r}{2} = 36 \\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 2 to clear the fraction:\n\n\\[ 9r = 72 \\]\n\nDivide by 9:\n\n\\[ r = 8 \\]\n\nThus, the number of red marbles is \\(\\boxed{8}\\)."
'The roots of the quadratic equation \\(4x^2 + 7x + k = 0\\) are given as \\(\\frac{-7 \\pm i\\sqrt{15}}{8}\\). These roots are in the form \\(\\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\\), where \\(a = 4\\), \\(b = 7\\), and \\(c = k\\).\n\nThe given roots are complex, indicating that the discriminant \\(b^2 - 4ac\\) is negative. The imaginary part of the roots is \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{15}}{8}\\), which corresponds to \\(\\frac{\\sqrt{-(b^2 - 4ac)}}{2a}\\).\n\nFrom the given roots, we have:\n\\[\n\\frac{\\sqrt{15}}{8} = \\frac{\\sqrt{-(b^2 - 4ac)}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nSince \\(a = 4\\), we have \\(2a = 8\\). Therefore:\n\\[\n\\sqrt{15} = \\sqrt{-(b^2 - 4ac)}\n\\]\n\nSquaring both sides, we get:\n\\[\n15 = -(b^2 - 4ac)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(b = 7\\) and \\(a = 4\\), we have:\n\\[\n15 = -(7^2 - 4 \\cdot 4 \\cdot k)\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we get:\n\\[\n15 = -(49 - 16k)\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\\[\n15 = -49 + 16k\n\\]\n\nAdding 49 to both sides:\n\\[\n64 = 16k\n\\]\n\nDividing by 16:\n\\[\nk = 4\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(k\\) is \\(\\boxed{4}\\).'

'To find a value for \\( x \\) such that \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x+1) \\), we first need to determine the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\).\n\nGiven \\( f(x) = 5x - 12 \\), we set \\( y = 5x - 12 \\) and solve for \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\):\n\n\\[\ny = 5x - 12\n\\]\n\n\\[\ny + 12 = 5x\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{y + 12}{5}\n\\]\n\nThus, the inverse function is \\( f^{-1}(x) = \\frac{x + 12}{5} \\).\n\nNow, we set \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x+1) \\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x + 12}{5} = f(x+1)\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( f(x+1) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(x+1) = 5(x+1) - 12 = 5x + 5 - 12 = 5x - 7\n\\]\n\nEquating the two expressions:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x + 12}{5} = 5x - 7\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by 5 to eliminate the fraction:\n\n\\[\nx + 12 = 25x - 35\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation:\n\n\\[\n12 + 35 = 25x - x\n\\]\n\n\\[\n47 = 24x\n\\]\n\nSolve for \\( x \\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{47}{24}\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x \\) that satisfies the equation is \\( \\boxed{\\frac{47}{24}} \\).'

Note that \\(0.125\\) is equivalent to \\(\\frac{1}{8}\\), and \\(2^{12} = 4096\\):\n\\[\n0.125 \\times 2^{12} = \\frac{1}{8} \\times 4096 = \\frac{4096}{8} = 512\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these results back into the original expression:\n\\[\n\\frac{512}{512} = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the simplified expression is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'

'To find the number of teams \\( n \\) in a round-robin tournament where 55 games are played, we use the formula for the number of games:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{n^2 - n}{2} = 55\n\\]\n\nFirst, multiply both sides by 2 to eliminate the fraction:\n\n\\[\nn^2 - n = 110\n\\]\n\nRearrange the equation to form a standard quadratic equation:\n\n\\[\nn^2 - n - 110 = 0\n\\]\n\nWe can solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -1 \\), and \\( c = -110 \\). Plug these values into the formula:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{-(-1) \\pm \\sqrt{(-1)^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-110)}}{2 \\cdot 1}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 \\pm \\sqrt{1 + 440}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 \\pm \\sqrt{441}}{2}\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 \\pm 21}{2}\n\\]\n\nThis gives us two potential solutions:\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 + 21}{2} = \\frac{22}{2} = 11\n\\]\n\n\\[\nn = \\frac{1 - 21}{2} = \\frac{-20}{2} = -10\n\\]\n\nSince the number of teams cannot be negative, the number of teams is \\( n = 11 \\).\n\nThus, there are \\(\\boxed{11}\\) teams in the tournament.'
"To solve the equation \\(\\lceil x \\rceil + \\lfloor x \\rfloor + x = 4.8\\), we need to understand the properties of the ceiling and floor functions. \n\nThe floor function \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor\\) gives the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(x\\), and the ceiling function \\(\\lceil x \\rceil\\) gives the smallest integer greater than or equal to \\(x\\). \n\nLet's denote \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor = n\\), where \\(n\\) is an integer. Then, we have:\n\\[ n \\leq x < n+1. \\]\n\nThe ceiling of \\(x\\) can be expressed as:\n\\[ \\lceil x \\rceil = n \\text{ or } n+1. \\]\n\nNow, let's consider the equation:\n\\[ \\lceil x \\rceil + \\lfloor x \\rfloor + x = 4.8. \\]\n\nSubstituting \\(\\lfloor x \\rfloor = n\\) into the equation, we have:\n\\[ \\lceil x \\rceil + n + x = 4.8. \\]\n\nSince \\(n \\leq x < n+1\\), we can express \\(x\\) as:\n\\[ x = n + f, \\]\nwhere \\(0 \\leq f < 1\\).\n\nSubstituting \\(x = n + f\\) into the equation, we get:\n\\[ \\lceil n + f \\rceil + n + (n + f) = 4.8. \\]\n\nThe ceiling function \\(\\lceil n + f \\rceil\\) will be:\n- \\(n\\) if \\(f = 0\\),\n- \\(n+1\\) if \\(0 < f < 1\\).\n\nSince \\(f\\) is not zero (otherwise the equation would not sum to a non-integer), we have:\n\\[ \\lceil n + f \\rceil = n + 1. \\]\n\nSubstituting this back, we get:\n\\[ (n + 1) + n + (n + f) = 4.8. \\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\\[ 3n + 1 + f = 4.8. \\]\n\nSolving for \\(f\\), we get:\n\\[ 3n + f = 3.8. \\]\n\nThus:\n\\[ f = 3.8 - 3n. \\]\n\nSince \\(0 \\leq f < 1\\), we have:\n\\[ 0 \\leq 3.8 - 3n < 1. \\]\n\nSolving the inequalities:\n1. \\(3.8 - 3n \\geq 0\\) gives \\(3.8 \\geq 3n\\) or \\(n \\leq \\frac{3.8}{3} = 1.2667\\).\n2. \\(3.8 - 3n < 1\\) gives \\(3.8 < 3n + 1\\) or \\(2.8 < 3n\\) or \\(n > \\frac{2.8}{3} = 0.9333\\).\n\nSince \\(n\\) is an integer, the only possible value for \\(n\\) is 1.\n\nSubstituting \\(n = 1\\) back, we find:\n\\[ f = 3.8 - 3 \\times 1 = 0.8. \\]\n\nThus, \\(x = n + f = 1 + 0.8 = 1.8\\).\n\nTherefore, the solution is \\(x = \\boxed{1.8}\\)."
'To simplify the expression \\(49x^2 + 14x(19-7x) + (19-7x)^2\\), we can expand and combine like terms.\n\nFirst, expand the middle term:\n\\[\n14x(19-7x) = 14x \\cdot 19 - 14x \\cdot 7x = 266x - 98x^2\n\\]\n\nNext, expand the last term:\n\\[\n(19-7x)^2 = (19)^2 - 2 \\cdot 19 \\cdot 7x + (7x)^2 = 361 - 266x + 49x^2\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute these expansions back into the original expression:\n\\[\n49x^2 + (266x - 98x^2) + (361 - 266x + 49x^2)\n\\]\n\nCombine like terms:\n- The \\(x^2\\) terms: \\(49x^2 - 98x^2 + 49x^2 = 0\\)\n- The \\(x\\) terms: \\(266x - 266x = 0\\)\n- The constant term: \\(361\\)\n\nThus, the expression simplifies to:\n\\[\n\\boxed{361}\n\\]'

"To find the value of \\( f(3) \\), we first need to understand the relationship between \\( f(-3) \\) and \\( f(3) \\). Given the function \\( f(x) = ax^4 - bx^2 + x + 5 \\), we can observe that:\n\n- The terms \\( ax^4 \\) and \\( -bx^2 \\) are even functions, meaning they are symmetric with respect to the y-axis. Therefore, \\( ax^4 \\) and \\( -bx^2 \\) will have the same value for \\( x = 3 \\) and \\( x = -3 \\).\n- The term \\( x \\) is an odd function, meaning it is antisymmetric with respect to the y-axis. Therefore, the value of \\( x \\) will change sign when \\( x \\) is replaced by \\(-x\\).\n\nGiven \\( f(-3) = 2 \\), we can write:\n\n\\[\nf(-3) = a(-3)^4 - b(-3)^2 - 3 + 5 = 2\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\n81a - 9b - 3 + 5 = 2\n\\]\n\n\\[\n81a - 9b + 2 = 2\n\\]\n\n\\[\n81a - 9b = 0\n\\]\n\nNow, let's find \\( f(3) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(3) = a(3)^4 - b(3)^2 + 3 + 5\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[\nf(3) = 81a - 9b + 3 + 5\n\\]\n\nSince we know from the equation \\( 81a - 9b = 0 \\), we substitute:\n\n\\[\nf(3) = 0 + 3 + 5 = 8\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(3) \\) is \\(\\boxed{8}\\)."
'To solve for \\( f(f(f(f(f(4))))) \\), we need to evaluate the function \\( f \\) multiple times, starting with \\( n = 4 \\).\n\n1. **Evaluate \\( f(4) \\):**\n   Since 4 is even, we use the second case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(4) = 4^2 - 4 \\times 4 - 1 = 16 - 16 - 1 = -1\n   \\]\n\n2. **Evaluate \\( f(-1) \\):**\n   Since -1 is odd, we use the first case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(-1) = (-1)^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\n3. **Evaluate \\( f(1) \\):**\n   Since 1 is odd, we use the first case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(1) = 1^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\n4. **Evaluate \\( f(1) \\) again:**\n   Since 1 is odd, we use the first case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(1) = 1^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\n5. **Evaluate \\( f(1) \\) one more time:**\n   Since 1 is odd, we use the first case of the function:\n   \\[\n   f(1) = 1^2 = 1\n   \\]\n\nThus, \\( f(f(f(f(f(4))))) = 1 \\).\n\nThe final answer is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'

"To solve the problem, we need to find the positive integer values of \\( x \\) for which the expression \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 \\) is between 10 and 50. This can be expressed as:\n\n\\[ 10 < x^2 + 4x + 4 < 50. \\]\n\nFirst, let's solve the inequality \\( x^2 + 4x + 4 > 10 \\):\n\n\\[ x^2 + 4x + 4 > 10 \\]\n\\[ x^2 + 4x + 4 - 10 > 0 \\]\n\\[ x^2 + 4x - 6 > 0. \\]\n\nTo find the critical points, we solve the equation \\( x^2 + 4x - 6 = 0 \\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}, \\]\n\nwhere \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 4 \\), and \\( c = -6 \\).\n\n\\[ x = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{4^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 \\cdot (-6)}}{2 \\cdot 1} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 + 24}}{2} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-4 \\pm \\sqrt{40}}{2} \\]\n\\[ x = \\frac{-4 \\pm 2\\sqrt{10}}{2} \\]\n\\[ x = -2 \\pm \\sqrt{10}. \\]\n\nThe roots are \\( x = -2 + \\sqrt{10} \\) and \\( x = -2 - \\sqrt{10} \\).\n\nSince \\(\\sqrt{10} \\approx 3.16\\), we have:\n\n\\[ x \\approx -2 + 3.16 = 1.16 \\]\n\\[ x \\approx -2 - 3.16 = -5.16. \\]\n\nThus, the inequality \\( x^2 + 4x - 6 > 0 \\) holds for \\( x < -2 - \\sqrt{10} \\) or \\( x > -2 + \\sqrt{10} \\). "Let's denote the value of a triangle as \\( T \\) and the value of a circle as \\( C \\).\n\nFrom the first equation:\n\\[\n3C + 5T = 21\n\\]\n\nFrom the second equation:\n\\[\n5C + 3T = 16\n\\]\n\nWe have the system of equations:\n1. \\( 3C + 5T = 21 \\)\n2. \\( 5C + 3T = 16 \\)\n\nTo solve this system, we can use the method of elimination. "To find the smallest possible value of the given expression, we can use symmetry and substitution.
